    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/PointRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/PointRenderer.tsx) (~30 LOC delta). Two surgical changes:
      - **Named-import block.** New import block right after the existing `crossFilter` block: `import { dispatchDrillThrough, isModifierClick } from "@/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough";`. Same locality precedent as the WD3-wiring-bar / WD3-wiring-rest-cat / WD3-wiring-rest-trend renderers — drill imports sit immediately next to cross-filter imports so future Claude reads them as a pair.
      - **Handler widening + modifier branch.** The existing `onPointClick` arrow widens its signature from parameterless `() => {...}` to `(e: React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>) => {...}` and gains a top-of-handler branch:
        ```ts
        const onPointClick = crossFilterReady
          ? (e: React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>) => {
              if (isModifierClick(e)) {
                dispatchDrillThrough({
                  chartId: dashboardTile!.tileId,
                  column: colorCh!.field,
                  value: p.rawColor,
                  sourceTileId: dashboardTile!.tileId,
                  filters: dashboardFilters,
                });
                return;
              }
              dispatchCrossFilter({
                column: colorCh!.field,
                value: toFilterValue(p.rawColor),
                sourceTileId: dashboardTile!.tileId,
              });
            }
          : undefined;
        ```
        Single-event-handler shape — same as the WD3-wiring-rest-cat family, because PointRenderer's onClick already lives at the per-mark level (per-point dispatch was the WD2 design). The `crossFilterReady ? ... : undefined` conditional shape is preserved (the WD2 gate). The `return;` after the drill dispatch is single-intent-load-bearing — without it a cmd-click would dispatch BOTH events.
      - **5-field payload** mirrors prior WD3 waves: `chartId` = `dashboardTile!.tileId`; `column` = `colorCh!.field` (the per-mark filter target — PointRenderer is unique in keying on `colorCh` not `xCh` because its filter target is the color group, not the quantitative x axis); `value` = `p.rawColor` RAW (NOT `toFilterValue`-coerced — server-side canonicaliser picks the right Date / number / categorical comparison per the inferred column type); `sourceTileId` = `dashboardTile!.tileId`; `filters` = `dashboardFilters` snapshot (reused from the WD2-dim concern's already-lifted reference, so no extra state).
      - **Both render paths** (`<Circle>` for default, `<path>` for glyph-shape encoding) bind the same widened `onClick={onPointClick}` — additive change preserves both branches uniformly. The WD2-dim per-point factor (`isDashboardDimmed` / `dimMul`) composes unchanged.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringRestPoint.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringRestPoint.test.ts) (new, ~190 LOC). 16 source-inspection tests across 7 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Suite split:
      - **Imports** (2): drillThrough named imports + WD2 crossFilter imports preserved.
      - **Handler widening** (2): handler now accepts `React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>`; conditional `crossFilterReady ? ... : undefined` shape preserved.
      - **Inline modifier branch** (5): branch fires BEFORE `dispatchCrossFilter`; 5-field payload shape; raw-value negative pin (no `toFilterValue` in drill block); `return;` after dispatch (single-intent); WD2 cross-filter regression with `toFilterValue(p.rawColor)`.
      - **cursorStyle gate** (1): cursor:pointer still gated on `crossFilterReady` — drill-through doesn't widen the cursor domain (a cmd-down cursor change is a separate polish wave per dormancy-debt).
      - **WD2-dim + WD2-wiring contracts preserved** (2): per-point dim factor still applied; both `<Circle>` and glyph `<path>` paths bind `onClick={onPointClick}`.
      - **Cross-cutting contracts** (4): WD3-wiring-rest-point marker; drill column matches WD2 cross-filter dispatch column (`colorCh!.field`); WD2-dim concern keys on the SAME `colorCh!.field` (drill + dispatch + dim symmetry); drill dispatch count = 1 (per-renderer single-shot enforcement).

  **Why this design.** The conditional handler shape — `crossFilterReady ? (e) => ... : undefined` — was chosen over an unconditional always-defined handler with internal gating. Three considered shapes:
  1. **Always-defined handler with `if (!crossFilterReady) return;` at the top.** Rejected because the `undefined` onClick prop is load-bearing: when there's no `colorCh`, the affordance (cursor:pointer) should also be off. Tying the gate to a single ternary keeps both affordances aligned and removes a runtime check on every mouse click.
  2. **Two separate handlers — one for drill, one for cross-filter — both gated on `crossFilterReady`.** Rejected as duplication: the modifier check is a single source of truth and the two dispatches share a closure over the same `p`, `dashboardTile`, `colorCh`, `dashboardFilters`. Splitting would require either calling both handlers in React's event chain (impossible — onClick is single-fire) or a wrapper component.
  3. **Conditional `crossFilterReady ? ... : undefined` arrow with internal modifier branch** (chosen). Minimal-diff, single load-bearing branch, both renderer paths bind the same handler — three-way symmetry across the renderer body, the dispatch contract, and the WD2-dim concern.

  PointRenderer's column choice (`colorCh!.field`, not `xCh!.field`) diverges from the trend / bar / cat renderers and is intentional. Bar / Arc / Funnel / Box / Waterfall / Combo / Line / Area all dispatch on `xCh.field` because their per-mark filter target IS the x-axis category (or, for trend, the x-axis value the nearest-x lookup resolves to). PointRenderer's per-mark filter target is the COLOR group — clicking a "North" point should filter the dashboard to Region=North. The cross-filter dispatch already followed this convention (the WD2-wiring-rest-point wave); WD3 inherits it for symmetry.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD3-wiring-rest-point (16 new in `wd3WiringRestPoint.test.ts`) all pass. 159 cumulative WD3 + adjacent WD2-trend / WD2-point tests green (foundation 11 + wiring-bar 12 + wiring-rest-cat 44 + sheet 21 + wiring-rest-trend 18 + wiring-rest-point 16 + wd2DimPoint + wd2WiringRestPoint), zero regression. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline). Client `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 53 errors (identical baseline).

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Heatmap drill (WD3-wiring-rest-rect).** Two-column drill payload design decision still deferred. RectRenderer cells sit at the intersection of `rowCh × colCh`; the current single-`column: string` event field doesn't accommodate. Either widen the foundation's `DrillThroughEvent.column` type to `string | { row: string; col: string }` (cleaner type, more changes in foundation + every existing consumer) OR fire two drill events with the receiver de-duping by event-time-proximity (simpler foundation, more complex receiver). WD3-sheet's render contract has to know which shape it consumes — the decision affects both files.
    - **ECharts drill (WD3-wiring-echarts).** 5 ECharts marks via the existing `onChartClick(params)` flow. `params.event.event` carries `metaKey` / `ctrlKey` so `isModifierClick(params.event.event)` works with no foundation changes. The substantive work is the per-renderer `dataIndex → (column, rawValue)` mapping.
    - **Server-side row fetch (WD3-server).** The sheet's placeholder body explicitly notes WD3-server is the future row source. Endpoint `/api/dashboards/:id/drill?chartId=&column=&value=` mirrors the existing XLSX export endpoint's chart-row lookup path.
    - **Hover-time cursor change (cursor: "zoom-in" on cmd-hover).** Carried over from prior WD3 waves. Needs a keydown/keyup window listener and applies to every renderer uniformly — separate polish wave with its own contract.
    - **Pure-quantitative scatter drill (no colorCh).** Pinned in the wave's test suite: when `crossFilterReady` is false (no colorCh), onPointClick is `undefined` — no cursor:pointer, no dispatch. A drill on a continuous x or y axis would need a different shape (range-select via brush, like LineRenderer's hypothetical cmd-zoom) and a different receiver — orthogonal to this wave.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD3-wiring-rest-trend · LineRenderer + AreaRenderer cmd / ctrl-click → drill-through.** Extends the WD3 family to the two trend renderers. Trend renderers have continuous-x marks (lines / stacked areas) and dispatch via NEAREST-X lookup rather than per-mark click — a click anywhere on the chart surface maps to the nearest data point on the inner-plot's x-axis via `localPoint(e).x` + an `xPx` binary search. The WD2-wiring family established this lookup; WD3 layers the modifier-key intent on top so cmd / ctrl-click routes the SAME `nearest.x` value to drill-through instead of cross-filter. Wave brings WD3 to 8 of 15 chart kinds wired (bar + cat-5 + line + area).

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/AreaRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/AreaRenderer.tsx) (~20 LOC delta). Same single-event-handler shape as the WD3-wiring-rest-cat family: the existing top-level `onClick={(e: React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>) => {...}}` already receives the MouseEvent, so the WD3 wiring is an inline branch inside the `if (nearest)` block — right before the existing `dispatchCrossFilter` call:
      ```ts
      if (nearest) {
        if (isModifierClick(e)) {
          dispatchDrillThrough({
            chartId: dashboardTile.tileId,
            column: xCh.field,
            value: nearest.x,
            sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId,
            filters: dashboardFilters,
          });
          return;
        }
        dispatchCrossFilter({
          column: xCh.field,
          value: toFilterValue(nearest.x),
          sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId,
        });
      }
      ```
      5-field payload mirrors WD3-wiring-bar shape: `chartId` = `dashboardTile.tileId`; `column` = `xCh.field`; `value` = `nearest.x` RAW (NOT `toFilterValue(nearest.x)` — the server's canonicaliser picks the right Date / number / categorical comparison based on the column's inferred type); `sourceTileId` = the tile id; `filters` = the already-lifted `dashboardFilters` snapshot.

    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx) (~45 LOC delta). Different shape because `dispatchCrossFilter` fires inside the PARAMETERLESS `onBrushUp` handler — the brush-zoom plumbing piggybacks the click semantic (a tiny `< 6 px` brush is treated as a click, with the recorded brush position driving the nearest-x lookup). `onBrushUp` has no access to the original MouseEvent. The design choice: stash the modifier flag in a `brushModifierRef = useRef<boolean>(false)` at `onBrushDown` time, consume it in `onBrushUp`. **`useRef` (not `useState`)** because the flag doesn't drive a re-render — only the brush rectangle `<rect>` does. A `useState` would force a re-render on every cmd-down without any visual change. Three call-sites:
      - **`onBrushDown`** assigns `brushModifierRef.current = isModifierClick(e);` right after the existing `setBrushStart(x)` / `setBrushEnd(x)` calls. The brushDown handler already accepts `(e: React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>)` — no signature change.
      - **`onBrushUp`** (tiny-drag click path, inside the existing `if (Math.abs(hi - lo) < 6)` branch + `if (dashboardTile)` gate + `if (nearest)` body): branches `if (brushModifierRef.current) { dispatchDrillThrough(...) } else { dispatchCrossFilter(...) }` — drill XOR cross-filter, never both. The drill branch is FIRST in the if/else (cmd → drill; default → filter).
      - **Reset** to `false` happens UNCONDITIONALLY before the `setBrushStart(null)` / `setBrushEnd(null)` calls, so a brush-zoom mouseup with cmd held (the path where `Math.abs(hi - lo) >= 6`) doesn't leave the flag dirty for the next click. Pinned in the test suite.

    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringRestTrend.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringRestTrend.test.ts) (new, ~230 LOC). 18 source-inspection tests across 7 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Suite split:
      - **AreaRenderer imports** (2): drillThrough named imports + WD2 untouched.
      - **AreaRenderer onClick inline branch** (4): branch inside `if (nearest)` block before `dispatchCrossFilter`; 5-field payload shape; raw-value negative pin; WD2 cross-filter regression.
      - **LineRenderer imports** (2): drillThrough named imports + WD2 untouched.
      - **LineRenderer brushModifierRef declaration** (1): `useRef<boolean>(false)` (NOT useState).
      - **LineRenderer capture on brushDown** (1): `brushModifierRef.current = isModifierClick(e);` inside the brushDown body.
      - **LineRenderer consume on brushUp** (5): if/else branch order (drill FIRST, then cross-filter); 5-field payload; raw-value negative pin; reset-before-state-clear pin (the reset must fire on EVERY brushUp exit, not just the dispatch path); WD2 else-branch regression with `toFilterValue(nearest.x)`.
      - **Cross-cutting contracts** (3): `WD3-wiring-rest-trend` marker per renderer; column-symmetry (drill + cross-filter both on `xCh.field`); drill-count = 1 per renderer (single-shot enforcement — pin against a future refactor that adds a second drill surface like a legend cmd-click).

  **Why this design.** Three alternative shapes were considered for LineRenderer's modifier capture. (1) **Store the full MouseEvent in the ref.** Rejected as a memory / lifecycle concern — React MouseEvents are pooled in synthetic-event implementations (less of a concern in React 17+ but still a leaky abstraction). Capture just the boolean flag, not the event. (2) **Restructure `onBrushUp` to receive the MouseEvent** (refactor brush-zoom internals so the click-fallthrough path knows its origin event). Rejected because the existing onBrushUp is called from both `onMouseUp` and `onMouseLeave` handlers — two different event surfaces; threading the event through both would complicate the brush-zoom contract for marginal benefit. The ref capture is a precise patch that doesn't touch the brush-zoom signature. (3) **`useRef<boolean>(false)` capture at brushDown** (chosen). Minimal-diff, no signature changes to existing handlers, single load-bearing line at each touch-point (`brushModifierRef.current = isModifierClick(e)` / `if (brushModifierRef.current) ...` / `brushModifierRef.current = false`).

  AreaRenderer didn't need the ref dance because its dispatch fires inside the top-level `onClick` arrow which already accepts the MouseEvent. The two renderers' divergent shapes reflect a pre-existing divergence in how they handle clicks: Area dispatches inside `onClick`, Line dispatches inside `onBrushUp` (because Line additionally supports brush-zoom). The WD3 wiring respects that divergence rather than forcing one renderer to adopt the other's shape.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD3-wiring-rest-trend (18 new in `wd3WiringRestTrend.test.ts`) all pass. 143 cumulative WD3 + adjacent WD2-trend tests green (foundation 11 + wiring-bar 12 + wiring-rest-cat 44 + sheet 21 + wiring-rest-trend 18 + wd2DimTrend 19 + wd2WiringRestTrend 18), zero regression. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline). Client `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 53 errors (identical baseline).

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Scatter drill (WD3-wiring-rest-point)**. PointRenderer's WD2-wiring dispatch is per-point on `p.rawColor`, gated on `crossFilterReady && !!colorCh`. The WD3 wiring follows but the wave is small enough to ship as a standalone follow-on. ~60 LOC.
    - **Heatmap drill (WD3-wiring-rest-rect)**. Two-column drill payload design decision deferred. RectRenderer cells sit at the intersection of rowCh × colCh; the current single-`column: string` event field doesn't accommodate. Either widen the foundation's `DrillThroughEvent.column` type OR fire two events with the receiver de-duping.
    - **ECharts drill (WD3-wiring-echarts)**. 5 ECharts marks via the existing `onChartClick(params)` flow. `params.event.event` carries `metaKey`/`ctrlKey`, so `isModifierClick(params.event.event)` works with no foundation changes — the substantive work is the per-renderer dataIndex → (column, rawValue) mapping.
    - **Brush-zoom + cmd-held interaction nuance**. Currently a cmd-down + drag-zoom mouseup falls into the brush-zoom path (not the click path), so cmd-zoom is structurally equivalent to plain zoom. A future design might want a "cmd-zoom = drill into the zoomed range" intent, but that requires a richer DrillThroughEvent payload (range vs. single value) and a different receiver.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD3-sheet · DrillThroughSheet receiver closes the user-visible loop.** Pre-this-wave, WD3-foundation + WD3-wiring-bar + WD3-wiring-rest-cat shipped a `DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT` dispatcher and wired 6 of 15 chart kinds to fire it on cmd / ctrl-click — but no listener subscribed and no UI showed up. The user got zero feedback on a modifier-click; the wave's value was structurally complete but practically invisible. This wave wires the receiving end so the cmd / ctrl-click → side-sheet round-trip works end-to-end on Bar / Arc / Funnel / Box / Waterfall / Combo. The remaining 9 chart kinds (rect / trend / point / 5 ECharts marks) still don't dispatch, but for the 6 wired ones the user experience is now: cmd-click → right-side Radix Sheet slides in showing the drill request (chart id, column, value, active-filter snapshot) plus a placeholder pinning the WD3-server endpoint as the future row source.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DrillThroughSheet.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DrillThroughSheet.tsx) (new, ~140 LOC). Pure render component wrapping the Radix [`Sheet`](../client/src/components/ui/sheet.tsx) primitive (right-side slide-in, default side). Props: `{ event: DrillThroughEvent | null; onOpenChange: (open: boolean) => void }`. Critical design choice: `open` is DERIVED from `event !== null` inside the component, NOT a separate prop. The two-prop shape (`open` + `event`) is an anti-pattern — `open=true` could pair with `event=null` and render an empty sheet; `open=false` with `event` set wouldn't close the sheet. Single source of truth on the parent's side: clear `event` to null, the sheet closes. Body sections: a `<SheetHeader>` showing the column + canonicalised value (via [`toFilterValue`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts) from the crossFilter helper so display matches the wire-storage stringification — null / Date / number / boolean handled uniformly); a "Pinned slice" `<dl>` grid with chartId / column / value rows; a "Filter context at click time" section iterating the captured `event.filters` snapshot via a local `summariseFilters(filters)` helper that branches on each `ChartFilterSelection` type (categorical → `column ∈ {v1, v2}`; date → `column between start and end`; numeric → `column in [min, max]`); a dashed-border placeholder pinning the WD3-server endpoint name (`/api/dashboards/:id/drill`) so a future-Claude wiring the row-list fetch can grep "WD3-server" and swap in the real list.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardView.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardView.tsx) — three additions, all additive (no behavioural removal):
      - **Imports.** New named imports right after the existing `crossFilter` import block: `import { DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT, type DrillThroughEvent } from '../lib/drillThrough';` and `import { DrillThroughSheet } from './DrillThroughSheet';`. Both surfaces sit at the dispatch/receive locality so future Claude reads them as a pair.
      - **State.** `const [drillThroughEvent, setDrillThroughEvent] = useState<DrillThroughEvent | null>(null);` declared right after `isExportingPdf`. Null means closed sheet; the listener sets the slice; the sheet's `onOpenChange(false)` clears it back to null so a re-open with the same payload re-fires the slide-in animation (Radix Sheet keys the slide-in on `open: false → true` transitions, not on prop identity).
      - **Listener `useEffect`.** Sits immediately after the existing `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` listener for code-locality — dispatch and receive sit as a pair across both filter and drill intents. The shape mirrors cross-filter's (SSR-safe `typeof window` guard; `window.addEventListener` + return-cleanup `removeEventListener`), but the detail validation is STRICTER: requires BOTH `detail.chartId` AND `detail.column` to be strings. Cross-filter only validates `column` because the toggle/append/replace semantics are column-only. Drill-through requires `chartId` because the (future) WD3-server fetch needs it — a malformed event without chartId would otherwise show an empty drill sheet with no row source. On a valid event the handler stores the full detail (`setDrillThroughEvent(detail)`) so the sheet has access to `chartId` / `column` / `value` / `sourceTileId` / `filters` all at once.
      - **JSX mount.** Mounts `<DrillThroughSheet event={drillThroughEvent} onOpenChange={(open) => { if (!open) setDrillThroughEvent(null); }} />` AFTER `<ShareDashboardDialog>` at the dialog cluster locality (pinned in the test suite via a JSX ordering assertion so a future refactor doesn't accidentally hoist it inside the section render branch, which would tie its mount lifecycle to the active sheet rather than the dashboard).
    - [server/package.json](../server/package.json) — explicit `test` list extended by one entry per invariant #4 (`../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3Sheet.test.ts`).

  **Why this design.** Three alternative shapes were considered for the receiver. (1) **A drill-through context provider** (`<DrillThroughProvider>` wrapping the dashboard, holding the event in context, with a `useDrillThrough()` hook to consume). Rejected because the event captures state that only `DashboardView` needs to know about (the sheet mounts there; no other component should care about which drill is active). Context providers add indirection that doesn't earn its keep when the consumer count is 1. (2) **Co-locate the sheet body inline inside DashboardView's render** (no separate component). Rejected because DashboardView is already 1000+ LOC; adding 140 LOC of sheet body would balloon it further, and the sheet is genuinely independent (it doesn't read DashboardView's other state). The component-split keeps the LOC delta on DashboardView at +30 (state + import + listener + mount) and lets the sheet's render contract evolve independently. (3) **Single-component render with `open` + `event` as two parallel props** (the two-prop anti-pattern flagged above). Rejected for the drift reason — single source of truth via `open = event !== null` makes the contract impossible to mis-pair. The chosen shape — event-derived open, event-only prop — is the same pattern Radix itself recommends for its primitives (the `Dialog` `open` prop semantics work equivalently when controlled).

  The placeholder body (rather than a real row fetch) is the right shape for this wave because (a) WD3-server isn't ready and (b) the sheet's render contract is already complete — chartId / column / value / filters are all bound. When WD3-server lands, the body's "Row fetch lands with the WD3-server endpoint" section gets replaced with a TanStack-Query-fetched row list. The component's prop interface doesn't change.

  **Tests.** 21 source-inspection cases across 7 suites in [`wd3Sheet.test.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3Sheet.test.ts) (~240 LOC). Appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Source-inspection (not behavioural / jsdom) because DashboardView is a 1000+-LOC React component that's expensive to mount under jsdom without a wide context-provider mock stack (auth, query-client, dashboard, edit-mode, sheet-state, ...); the load-bearing shape lives in the listener body + the prop wiring, both of which read clearly off the source. The 7 suites:
    - **DashboardView imports drillThrough surfaces** (2): named imports of `DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT` + `DrillThroughEvent` type from `../lib/drillThrough`; import of `DrillThroughSheet` from `./DrillThroughSheet`.
    - **DashboardView holds drillThroughEvent state** (1): state slice declared with `useState<DrillThroughEvent | null>(null)`.
    - **DashboardView subscribes to DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT with cleanup** (4): addEventListener + return-cleanup pattern; STRICTER detail validation (chartId AND column); setter receives full detail; SSR-safe `typeof window === 'undefined'` guard.
    - **DashboardView mounts DrillThroughSheet with the right props** (2): prop wiring (event prop + onOpenChange clearing event to null on close); JSX ordering — sheet mounts AFTER `<ShareDashboardDialog>` at the dialog cluster locality.
    - **DrillThroughSheet imports + prop signature** (4): Radix Sheet primitives from `@/components/ui/sheet`; DrillThroughEvent type; toFilterValue from crossFilter for display canonicalisation; props interface shape.
    - **DrillThroughSheet render contract** (5): `open = event !== null` derived; `side="right"` slide-in; chartId / column / value field reads; toFilterValue call for the value display; WD3-server placeholder pin.
    - **summariseFilters covers all three ActiveChartFilters types** (3): categorical / date / numeric branches.

  88 cumulative WD3 tests now pass (foundation 11 + wiring-bar 12 + wiring-rest-cat 44 + sheet 21), zero regression. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline). Client `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 53 errors (identical baseline).

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Server-side row fetch (WD3-server).** The sheet's placeholder body explicitly notes WD3-server is the future row source. The endpoint `/api/dashboards/:id/drill?chartId=&column=&value=` will mirror the existing XLSX export endpoint's chart-row lookup path. Separate wave because it touches server / route registration / DuckDB lookup — orthogonal to client receiver shape.
    - **The other 9 chart kinds.** rect / trend / point on the visx side; treemap / sunburst / sankey / calendar / candlestick on the ECharts side. Each follows the WD3-wiring-* pattern (modifier branch at the top of onClick) but the per-renderer dataIndex → (column, rawValue) mapping is the substantive work per wave. The sheet listener already accepts events from any source — those waves are pure dispatcher additions.
    - **Sheet body customisation per chart type.** Different chart kinds might benefit from different sheet layouts (e.g. a candlestick drill might show OHLC + volume; a treemap drill might show the parent hierarchy). For now a uniform layout works because the underlying-rows display is the load-bearing piece — chart-specific framing is a later polish wave.
    - **Pagination / row-count cap / virtualisation.** A drill-through on a large categorical bucket could return tens of thousands of rows. The current placeholder doesn't render any rows, so this is purely a WD3-server design decision (default 1000-row cap with pagination, or stream-as-you-scroll with TanStack Query infinite query). Deferred to WD3-server.
    - **Telemetry / drill-usage analytics.** Track "user clicked drill-through" events for product analytics. Pure observability concern, not a UX one — separate wave.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD3-wiring-rest-cat · 5 categorical visx renderers cmd / ctrl-click → drill-through.** Fans out the WD3-wiring-bar pattern to the 5 categorical visx renderers that already share the BarRenderer's dispatch contract: [`ArcRenderer`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ArcRenderer.tsx) (donut / pie segments), [`FunnelRenderer`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/FunnelRenderer.tsx) (stages), [`BoxRenderer`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BoxRenderer.tsx) (box-plot rectangles), [`WaterfallRenderer`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/WaterfallRenderer.tsx) (delta bars, total-row carve-out preserved), and [`ComboRenderer`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ComboRenderer.tsx) (bars only — secondary-axis line marks deliberately un-wired). Each renderer's existing onClick widens to accept the event and gains a top-of-handler modifier-key branch that short-circuits `dispatchCrossFilter` and routes to `dispatchDrillThrough` instead. The wave closes the categorical-mark drill-through surface for the visx pack at 6 of 10 visx renderers, matching the WD2-wiring-rest-cat scope wave-for-wave.

  **What landed.** Each renderer received the same three localised changes that landed in WD3-wiring-bar:
    - **Import.** Added a second named-import block right after the existing `crossFilter` block: `import { dispatchDrillThrough, isModifierClick } from "@/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough";`. The two intent surfaces sit side-by-side at the import header so future Claude reads them as a pair. Pre-existing `dispatchCrossFilter` / `isCrossFilterActive` / `toFilterValue` imports untouched (regression-pinned per renderer).
    - **Arrow widening.** Each renderer's `onClick` arrow widens from `() => {...}` to `(event: React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>) => {...}`. `React.MouseEvent` resolves as a global namespace (every renderer already references it elsewhere — `onMouseMove` handlers, `localPoint(e)` typings, etc. — without importing `React` as a default). Same typing convention as WD3-wiring-bar.
    - **Modifier branch.** Added at the TOP of the handler body, BEFORE the pre-existing `dispatchCrossFilter` call:
      ```ts
      if (isModifierClick(event)) {
        dispatchDrillThrough({
          chartId: dashboardTile.tileId,
          column: <renderer-specific>,
          value: <renderer-specific raw>,
          sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId,
          filters: dashboardFilters,
        });
        return;
      }
      ```
      The renderer-specific column + raw-value pairs mirror the WD2-wiring-rest-cat dispatch carve-outs exactly:

      | Renderer | column expression | value (raw — NOT toFilterValue-coerced) |
      |---|---|---|
      | ArcRenderer | `labelCh.field` | `arc.data.rawKey` |
      | FunnelRenderer | `enc.x.field` | `s.rawLabel` |
      | BoxRenderer | `enc.x.field` | `s.rawCategory` |
      | WaterfallRenderer | `enc.x.field` | `b.rawCategory` (gated by outer `clickable` which AND-skips `b.isTotal`) |
      | ComboRenderer | `xCh.field` | `rawX` (bars only; secondary-axis `<LinePath>` not wired) |

      Drill-through value coercion is the SERVER's job — the type-original raw (Date / number / categorical string) lets the server's canonicaliser pick the right comparison for each column's inferred type. Coercing client-side via `toFilterValue` would lossy-stringify before the server saw it. Every renderer already lifts `dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters` at the top for the WD2-dim concern, so the WD3 payload reuses the same reference — no extra state.

    The WaterfallRenderer carve-out is the only carve-out worth calling out individually: its existing `onClick` is gated by `clickable` rather than `dashboardTile` (because `clickable = !!dashboardTile && !b.isTotal` — the AND-gate that excludes synthetic summary rows from cross-filter dispatch). The drill wiring keeps `clickable` as the outer guard, so a cmd-click on a total-row bar can't fire a drill event either. This is the right shape: total rows aren't categorical values the user can drill-into in the first place. ComboRenderer's carve-out is structural: only the bar `<Bar>` element gets the drill branch; the secondary-axis `<LinePath>` stays continuous and un-wired (a continuous trend has no per-mark categorical brush target — same rationale as the WD2-wiring-rest-cat dispatch carve-out).

    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringRestCat.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringRestCat.test.ts) (new, ~240 LOC). 44 source-inspection tests across 11 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. The suite parametrises over a 5-renderer table (name × column × raw-value × outer-gate × tileId-expression) so each new tested contract auto-fans across all five renderers. The test file structure:
      - **Per-renderer suites (5 × 2 suites = 10)**: imports (2 cases each: drillThrough named imports + WD2 untouched) and onClick branch shape (6 cases each: React.MouseEvent typing + branch order + 5-field payload + `return;` + raw-value negative pin + plain-click regression).
      - **Cross-cutting suite (1, 4 cases)**: `WD3-wiring-rest-cat` marker per renderer; column-symmetry pin (dim + cross-filter + drill all on the same column); WaterfallRenderer's outer gate is `clickable` (not `dashboardTile`); ComboRenderer dispatches drill EXACTLY ONCE (regex-counted — bars-only carve-out enforcement).

  **Why this design.** The 5 renderers share a common dispatch shape with BarRenderer (lifted `dashboardFilters` + `dashboardTile` + `dispatchCrossFilter` body + raw-value passed via `toFilterValue` on the wire), so the WD3 wiring layered on top is equally uniform — minimum-divergence between the WD2 and WD3 concerns in each renderer makes the per-renderer mental model "what does click do" simply "branch on modifier key, drill or filter". The alternative — extracting a shared `useChartTileClickIntent(event, payload)` hook or a `handleChartMarkClick(event, payload, mode)` helper — was rejected for the same reason WD3-wiring-bar rejected it: the WD2-wiring family established that per-renderer click handlers live inline + close over the cell / arc / segment local, which is the right pattern for the data-binding context. A helper would force every WD3-wiring-* wave to refactor its renderer's call-site shape away from the inline closure pattern that the rest of the family uses.

  The parametric test-table choice (a single `renderers: Array<{ name, src, column, rawValue, tileIdExpr, outerGate }>` driving a `for (const r of renderers)` loop) is the right shape because the 5 renderers vary in exactly 4 axes (column expression, raw-value identifier, outer gate, tile-id expression), and a non-parametric test file would have repeated the same 6 assertions 5 times verbatim. The cross-cutting suite stays separate because it tests properties that DON'T vary per renderer (the WD3-wiring-rest-cat marker, column-symmetry across the three concerns, structural carve-outs that are renderer-specific in their own right). A future WD3-wiring-rest-rect wave that varies in a 5th axis (e.g. "dispatches two columns at once") can extend the table cleanly.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD3-wiring-rest-cat (44 new in `wd3WiringRestCat.test.ts`) all pass. WD3-wiring-bar (12) + drillThrough (11) + WD2-wiring-rest-cat (36) + WD2-dim-cat (27) all green — 130 cumulative drill / dim / wiring tests across the categorical visx renderer surface, zero regression. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline). Client `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new typecheck errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Heatmap drill (WD3-wiring-rest-rect)**. RectRenderer cells sit at the intersection of two columns (rowCh × colCh) so the drill payload needs a two-column shape — the current single-`column: string` event field doesn't accommodate that. Two possible shapes: (1) widen `DrillThroughEvent.column` to `string | { row: string; col: string }`; (2) keep single-column and fire two events with the receiver de-duping. Decision deferred to the WD3-wiring-rest-rect wave proper because the receiving side-sheet (WD3-sheet) also needs to know which shape to consume.
    - **Trend drill (WD3-wiring-rest-trend)**. Line / Area renderers' WD2-wiring shape is nearest-x lookup via `bisector(...).left` — different shape from the per-mark click. Drill mirrors that lookup but the test fixture is more involved (jsdom-style mock of `localPoint(e)` + `bisector` invariants). Separate wave.
    - **Scatter drill (WD3-wiring-rest-point)**. PointRenderer dispatches per-point on `p.rawColor` (WD2-wiring-rest-point); drill follows but is gated on `crossFilterReady` + `!!colorCh` like the dispatch.
    - **ECharts drill (WD3-wiring-echarts)**. The 5 ECharts marks (Treemap / Sunburst / Sankey / Calendar / Candlestick) read clicks via `onChartClick(params)` with a different event-shape contract — `params` carries `componentType`, `dataIndex`, `value`, etc. rather than `MouseEvent`. `isModifierClick` already accepts a sparse `{ metaKey?, ctrlKey? }` event shape and ECharts' params object includes the `event.event` raw DOM event we can read; but the per-renderer wiring decision (which dataIndex maps to which column / rawValue) is the substantive work.
    - **Hover-time cursor change** (e.g. `cursor: "zoom-in"` on cmd-hover). Skipped here for the same reason as WD3-wiring-bar — needs a keydown / keyup window listener. Polish wave, deferred.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD3-wiring-bar · BarRenderer cmd / ctrl-click → drill-through.** First per-renderer consumer of yesterday's [`drillThrough.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough.ts) foundation. The pre-WD3 [`BarRenderer.tsx`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx) `onClick` had a clean two-branch shape — `if (grid.inGrid) { grid.toggleFilter(...) }` for chat / explorer + `if (dashboardTile) { dispatchCrossFilter(...) }` for the dashboard tile — with both branches firing on a parameterless arrow `() => {...}`. The WD3 modifier-key intent layers ON TOP without disturbing either pre-existing path: a top-of-handler branch gated on `dashboardTile && isModifierClick(event)` short-circuits to `dispatchDrillThrough({...})` and returns; non-modifier clicks fall through to the pre-wave behaviour byte-for-byte.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx). Three localised changes — additive, no removal:
      - **Import.** Added a second named-import block right after the existing `crossFilter` block: `import { dispatchDrillThrough, isModifierClick } from "@/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough";`. The two intent surfaces (cross-filter + drill-through) sit side-by-side at the import header so future Claude reads them as a pair. The pre-existing `dispatchCrossFilter` / `isCrossFilterActive` / `toFilterValue` import is untouched (negative-pinned in the test suite).
      - **Arrow widening.** The `onClick` arrow widens from `() => {...}` to `(event: React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>) => {...}` so the modifier check can read the event flags. The event-parameter typing matches the existing `onMouseMove` handler immediately above — same React MouseEvent contract.
      - **Modifier branch.** Added at the TOP of the handler body (BEFORE `if (grid.inGrid)` and `if (dashboardTile) dispatchCrossFilter`):
        ```ts
        if (dashboardTile && isModifierClick(event)) {
          dispatchDrillThrough({
            chartId: dashboardTile.tileId,
            column: enc.x.field,
            value: c.outerRaw,
            sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId,
            filters: dashboardFilters,
          });
          return;
        }
        ```
        The 5-field payload: **`chartId: dashboardTile.tileId`** because on a dashboard the tile id IS the chart-by-position identifier (`chart-0`, `chart-1`, ...) — same lookup convention the XLSX export endpoint already uses. **`column: enc.x.field`** mirrors the WD2-wiring-bar dispatch column + the WD2-dim-bar dim column so all three concerns key on the same axis (pinned in a cross-cutting test). **`value: c.outerRaw`** is the type-original raw — NOT `toFilterValue(c.outerRaw)`; drill-through value coercion is the SERVER's job (the server's canonicaliser picks the right Date / number / categorical comparison based on the column's inferred type, so a client-side lossy stringification would force the server to undo the cast). **`sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId`** mirrors the `CrossFilterEvent.sourceTileId` shape so future tile-scoped UI ("highlight the originating tile while the drill-sheet is open") has the lookup it needs. **`filters: dashboardFilters`** threads the already-lifted dashboard-wide filter map (originally lifted at the top of the renderer for the WD2-dim concern) so the server applies the dashboard's currently-active filter context BEFORE pinning (column, value) — fixes the race between a cmd-click and a concurrent global-filter edit on another tile.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringBar.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd3WiringBar.test.ts) (new, ~200 LOC). 12 source-inspection tests across 3 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Source-inspection (not pure-function) because the wave's load-bearing artefact is JSX inside a React component — running the renderer would need a vdom harness for marginal value. The suite slices into 3 groups:
      - **Imports** (2): named import of `isModifierClick` + `dispatchDrillThrough` from `@/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough`; WD2 crossFilter imports unchanged (additive-change pin).
      - **onClick branch shape** (8): event-parameter typing (`React.MouseEvent<SVGElement>`); branch order (modifier FIRST so it short-circuits before grid.inGrid + dispatchCrossFilter); `dashboardTile && isModifierClick(event)` gate (drill is dashboard-only); 5-field payload shape; `return;` after dispatch (single-intent contract); value passed RAW with a negative pin against `toFilterValue(` inside the drill block; WD2 cross-filter dispatch still fires on plain click (regression pin); chat / explorer grid.inGrid path unchanged (regression pin).
      - **Cross-cutting contracts** (2): `WD3-wiring-bar` marker present (grep-ability); dim / dispatch / drill all key on `enc.x.field` (symmetry pin — drift would produce a "click-to-drill on a column you can't click-to-filter" UX mismatch).

  **Why this design.** Three alternative shapes were considered. (1) **Top-level conditional, two parallel handlers.** Split `onClick` into `(event) => isModifierClick(event) ? handleDrill(event) : handlePlainClick(event)`. Rejected: forces an awkward refactor of the existing branch tree (chat-vs-dashboard) into two parallel branch trees, adds 30 LOC of duplication on something that's a 5-line guard inside the same handler. (2) **An extracted `useDashboardClickIntent()` hook returning a 3-state intent.** Rejected: forces every WD3-wiring-* wave to refactor its renderer's call-site shape away from the inline closure pattern; the WD2-wiring family establishes that per-renderer click handlers live inline + close over the cell / arc / segment local, which is the right pattern for the data-binding context. (3) **Inline guard at the top of the existing handler** (chosen). Minimal diff, preserves the existing branch tree byte-for-byte under the guard, and reads naturally: "if a dashboard-tile click is modifier-held, drill instead". The guard's AND-gate (`dashboardTile && isModifierClick(event)`) is load-bearing — without the `dashboardTile` left-operand, a chat / explorer modifier-click would attempt to dispatch a drill-through event that has no listener (drill-through is a dashboard-only feature). With the gate, chat / explorer cmd-clicks fall through to the grid.inGrid filter path unchanged, preserving the chat / explorer UX exactly.

  The decision to thread `dashboardFilters` into the `filters` snapshot rather than letting the server look up the active filter map by tile id afterwards is a robustness-vs-cleanliness trade-off. Lookup-by-tile-id would be cleaner but introduces a race: between the click time and the server arriving at the lookup, another tile's cross-filter dispatch could mutate `globalFilters`. Capturing the filter snapshot inline at click time makes the drill-through deterministic — the rows the server returns reflect the filter context the user saw at click time. The cost is one map serialisation per click; the gain is determinism.

  The `chartId === sourceTileId === dashboardTile.tileId` triple equality might look redundant. It isn't: `chartId` is the server-facing identifier (which chart's underlying rows to fetch), `sourceTileId` is the client-facing identifier (which UI tile fired the event), and `dashboardTile.tileId` is the renderer-local source of both. They happen to coincide on a dashboard because the dashboard's chart-by-position convention assigns the same string to both roles — but the event's two fields stay semantically distinct so a future "duplicate chart" feature (where the same chartId might back two tiles) doesn't have to refactor the event payload.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD3-wiring-bar (12 new in `wd3WiringBar.test.ts`) all pass. WD2 family unchanged. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline). Client `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new typecheck errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Visual feedback at click time** (no flash / no cursor change on cmd-hover). The cursor stays `pointer` regardless of modifier state because the modifier intent is a discrete branch, not a hover-time mode. A future polish wave could add a `cursor: "zoom-in"` or similar on cmd-hover, but that needs a `useEffect` listening for keydown / keyup at the window level — separate concern.
    - **Listener + side-sheet** (the receiving end). Today the event fires into the void on a real dashboard (no listener subscribes to `DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT` yet). WD3-sheet wires the DashboardView `useEffect` + the `<DrillThroughSheet>` Radix component; WD3-server wires the `/api/dashboards/:id/drill` endpoint.
    - **The other 14 renderers.** WD3-wiring-rest-cat (5 cat renderers), WD3-wiring-rest-rect (heatmap — needs a two-column drill payload OR a single-column shape decision), WD3-wiring-rest-trend (Line + Area — nearest-x lookup), WD3-wiring-rest-point (scatter — per-point on colorCh), WD3-wiring-echarts (5 ECharts marks via `onChartClick` params) follow in subsequent waves. Each ~50–80 LOC + tests.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD3-foundation · drill-through pure helper module.** The WD2-wiring + WD2-dim families closed end-to-end yesterday at 15 of 15 chart kinds with a categorical filter target (10 visx + 5 ECharts). The next 1000x master-plan promise on Workstream 4 is drill-through: cmd / ctrl held during a chart-mark click opens a side-sheet showing the underlying rows behind that data point. The detection of cmd / ctrl must be uniform across all 15 renderers — same "share the helper, not the wiring" precedent set by WD2's [`crossFilter.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts) — so this foundation wave ships the pure helper before any renderer wires it in.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough.ts) (new, ~110 LOC). Mirrors [`crossFilter.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts)'s public shape so the two click intents stay co-located in the renderer's mental model:
      - `DrillThroughEvent` interface — `chartId: string`, `column: string`, `value: unknown`, optional `sourceTileId: string` + `filters?: ActiveChartFilters` snapshot. `value` is widened to `unknown` to match the precedent set by `toFilterValue` / `isCrossFilterActive` (both accept the BarCell.outerRaw type-original); the `filters` snapshot lets the server endpoint apply the dashboard's currently-active global + per-tile filter context BEFORE pinning (column, value) so the drilled-into rows respect the current filter state. The required-vs-optional split mirrors `CrossFilterEvent`: `chartId` + `column` + `value` are required so a renderer with no enclosing dashboard tile (chat / explorer) wouldn't dispatch a partial event anyway.
      - `DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT = "marico:drill-through"` — canonical CustomEvent name. The `marico:` prefix namespaces apart from anything chart libraries (recharts / echarts) might dispatch on window — mirrors `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT = "marico:cross-filter"`.
      - `isModifierClick(event)` — cross-platform modifier check. macOS uses `metaKey` (⌘); Windows / Linux use `ctrlKey`. EITHER flag fires drill-through (OR-truth, not AND — Safari occasionally synthesises both flags on certain events, and the contract should accept that gracefully). Accepts a sparse event shape `{ metaKey?: boolean; ctrlKey?: boolean } | undefined | null` so the three event shapes used by the WD2-wiring family — React synthetic / native DOM / ECharts onChartClick — all pass typecheck. `undefined` / `null` event → `false` (defensive fallback to the safe cross-filter intent if a renderer somehow loses its event in a test or SSR path).
      - `dispatchDrillThrough(event)` — fires the CustomEvent on `window`. No-op in non-browser env (SSR, server-test); returns `true` iff actually dispatched. Mirrors `dispatchCrossFilter`'s SSR-safe short-circuit shape: `if (typeof window === "undefined" || typeof CustomEvent === "undefined") return false;` then `window.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent<DrillThroughEvent>(DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT, { detail: event }))`.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough.test.ts) (new, ~140 LOC). 11 pure-function tests across 4 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Mirrors [`crossFilter.test.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.test.ts)'s approach (actual import + runtime assertions, NOT source-inspection — the helper has no React dependency so we can exercise it directly).
      - **DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT canonical name** (1): pin against rename.
      - **isModifierClick** (5): metaKey held → true; ctrlKey held → true; both flags → true; neither → false; null / undefined event → false; unrelated `shiftKey` / `altKey` ignored (negative pin against a future "any-modifier" widening).
      - **dispatchDrillThrough runtime** (2): returns false in a no-window env (node:test); returns false on a minimal event payload to confirm CustomEvent-undefined branch.
      - **DrillThroughEvent shape contract** (2): minimal-event acceptance (chartId + column + value with null / unknown value); full-event acceptance (filters snapshot with mixed date + categorical selections; sourceTileId).
    - [server/package.json](../server/package.json) — explicit `test` list extended by one entry per invariant #4 (`../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/drillThrough.test.ts`). Server `npm test` is an explicit file list, not a glob — a new test file not appended is silently skipped.

  **Why this design.** Three alternative shapes were considered for the modifier-detection layer. (1) **Inline detection per renderer.** Rejected because cmd-vs-ctrl handling has to stay uniform across 15 renderers (10 visx + 5 ECharts) — duplicating `event.metaKey || event.ctrlKey` 15 times invites drift. The WD2 precedent established a single pure helper as the canonical mechanism. (2) **A custom React hook (`useModifierClick()`)**. Rejected because the WD2 path is non-hook — the renderer's onClick handler closure reads `dashboardTile` from `useDashboardTileContext()` once at render time, then any per-event branching happens inside the handler body without further hook calls (you can't call hooks inside an event handler). Adding a hook would force every WD3-wiring-* wave to refactor its renderer's call-site shape away from the closure pattern. (3) **A pure helper module mirroring crossFilter.ts** (chosen). Same shape consistency, same import pattern, same SSR-safe `dispatchX` contract. The renderer's onClick handler will look like: `if (isModifierClick(event)) dispatchDrillThrough({...}); else dispatchCrossFilter({...});` — a clean two-line branch that future Claude reads as a pair.

  The `value: unknown` widening on `DrillThroughEvent` is a deliberate choice. `CrossFilterEvent.value` is `string | number | boolean | null | undefined`, but `isCrossFilterActive` already widened to `unknown` in WD2-dim-bar to let renderers pass `BarCell.outerRaw` (typed `unknown` after the pipeline strips concrete types). Mirroring the wider type here keeps the WD3-wiring renderer code-equivalent: a renderer reading `c.outerRaw` for the cross-filter dispatch reads the SAME `c.outerRaw` for the drill-through dispatch — no second narrowing cast. The server endpoint applies its own canonicalisation when querying the underlying rows; client-side coercion would just duplicate work.

  The optional `filters: ActiveChartFilters` snapshot on `DrillThroughEvent` (NOT present on `CrossFilterEvent`) reflects a fundamental difference between the two intents. Cross-filter dispatch is purely additive — it edits the dashboard-wide filter map and the entire dashboard re-renders against the new filters automatically. Drill-through dispatch is a server-side query that needs to know the ENTIRE filter context up front so it can apply all of them before pinning the clicked (column, value). Threading the snapshot through the event lets the renderer capture the filters atomically at click time (no race with a concurrent global-filter edit by another tile).

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD3-foundation (11 new in `drillThrough.test.ts`) all pass; the rest of the WD2 family (crossFilter 29 + dashboardTileContext 16 + wd2WiringRestCat 36 + wd2WiringRestRect 13 + wd2WiringRestTrend 19 + wd2WiringRestPoint 19 + wd2WiringEcharts 23 + wd2DimFoundation 11 + wd2DimBar 16 + wd2DimCat 27 + wd2DimRect 13 + wd2DimTrend 19 + wd2DimPoint 19 + wd2DimEchartsTreemap 19 + wd2DimEchartsRest 23 — pre-existing) untouched. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline). Client `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new typecheck errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Per-renderer onClick wiring**. The 15 renderers (10 visx + 5 ECharts) each need a small onClick branch added: `if (isModifierClick(event)) { dispatchDrillThrough({...}); return; }` before the existing `dispatchCrossFilter({...})` call. Deferred to a sequence of follow-on waves (WD3-wiring-bar; WD3-wiring-rest-cat for the 5 cat renderers; WD3-wiring-rest-rect for heatmap; WD3-wiring-rest-trend for Line + Area; WD3-wiring-rest-point for scatter; WD3-wiring-echarts for the 5 ECharts marks). Each wave ~50–80 LOC + tests.
    - **DashboardView listener + side-sheet**. The receiving end of the event (a `useEffect` subscribing to `DRILL_THROUGH_EVENT` + a `<DrillThroughSheet>` Radix Dialog / Sheet component) is the next wave's scope (WD3-sheet). It will hold a state slice `{ open: boolean; chartId: string; column: string; value: unknown; filters: ActiveChartFilters }` and render a fetch-driven row list.
    - **Server endpoint `/api/dashboards/:id/drill?chartId=&column=&value=`**. Returns underlying rows for a (chart, column, value) pinned by the active filter snapshot. Deferred to a server-side wave (WD3-server). Approach will mirror the existing `/api/dashboards/:id/export/xlsx` endpoint's chart-row lookup path — that endpoint already knows how to project each chart's backing rows for export.
    - **Browser-equiv tests** for `dispatchDrillThrough` in a DOM environment. node:test runs without a DOM by default, so the dispatch path that actually fires the CustomEvent isn't exercised today. The dim-OFF short-circuit IS pinned (returns `false` when `typeof window === "undefined"`). A future jsdom integration test could exercise the dispatch path end-to-end, but the pure helper has no logic on the actual-dispatch branch beyond the CustomEvent constructor call — the value is marginal.
    - **Shift / alt as additional modifier intents**. Some applications reserve shift-click for multi-select and alt-click for additive operations. The current contract is strictly cmd / ctrl for drill-through; the test suite pins a negative against `shiftKey` / `altKey` triggering drill-through. A future "additive drill-through" or "multi-pin drill-through" wave could extend `isModifierClick` to a richer return shape, but that's not on the master plan.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-echarts-rest · SankeyRenderer + CalendarRenderer + CandlestickRenderer per-dataItem dim.** Closes the WD2-dim-* family entirely. WD2-dim-echarts-treemap shipped 2 of 5 ECharts marks via the inline-itemStyle mechanism inside the `tree` memo (matching leaves emit byte-identical pre-wave shape via conditional spread). The three remaining renderers in [`SpecialtyRenderers.tsx`](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx) — Sankey, Calendar, Candlestick — have different per-dataItem data shapes (nodes-array; tuple array; OHLC tuple array) plus downstream consumers (`range` memo + `visualMap.min/max` for Calendar) that read the pre-wave tuple form. The shape choice that defines this wave: a SEPARATE `dimmedX` memo per renderer that emits a dim-aware data array consumed by ECharts, while the pre-wave data memo stays byte-identical for the downstream consumers. The dim memo short-circuits to identity when dim is OFF (`if (!dashboardDimActive) return data;`) so the `optionsKey` JSON is byte-identical to the pre-wave shape — no unnecessary canvas re-render on mount.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx) — three renderer additions. Each follows the same shape: lift the dim triplet right after the renderer-specific `onChartClick` `useCallback` (mirrors the WD2-dim-echarts-treemap code-locality with dispatch); add a `dimmedX` `useMemo` with identity short-circuit on dim-OFF; rewire the existing `optionsKey` memo to read `dimmedX` (keeping the JSON field name as the pre-wave key for byte-stability); bind the buildOptions series `data` to `dimmedX`.
    - **SankeyRenderer**. Per-node dim on `sourceCh.field` (mirrors the dispatch column). `nodes: Array<{ name: string }>` widens to `Array<{ name: string; itemStyle?: { opacity?: number } }>` via the dim-memo return type. Non-matching nodes promoted via spread (`{ ...n, itemStyle: { opacity: 0.4 } }`); matching nodes pass through identically. Edges (`links`) stay untouched — same carve-out as the WD2-wiring-echarts dispatch path (an edge has no single categorical value to filter on, so dimming would have no membership target). The dim memo's deps `[nodes, dashboardDimActive, dashboardFilters, sourceCh.field]` ensure dim-state changes rebuild the array. The `{ nodes, links }` parent memo stays untouched — the dim concern lives downstream of the data-construction concern.
    - **CalendarRenderer**. Per-cell dim on `dateCh.field`. The pre-wave `series` is `Array<[string, number]>` (ISO date string + value tuples); the dim memo emits `Array<[string, number] | { value: [string, number]; itemStyle: { opacity: number } }>`. ECharts heatmap accepts both forms in the same data array — matching cells stay as tuples (byte-identical pre-wave), non-matching cells get promoted to the rich-object form. The `range` memo + `visualMap.min/max` computations downstream continue to consume the pre-wave `series` (pre-promotion) so their tuple destructuring (`series.map(([s]) => ...)`, `series.map(([, v]) => v)`) stays safe — the dim concern is encapsulated to the series-data flow to ECharts only. The pre-wave `optionsKey` memo was moved BELOW the dim memo + rewired to read `series: dimmedSeries` (field name stays as `series` for byte-identical JSON on dim-off).
    - **CandlestickRenderer**. Per-bar dim on `xCh.field`. The dim membership check uses `xs[i]` (the categorical x-axis label) NOT the OHLC tuple values themselves — OHLC are quantitative; the categorical key for the dim factor lives in the parallel `xs` array. The dim memo's deps include `xs` so a reshuffling of the categorical axis triggers a dim recompute. Non-matching tuples promoted to `{ value: tuple, itemStyle: { opacity: 0.4 } }`. The pre-wave `optionsKey` memo rewired to read `dimmedSeries` (field name stays as `series`).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimEchartsRest.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimEchartsRest.test.ts) (new, ~270 LOC). 23 tests across 4 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. The test file slices `SpecialtyRenderers.tsx` into per-renderer bodies via `indexOf("export function <Name>Renderer")` so assertions can't false-match across renderers.
      - **SankeyRenderer per-node dim** (6): lifted triplet on `sourceCh.field`; `dimmedNodes` memo identity short-circuit on dim-OFF; non-matching node spread shape; `optionsKey` field-name preservation; series data binding; edges stay un-dimmed (negative pin).
      - **CalendarRenderer per-cell dim** (7): lifted triplet on `dateCh.field`; `dimmedSeries` identity short-circuit; non-matching cell tuple→object promotion; matching cells stay as tuples (byte-identical pre-wave); `optionsKey` field-name preservation; range memo + visualMap min/max consume pre-wave `series` not `dimmedSeries`; series data binding.
      - **CandlestickRenderer per-bar dim** (7): lifted triplet on `xCh.field`; `dimmedSeries` identity short-circuit; dim membership against `xs[i]` not OHLC values; non-matching tuple→object promotion; deps include `xs` for reshuffle-recompute; `optionsKey` field-name preservation; series data binding.
      - **Cross-cutting contracts** (3): 0.4 dim factor consistent; `WD2-dim-echarts-rest` marker per renderer; dim/dispatch column matches per renderer (Sankey: `sourceCh.field`; Calendar: `dateCh.field`; Candlestick: `xCh.field`).

  **Why this design.** Two implementation shapes were considered for each renderer. (1) **Inline injection into the pre-wave data memo** (like WD2-dim-echarts-treemap). Rejected for Calendar + Candlestick because both have downstream tuple-destructuring consumers (`range`, `visualMap.min/max`) — mixing tuple and rich-object forms inside the same array would break those iterators. The TreemapRenderer pattern worked there because the `tree` array had no downstream consumers; Calendar + Candlestick aren't that lucky. Inline injection WOULD have worked for SankeyRenderer (no downstream consumers of `nodes`), but using a separate dim memo there too keeps the wave uniform across the three renderers — one mental model, one test pattern. (2) **Separate `dimmedX` memo with identity short-circuit** (chosen). The pre-wave data memo stays byte-identical for any downstream consumer; the dim concern is encapsulated to a single derived memo that flows to ECharts. The identity short-circuit (`if (!dashboardDimActive) return data;`) is the load-bearing piece: dim-off transitions never churn the `optionsKey` JSON because `dimmedX === data` by reference equality, and the JSON serialiser produces a byte-identical stream. The `optionsKey` field name was kept as the pre-wave key (`nodes` for Sankey, `series` for Calendar + Candlestick) by writing `{ nodes: dimmedNodes, ... }` and `{ series: dimmedSeries, ... }` — the JSON property name is what `JSON.stringify` writes, and matching the pre-wave name preserves the dim-off JSON byte-stream. Two alternative naming schemes were considered: (a) rename the field to `dimmedNodes` / `dimmedSeries` — rejected because the dim-off JSON would diverge from the pre-wave shape, churning the optionsKey on initial mount without any visual change. (b) Drop the optionsKey memo entirely and rely on the `data` array identity as the re-render trigger — rejected because EChartsBase's mount-effect runs once with empty deps and reads `optionsKey` from its props, so the optionsKey IS the canonical re-render trigger; bypassing it would require a deeper refactor of EChartsBase's render-trigger contract. The decision to put the dim membership check on `xs[i]` rather than the OHLC values for Candlestick is the third design choice: the OHLC tuple `[open, close, low, high]` is quantitative (4 numeric values) — a "filter by OHLC value" interpretation has no meaningful business semantics. The categorical key for a candlestick bar IS its x-axis label (typically an ISO date for a time-series candlestick), and that's where the dispatch fires too (`xs[dataIndex]`). Pairing dim membership to the same lookup keeps the dim/dispatch behaviour symmetric — a click that toggles a categorical x-axis filter brushes the same bars that dim under that filter elsewhere.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-echarts-rest (23 new in `wd2DimEchartsRest.test.ts`) + the rest of the WD2-dim-* family (16 + 13 + 27 + 13 + 19 + 19 + 19 = 126 pre-existing across foundation, bar, cat, rect, trend, point, echarts-treemap) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing) + WD2-wiring-echarts (23 pre-existing — onChartClick wiring untouched) all green. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **ECharts opacity-callback alternative.** ECharts supports `series.itemStyle.opacity` as a callback function `(params) => number` that receives the dataIndex. The callback could read the dim state from a closure, avoiding the per-dataItem object promotion. Rejected because callback functions don't serialise via `JSON.stringify` (they stringify to `"[Function]"` or skip entirely), which would break the `optionsKey` re-render trigger contract. The per-dataItem injection is the right shape for the `optionsKey`-driven re-render model EChartsBase already uses.
    - **Edge dim for Sankey on cross-column source/target.** When source and target are different columns (e.g. `Region → Channel`), an edge represents a specific (source, target) intersection that could in principle be dimmed if either column's filter excludes it. Rejected because WD2-wiring-echarts deliberately deferred cross-column dispatch via the same carve-out — dispatch doesn't fire on edges, so dim on edges would have no reciprocal action.
    - **Parallel / Choropleth / Gauge dim.** Same skip list as WD2-wiring-echarts. Parallel lines are continuous (no categorical target). Choropleth is a stub awaiting geo registration. Gauge is a single-value KPI.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-echarts-treemap · TreemapRenderer + SunburstRenderer leaf-only dim on `labelCh.field`.** First wave on the WD2-dim-echarts series. Closes 2 of 5 ECharts marks. Diverges from the visx pack's mechanism in a fundamental way: visx renderers post-render mutate per-mark `fillOpacity` / `strokeOpacity` via React JSX props inside `.map((p) => <Circle … />)` bodies. ECharts mounts its own canvas instance via `EChartsBase` and reads styling from the per-dataItem `itemStyle.opacity` field at series-construction time — there's no post-render React boundary to intercept. The dim factor must therefore be injected inline into the dataItem objects inside each renderer's `tree` memo, not as a post-render prop. This is the shape choice that defines every WD2-dim-echarts-* wave.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/TreemapRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/TreemapRenderer.tsx). `isCrossFilterActive` added to the crossFilter named-import alongside the already-present `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. `TreemapNode.itemStyle` widened from `{ color?: string }` to `{ color?: string; opacity?: number }` — the minimum change that lets per-dataItem dim factors live inline. Triplet lifted right after the existing `onChartClick` `useCallback` (dispatch + dim share the same code locality as discussed for WD2-dim-point — defined first dispatch, then dim, so future Claude reads them as a pair):
      ```ts
      const dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters;
      const labelFilterSel = dashboardFilters?.[labelCh.field];
      const dashboardDimActive =
        !!labelFilterSel &&
        labelFilterSel.type === "categorical" &&
        labelFilterSel.values.length > 0;
      ```
      Crucially placed BEFORE the `tree` memo so the memo can consume it. Inside the `tree` memo, a local `dimLeaf(name: string): TreemapNode["itemStyle"] | undefined` arrow encapsulates the dim test:
      ```ts
      const dimLeaf = (name: string): TreemapNode["itemStyle"] | undefined =>
        dashboardDimActive &&
        !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, labelCh.field, name)
          ? { opacity: 0.4 }
          : undefined;
      ```
      Both the flat (`!groupCh`) and hierarchical (with `groupCh`) projections use `dimLeaf(name)` and conditional-spread:
      ```ts
      return Array.from(totals.entries()).map(([name, value]) => {
        const itemStyle = dimLeaf(name);
        return itemStyle ? { name, value, itemStyle } : { name, value };
      });
      ```
      Matching leaves emit `{ name, value }` — byte-identical to the pre-wave shape, so `optionsKey = JSON.stringify({ tree, w, h })` doesn't churn when no filter is active. Tree memo deps widened from `[data, labelCh, valueCh, groupCh]` to `[data, labelCh, valueCh, groupCh, dashboardDimActive, dashboardFilters]` so dim-state changes rebuild the tree → `optionsKey` updates → ECharts re-renders the canvas with the new opacity values. Parents (the `groupCh` value, when present) stay un-dimmed because they're structural hierarchy, not the filterable mark — mirrors the WD2-wiring-echarts leaf-only dispatch carve-out.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx) (SunburstRenderer). Same dim shape as TreemapRenderer. `SunburstNode` interface widened to add `itemStyle?: { opacity?: number }` (Sunburst's pre-wave node had no `itemStyle` field at all — the wave introduces it cleanly). The `useDashboardTileContext()` call relocated from after `optionsKey` to before the `tree` memo so the dim triplet can sit between (lifted then consumed by the memo). `onSunburstClick` `useCallback` and `optionsKey` memo orderings preserved. The crossFilter import block extended to include `isCrossFilterActive` (applies to all five renderers in `SpecialtyRenderers.tsx` — TreemapRenderer's file is independent).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimEchartsTreemap.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimEchartsTreemap.test.ts) (new, ~290 LOC). 19 tests across 7 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **TreemapRenderer imports + node-type widening** (2): `isCrossFilterActive` named-imported; `TreemapNode.itemStyle` widened to `{ color?: string; opacity?: number }`.
      - **TreemapRenderer dim triplet** (3): `dashboardFilters` / `labelFilterSel` / `dashboardDimActive` lifted on `labelCh.field` with full categorical guards; triplet sits BEFORE the tree memo; triplet sits AFTER `onChartClick` (dispatch defined first then dim — code-locality with WD2-wiring-echarts).
      - **TreemapRenderer dimLeaf helper + tree-memo wiring** (4): `dimLeaf(name)` returns `{ opacity: 0.4 }` for non-matching leaves; called in BOTH branches; conditional spread preserves byte-identical pre-wave shape for matching leaves; tree memo dep array includes `dashboardDimActive` + `dashboardFilters`.
      - **SunburstRenderer imports + node-type widening** (2): mirrors TreemapRenderer's set on SpecialtyRenderers source.
      - **SunburstRenderer dim triplet** (2): lifted triplet + before-tree-memo placement.
      - **SunburstRenderer dimLeaf helper + tree-memo wiring** (3): `dimLeaf` definition; both branches projection (scoped to the Sunburst body via `indexOf("export function SunburstRenderer") … indexOf("export function SankeyRenderer")` to avoid pollution from other renderers in the same file); dep array.
      - **Cross-cutting contracts** (3): 0.4 dim factor consistent across the WD2-dim-* family; matching leaves emit a byte-identical pre-wave shape (`{ name, value }` no itemStyle field); both source files carry the `WD2-dim-echarts-treemap` marker for future grep-ability.

  **Why this design.** Three implementation shapes were considered. (1) **Filter the tree before construction**: drop non-matching leaves entirely from the `tree` memo so ECharts simply doesn't render them. Rejected — would visually equate "filtered out" with "didn't exist", losing the dim-vs-hide distinction that the WD2-dim-* family is built on. Also reshapes the tree topology (a parent might end up with zero children), causing the layout to shift on every filter toggle — visually unstable. (2) **Inject opacity into the series-level `itemStyle`**: set a uniform opacity on the series object inside `buildOptions`. Rejected because series-level `itemStyle` applies to ALL dataItems (no per-leaf granularity), so it would dim every leaf uniformly. (3) **Per-dataItem `itemStyle.opacity` injection** (chosen): set `{ opacity: 0.4 }` on each non-matching leaf at tree-build time, leave matching leaves with no itemStyle (byte-identical to pre-wave). The conditional-spread pattern is the load-bearing piece: matching leaves emit exactly the pre-wave shape so `optionsKey` stays stable on a dim-off render (no ECharts re-render churn when the user clears a filter). The `dimLeaf` helper lifted as a local arrow inside the memo body — rather than as a module-level function — is the second design choice: it captures `dashboardDimActive` + `dashboardFilters` + `labelCh.field` via closure so the per-leaf call site stays brief (`dimLeaf(name)` vs. `dimLeafIf(dashboardDimActive, dashboardFilters, labelCh.field, name)`). Lifting it inside the memo also pairs the helper's lifecycle with the dim factor's input deps — when those change, both rebuild together. The leaf-only carve-out (parents stay un-dimmed) is the third design choice: it mirrors the WD2-wiring-echarts dispatch carve-out for the same reason — parents are structural hierarchy, not the filterable mark, and the dispatch column would diverge between rings if parent-ring filtering were wired (two-column dispatch via the RectRenderer pattern is a deferred follow-on).

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-echarts-treemap (19 new in `wd2DimEchartsTreemap.test.ts`) + the rest of the WD2-dim-* family (16 + 13 + 27 + 13 + 19 + 19 = 107 pre-existing across foundation, bar, cat, rect, trend, point) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing) + WD2-wiring-echarts (23 pre-existing — onChartClick wiring untouched) all green. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Two-column dispatch + dim for hierarchical treemaps.** When `groupCh` is set, the parent ring carries `groupCh` values + the leaf ring carries `labelCh` values. WD2-wiring-echarts deliberately deferred parent-ring dispatch via the same carve-out (would need a two-column dispatch shape like RectRenderer's WD2-wiring-rest-rect). WD2-dim-echarts-treemap inherits the same restriction — leaves dim, parents don't. A future WD2-dim-echarts-treemap-parent wave (or a follow-on after the two-column dispatch lands) could extend.
    - **Color-saturation dim factor.** ECharts treemap levels carry `colorSaturation: [0.45, 0.85]` ranges. A dim factor that reduces saturation (rather than opacity) on non-matching leaves would visually integrate better with the color-saturation gradient the treemap already uses. Out of scope — opacity is the WD2-dim-* family's canonical mechanism for uniformity.
    - **WD2-dim-echarts-rest** (SankeyRenderer + CalendarRenderer + CandlestickRenderer). Sankey nodes dim on `sourceCh.field` (edges skipped per the WD2-wiring-echarts carve-out). Calendar per-cell dim on `dateCh.field` — the `[date, value]` tuple data array needs to be promoted to `{ value: [date, value], itemStyle: { opacity } }` objects so ECharts can read per-cell opacity from the data. Candlestick per-bar dim on `xCh.field` via parallel `itemStyle`-by-index array. Each ships as its own focused wave; bundling all three risks a fat ~250 LOC wave for a single test file.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-point · PointRenderer scatter dims per-point on `colorCh.field`.** Closes the WD2-dim-* family for every visx renderer with a categorical filter target. PointRenderer diverges from WD2-dim-trend's per-series shape: scatter marks are individually filter-targetable (the existing WD2-wiring-rest-point dispatch fires per-point on `p.rawColor` — each clicked dot toggles its color group), so the dim is per-point too. A point with a color group NOT in the active categorical cross-filter on `colorCh.field` fades to ~0.4 opacity; a point in the active selection stays at full opacity. Pure quantitative scatters (no color encoding) and chat / explorer surfaces have no categorical field to filter against; nothing to dim. The dim factor and the dispatch share the exact same applicability domain (`!!dashboardTile && !!colorCh`) so both opt-in together — a chart that has no colorCh stays click-inert AND dim-inert.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/PointRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/PointRenderer.tsx). `isCrossFilterActive` added to the crossFilter named-import alongside the already-present `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. Triplet lifted right after the existing `crossFilterReady` gate (intentionally co-located so dispatch + dim conditions stay discoverable as a pair):
      ```ts
      const dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters;
      const colorFilterSel = colorCh
        ? dashboardFilters?.[colorCh.field]
        : undefined;
      const dashboardDimActive =
        !!colorCh &&
        !!colorFilterSel &&
        colorFilterSel.type === "categorical" &&
        colorFilterSel.values.length > 0;
      ```
      The colorCh-truthy gate on the ternary keeps the access path safe in the pure-quantitative scatter case where `colorCh` is null — the ternary collapses to `undefined` and `dashboardDimActive` falls through to false without ever dereferencing `null.field`. Inside `points.map((p) => { ... })`, AFTER `cx` / `cy` lift but BEFORE the `if (shapeCh)` render branching, the per-point dim factor:
      ```ts
      const isDashboardDimmed =
        dashboardDimActive &&
        !isCrossFilterActive(
          dashboardFilters!,
          colorCh!.field,
          p.rawColor,
        );
      const dimMul = isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1;
      ```
      Both non-null assertions are safe because `dashboardDimActive` AND-gates on `!!colorCh`. Passing `p.rawColor` (not `p.colorKey`) is load-bearing for non-string color dims — Date / numeric / boolean values produce different strings via `asString` (used to build `colorKey`) versus `toFilterValue` (used by `isCrossFilterActive` internally), so matching against the raw form is the only correct comparison. `dimMul` is lifted once per point so the fill (`0.7 * op`) and the stroke (`op`) both consume the same factor on whichever branch renders — a dimmed fill with a non-dimmed ring would render as a faded dot with a stark outline. Both render branches mutate to multiply `dimMul`: the glyph `<path>` (shape-encoded scatter) gains `fillOpacity={0.7 * op * dimMul}` + `strokeOpacity={op * dimMul}`; the plain `<Circle>` (default scatter) takes the identical composition. The pre-wave `cursorStyle` + `onPointClick` + `onPointMove` + `onMouseLeave` are untouched — the dispatch path is exactly what WD2-wiring-rest-point shipped.
