    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimPoint.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimPoint.test.ts) (new, ~260 LOC). 19 tests across 7 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **Import shape** (1): `isCrossFilterActive` named-imported alongside `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue` in the crossFilter import block.
      - **Lifted triplet** (5): `dashboardFilters` read off `dashboardTile?.filters` once; `colorFilterSel` only when colorCh exists (ternary gate); `dashboardDimActive` carries the four-guard `!!colorCh && !!colorFilterSel && colorFilterSel.type === "categorical" && colorFilterSel.values.length > 0`; placement BEFORE `points.map` JSX body (lifts only once per render not per point); placement adjacent to `crossFilterReady` (≤ 1500 chars apart — proves dispatch and dim opt-in conditions live as a discoverable pair).
      - **Per-point isDashboardDimmed + dimMul** (4): AND-gate on `dashboardDimActive` + `!isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, colorCh!.field, p.rawColor)`; doesNotMatch pin against `toFilterValue(p.rawColor)` double-coercion regression (the helper coerces internally); `dimMul = isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1` lifted once per point; the 0.4 dim factor is the same value the rest of the WD2-dim-* family settled on; placement AFTER `cx` / `cy` but BEFORE the `if (shapeCh)` branching so both render paths see the same `dimMul`.
      - **Glyph `<path>` branch** (2): `fillOpacity={0.7 * op * dimMul}` (preserves baseline 0.7 + legend op); `strokeOpacity={op * dimMul}` (preserves legend op).
      - **Plain `<Circle>` branch** (3): identical fillOpacity + strokeOpacity composition; doesNotMatch pin against `isDashboardDimmed ? "hsl(var(--foreground))"` outline regression + `strokeWidth={isDashboardDimmed` — opacity-only contract is uniform across the WD2-dim-* family.
      - **Documentation comment** (1): the lifted-locals comment cites `WD2-dim-point` + names the per-point shape divergence from per-series trends (the words `per-point` and `individually filter-targetable` are pinned) so future Claude sees the shape choice called out explicitly rather than reading it as a divergence.
      - **Dispatch / dim applicability pair** (2): `crossFilterReady = !!dashboardTile && !!colorCh` literal retained (dispatch unchanged); dim and dispatch gates share `!!colorCh` as the load-bearing applicability pin.

  **Why this design.** Three shape choices were considered. (1) **Per-series dim**, mirroring WD2-dim-trend: aggregate points by colorKey and dim the whole color group when its rawColor isn't in the active filter. Rejected because scatter marks are NOT aggregated into a series-like primitive — each `<Circle>` / glyph `<path>` is rendered independently from a flat `points` array, so there's no series-level shape to dim once; the per-series approach would require duplicating the colorKey → matched? map across every point lookup anyway. (2) **Per-point dim with colorKey lookup** (instead of per-point `isCrossFilterActive` call): build a `Map<colorKey, boolean>` once per render mapping colorKey → "in active filter", then look up per point. Rejected because the cost of `isCrossFilterActive` is `O(values.length)` where `values.length` is typically ≤ 10 categorical values, and for a typical scatter (≤ 500 points), the total cost is ≤ 5 K membership tests — well under any rendering cost, and the implementation is two lines instead of a precomputed map. The lookup-map approach is worth revisiting only when a scatter renders 10 K+ points. (3) **Per-point isCrossFilterActive call** (chosen): inline the per-point check inside `points.map`, multiply opacity by `dimMul`. Identical surface across both render branches (glyph + plain Circle) without a precomputation phase. The `dimMul` lift per point — rather than per render — is the second design choice: the alternative (compute `isDashboardDimmed` separately for fill and stroke) would couple two opacity expressions that must always agree to stay visually coherent (the faded-fill / stark-ring failure mode). Centralising via `dimMul` is the load-bearing single-source-of-truth pattern that prevents a future "I'll just tune the fill" edit from silently desynchronising the ring opacity. This mirrors the WD2-dim-area `dimMul`-shared-between-fill-and-stroke pattern at the per-iteration level (area dims once per series; point dims once per point). The opacity-only contract (no outline for matching marks) is the third design choice: WD2-dim-bar / -cat / -rect / -trend all settled on opacity-only because outlining matched marks on every tile of a multi-tile dashboard would be visually noisy. Preserving the uniform contract across renderers means the 0.4 dim factor (and any future visual-design wave that tweaks it) propagates with a single per-renderer touch instead of per-mark-type overrides.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-point (19 new in `wd2DimPoint.test.ts`) + the rest of the WD2-dim-* family (16 + 13 + 27 + 13 + 19 = 88 pre-existing across foundation, bar, cat, rect, trend) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing) + WD2-wiring-rest-point (13 pre-existing — per-point dispatch wiring untouched) all green. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Per-shape dim differentiation.** The shape encoding (`encoding.shape`) renders glyph paths with shape-distinct geometry (circle / square / triangle / diamond / …). WD2-dim-point dims fill + stroke uniformly across all shapes; a per-shape variation (e.g. preserve diamond strokes at full opacity because diamonds are intrinsically less visible at small sizes) was considered and rejected because the shape encoding is independent from the color encoding — a point's filter-membership has no semantic relationship to its glyph shape, so the dim shouldn't vary by shape.
    - **Per-bubble (size encoding) dim adjustment.** Bubble charts use the `size` encoding to map quantitative values to glyph radius (`SIZE_RANGE = [3, 22]`). A larger bubble dimmed at 0.4 is still more visible than a smaller bubble at full opacity, but rebalancing the dim factor against bubble area would couple two unrelated encodings. Out of scope.
    - **Per-shape (shape encoding) dim factor differentiation against the colorCh dim.** A point can simultaneously be shape-encoded AND color-encoded (two-dim scatter). WD2-dim-point dims only on the color dimension because the dispatch (WD2-wiring-rest-point) only fires on `colorCh.field` — there's no shape-field dispatch yet, so there's nothing to dim against. A future WD2-dim-point-shape wave could add a `shapeCh.field` membership check if the shape dimension ever gains a dispatch path.
    - **WD2-dim-echarts** (5 ECharts marks: Treemap / Sunburst / Sankey / Calendar / Candlestick). Different mechanism — ECharts mounts its own canvas instance and the dim factor must be expressed as `itemStyle.opacity` per dataItem at the `buildOptions(echarts, theme)` level rather than as a post-render fillOpacity prop. Touches `TreemapRenderer.tsx`'s tree memo + `SpecialtyRenderers.tsx`'s per-renderer series builders. The renderer's `useDashboardTileContext()` read + `dashboardDimActive` lifting can live inside each renderer body; the question is how to thread filters into the (currently field-only) series builders without leaking the dashboard concern across the buildOptions call. Ships as a follow-on wave (possibly split per renderer if the surface area warrants).
    - **The 4 remaining visx renderers (KPI / Radar / Regression / pure-quantitative-scatter).** Same skip list as WD2-wiring-rest-point: KPI is a single-value scalar (no categorical mark); Radar's polar dim semantics would need a separate design (a dim that fades a single radar polygon out of two would break the structural shape comparison); Regression's line is a fit, not a categorical mark; pure-quantitative-scatter has no colorCh (WD2-dim-point's gate already returns "no dim" for these).

 Trend renderers have continuous-x marks — lines and stacked areas — so the WD2-dim-* family's per-mark dim shape (BarRenderer + categorical pack + rect) doesn't apply: there's no per-point categorical brush target a continuous trend can dim against. The natural dim concept is per-SERIES: when an active categorical cross-filter on `colorCh.field` doesn't include a series's rawColor, the series's stroke / fill opacities multiply by 0.4. The gate (`!!colorCh`) follows the WD2-wiring-rest-point colorCh-gating precedent — single-series trends have no color field to filter against, so the dim factor never fires.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx). `isCrossFilterActive` added to the crossFilter import. `Series` interface extended with `rawColor?: unknown` (preserved alongside the stringified `key` so the dim check can call `isCrossFilterActive` with the same shape WD2 cross-filter events recorded — without rawColor preservation, the stringified key would miss for non-string color dims because `asString(Date)` and `toFilterValue(Date)` produce different strings, same for numbers / booleans via subtle Number coercion paths). The colorCh group builder refactored from per-row `groups.get(k) ?? []` + push into a `Map<string, { points: SeriesPoint[]; rawColor: unknown }>` so the first occurrence of each color key captures rawColor before subsequent points get appended; the return-projection threads `rawColor: agg.rawColor` onto each Series. Lifted triplet right after `useDashboardTileContext()`:
      ```ts
      const dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters;
      const colorFilterSel = colorCh
        ? dashboardFilters?.[colorCh.field]
        : undefined;
      const dashboardDimActive =
        !!colorCh &&
        !!colorFilterSel &&
        colorFilterSel.type === "categorical" &&
        colorFilterSel.values.length > 0;
      ```
      The colorCh truthy gate is load-bearing — without it the optional chain on `dashboardFilters?.[colorCh.field]` would throw on a null colorCh access. Inside the per-series `<LinePath>` render loop (line ~616), `isDashboardDimmed = dashboardDimActive && !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, colorCh!.field, s.rawColor)`. The non-null assertions on `dashboardFilters` and `colorCh` are safe because `dashboardDimActive` AND-gates both. The `<LinePath>` strokeOpacity composes `op * (isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)` — the existing `op = seriesOpacity(s.key, legend.state)` (per-series legend opacity factor: 1 normally, 0 when legend-hidden) stays intact so a legend-hidden series at `op === 0` still renders nothing and a legend-visible dimmed series renders at 0.4.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/AreaRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/AreaRenderer.tsx). Same Series-extension + group-builder refactor as LineRenderer (the two files have parallel shapes for the colorCh group builder by design). Lifted triplet matches. The render loop diverges in one place: each area-render iteration emits BOTH an `<AreaClosed>` filled area AND a bordering `<LinePath>` stroke. A dimmed fill with a non-dimmed border would render as a faded area with a stark outline — visually incoherent. WD2-dim-trend lifts a single `dimMul = isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1` per iteration and consumes it in both: `<AreaClosed fillOpacity={0.55 * op * dimMul}>` + `<LinePath strokeOpacity={op * dimMul}>`. The `stacked` memo (which projects each series through a unified x domain to make stacked areas additive) preserves rawColor via spread (`out.push({ ...s, points: stackedPoints })`) — no per-series field-by-field re-projection needed.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimTrend.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimTrend.test.ts) (new, ~200 LOC). 19 tests across 5 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **LineRenderer imports + Series shape** (4): `isCrossFilterActive` named-imported; `Series` carries `rawColor?: unknown`; colorCh group builder preserves the type-original value; `Array.from(groups.entries()).map` threads `rawColor: agg.rawColor` through the projection.
      - **LineRenderer per-series dim** (3): lifted triplet with colorCh gate; per-series `isDashboardDimmed` checks `isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, colorCh!.field, s.rawColor)`; LinePath strokeOpacity composes `op * (isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)`.
      - **AreaRenderer imports + Series shape** (4): mirrors LineRenderer's set on AreaRenderer source.
      - **AreaRenderer per-series dim** (5): lifted triplet; per-series isDashboardDimmed; `dimMul` shared local; `<AreaClosed fillOpacity={0.55 * op * dimMul}>` preserved baseline; `<LinePath strokeOpacity={op * dimMul}>`; stacked memo preserves rawColor via spread.
      - **Cross-cutting colorCh gating** (2): both renderers' `dashboardDimActive` AND-gate on `!!colorCh` so single-series trends skip dim entirely (and the `colorCh!.field` non-null assertion inside the map is type-safe).

  **Why this design.** The single biggest design choice was the per-series shape (not per-point or per-segment). Three alternatives existed. (1) **Per-point dim**: dim individual points along a series when their x value isn't in an active x-filter. Rejected because trend x-axes are typically numeric / temporal — there's no categorical x to filter against, and an x-filter on a numeric axis is a range, not a discrete value, so per-point membership doesn't apply. (2) **Per-segment dim**: split each line into segments and dim segments crossing non-matching x ranges. Rejected because it requires re-projecting the per-point data into per-segment data each render, adds rendering complexity, and produces a visually jarring "broken line" effect that doesn't communicate "this series is filtered" — it communicates "this series has gaps". (3) **Per-series dim** (chosen): treat the whole trend as one mark, dim it as a unit when its color group isn't in the active filter. Reads as "this trend is faded because it's not in the current filter selection" — matches the bar / cat / rect dim semantics where each mark is independently dimmed. The AreaRenderer's `dimMul`-shared-between-fill-and-stroke pattern is the second design choice: the alternative (compute `isDashboardDimmed` twice per series, once for fill once for stroke) would be cleaner from a co-locality standpoint but couples two opacity expressions that must always agree. Centralising via `dimMul` is the load-bearing single-source-of-truth pattern that prevents a future "I'll just tune the fill opacity" edit from breaking the visual coherence by accident.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-trend (19 new in `wd2DimTrend.test.ts`) + the rest of the WD2-dim-* family (16 + 13 + 27 + 13 = 69 pre-existing across foundation, bar, cat, rect) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing) + WD2-wiring-rest-trend (18 pre-existing — nearest-x dispatch wiring untouched) all green. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Per-point markers on the line.** Line renderers can render per-point markers (circles at each data point). Those weren't dimmed in this wave because they share the series stroke / fill and would inherit any series-level dim transparently if they're nested inside the same `<Group>`. The current LineRenderer does NOT render per-point markers on the primary series path, so no test pins their dim factor — if a future visual-design wave adds them, this dim shape needs to extend.
    - **Comparison overlay dim.** The WC5.6 prior-period faded comparison line at line ~588 already has its own `0.32 * op` strokeOpacity factor. WD2-dim-trend doesn't extend it because the comparison overlay is an analytical artifact, not the primary series — dimming it again when its parent series is dimmed would compound to 0.13 (essentially invisible). Pinned by absence-of-isDashboardDimmed-in-the-comparison-render-path test if a future wave wants to wire it.
    - **WD2-dim-point** (PointRenderer scatter). Same per-color-group shape; ships as its own atomic because the scatter mark is per-point (the dim membership is checked per point against `colorCh.field`, not aggregated to per-series).
    - **WD2-dim-echarts** (5 ECharts marks). `itemStyle.opacity` per dataItem at the `buildOptions(echarts, theme)` level. Different mechanism from the visx fill/stroke opacity post-render mutation.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-rect · RectRenderer heatmap dims via OR-of-row-OR-col.** Closes the heatmap on the WD2-dim-* family. Heatmap cells sit at the intersection of two categorical dimensions (`rowCh` × `colCh`), so the dim contract diverges in shape from every other renderer the dim family has touched so far: WD2-dim-bar / -cat all check a single x-field's filter; WD2-dim-rect checks both `rowCh.field` and `colCh.field` and the cell is dimmed if EITHER filter excludes its raw value. This is intentionally NOT symmetric with WD2-wiring-rest-rect's two-dim dispatch shape (which fires BOTH row + col CROSS_FILTER_EVENT events on click, AND-style) — the dispatch and dim sides of a heatmap interaction model two different mental shifts. On click, the user explicitly chose a (row, col) intersection, so they want both filters applied. On dim, the user is reading "which cells survive the filter intersection?", so the natural answer is to keep only cells passing BOTH the row and col filters, which means dimming if either fails. The AND-of-passing-filters is equivalent to OR-of-failing-filters via De Morgan, but expressing it as `isRowDimmed || isColDimmed` reads more directly off the per-cell context (the cell knows it has a row + col; each can independently fail).

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/RectRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/RectRenderer.tsx). `isCrossFilterActive` added to the crossFilter named-import alongside `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. Two independent lifted triplets right after `useDashboardTileContext()`:
      ```ts
      const dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters;
      const rowFilterSel = dashboardFilters?.[rowCh.field];
      const colFilterSel = dashboardFilters?.[colCh.field];
      const dashboardRowDimActive =
        !!rowFilterSel &&
        rowFilterSel.type === "categorical" &&
        rowFilterSel.values.length > 0;
      const dashboardColDimActive =
        !!colFilterSel &&
        colFilterSel.type === "categorical" &&
        colFilterSel.values.length > 0;
      ```
      Two independent flags (not a combined `dashboardDimActive`) so the OR-of-row-OR-col contract behaves correctly across the three filter cases: row-only filter dims along rows only (col flag is false → `isColDimmed` always false → only `isRowDimmed` decides); col-only filter dims along cols only; row+col filter intersects via OR (a cell fails if either filter excludes it). Inside the per-cell `.map(...)` body:
      ```ts
      const isRowDimmed =
        dashboardRowDimActive &&
        !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, rowCh.field, rowRawByKey.get(row));
      const isColDimmed =
        dashboardColDimActive &&
        !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, colCh.field, colRawByKey.get(col));
      const isDashboardDimmed = isRowDimmed || isColDimmed;
      ```
      Both `isRowDimmed` / `isColDimmed` use `rowRawByKey.get(row)` / `colRawByKey.get(col)` — the raw-value maps WD2-wiring-rest-rect already built so the dispatch could carry type-original Date / number / boolean values. Comparing stringified row / col keys against the cross-filter's raw values would always miss for non-string dims (a Date row + a Date filter would never match because Date stringification rounds-trips differently across the click → toggle → dim path). The cell `<rect>` gains `fillOpacity={isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1}` — no prior baseline (heatmap cells were full opacity for visibility against the sequential color scale), so the matched-cell default of 1 preserves the pre-WD2-dim render. The 0.5-px background stroke + the title tooltip stay untouched: they're structural grid geometry + the cell's quantitative tooltip readout, not the filterable mark itself.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimRect.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimRect.test.ts) (new, ~160 LOC). 13 tests across 6 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **Import shape** (1): `isCrossFilterActive` named-imported.
      - **Two-dim lifted locals** (3): `dashboardFilters` lifted once; `rowFilterSel` + `colFilterSel` read separately on `rowCh.field` / `colCh.field`; `dashboardRowDimActive` + `dashboardColDimActive` both carry the full triple-guard (categorical + non-empty).
      - **Per-cell OR logic** (4): `isRowDimmed` shape; `isColDimmed` shape; the OR composition `isDashboardDimmed = isRowDimmed || isColDimmed`; pin against stringified row/col regression (a doesNotMatch on `isCrossFilterActive(..., rowCh.field, row,` proves the test uses the raw lookup, not the bare key).
      - **fillOpacity binding** (2): `<rect>` renders `fillOpacity={isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1}`; stroke / strokeWidth are NOT predicated on `isDashboardDimmed` (heatmap grid lines stay structural).
      - **Lifted-locals placement** (1): both `dashboardRowDimActive` + `dashboardColDimActive` appear BEFORE the per-cell `<rect>` rendering.
      - **Documentation comment** (2): the lifted-locals comment names `OR-of-row-OR-col` and the symmetric pairing with the WD2-wiring-rest-rect `two-dim DISPATCH` so future Claude sees the AND-dispatch / OR-dim asymmetry called out explicitly rather than reading it as a divergence.

  **Why this design.** The shape choice (`OR-of-row-OR-col`) was the load-bearing decision. Three alternatives were considered. (1) **AND-of-row-AND-col**: a cell is dimmed only if BOTH row + col filters exclude it. Rejected because a cell with a passing row + failing col would render at full opacity, suggesting it survives a filter it doesn't — visually misleading. (2) **Row-priority**: dim by row only when a row filter is active; ignore col filters for dim. Rejected because it makes col filters dim-invisible on heatmaps (they'd still dispatch + dim other tiles, just not this one). (3) **Per-row "any col passes" / per-col "any row passes"**: dim a row of cells if no col in the row passes the col filter. Rejected because it requires precomputing per-row + per-col survival maps (O(R × C) ops per render) and produces a structurally different visual than the cell-level OR — the entire row dims as a block rather than per-cell. The OR-of-row-OR-col gives the cleanest mental model: a cell passes the filter intersection iff it passes BOTH dims; a cell that fails either dim should fade. The two-flag pattern (not a combined `dashboardDimActive`) was preferred over a single OR-ed flag because the three filter cases (row-only, col-only, row+col) each want different per-cell logic, and inlining the AND into a single `dashboardDimActive` would re-create the work per cell rather than amortising it. Alternative considered: precompute a per-row + per-col bool array indicating "does this row/col pass its filter?" and look those up in the cell map. Rejected for simplicity — the per-cell `isCrossFilterActive` call is O(values.length) which in practice is ≤ 10 categorical values, so the cumulative cost on a 20×20 heatmap is ≤ 4 K ops, well under any rendering cost. Worth revisiting if a heatmap with 1000-cell renderings starts paging.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-rect (13 new in `wd2DimRect.test.ts`) + the rest of the WD2-dim-* family (16 + 13 + 27 = 56 pre-existing across foundation, bar, cat) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing) + WD2-wiring-rest-rect (11 pre-existing — two-dim dispatch wiring untouched) all green. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical to pre-WD2-dim-foundation baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Combined dispatch + dim tile-source attribution.** If the brushed source tile happens to be a heatmap (rare but possible — the brushed tile's own (row, col) pair survives the filter intersection so its single brushed cell stays full opacity, every other cell dims), the user sees a clean self-isolation. No additional source-tile guard is needed because the OR contract already handles this correctly.
    - **Heatmap stroke dim.** The 0.5-px background stroke could dim too for a more uniform fade, but it's structural grid signaling rather than data — keeping it visible across dimmed cells preserves the heatmap's readability as a grid. Pinned by test that strokeWidth + stroke aren't predicated on `isDashboardDimmed`.
    - **WD2-dim-trend** (Line + Area). Continuous-x trends. Dim shape diverges further — per-series dim when an active `colorCh.field` filter doesn't include the series (no per-point dim because the x-axis is continuous, not categorical). Ships as its own atomic.
    - **WD2-dim-point** (PointRenderer scatter). Conditional on `colorCh`. Same per-series-by-color pattern as the trend wave.
    - **WD2-dim-echarts** (5 ECharts marks). `itemStyle.opacity` per dataItem at the `buildOptions` level. Different mechanism from the visx fillOpacity post-render mutation.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-cat · 5 categorical visx renderers dim non-matching marks (Arc / Funnel / Box / Waterfall / Combo).** Fans WD2-dim-bar to the categorical-by-construction renderer pack the WD2-wiring-rest-cat wave wired earlier. Each renderer has a categorical primary x-field (the dispatch column from WD2-wiring-rest-cat) and a mark that maps 1-to-1 to one categorical value — slices for Arc, stage rects for Funnel, box rects for Box, contribution bars for Waterfall, primary-axis bars for Combo. The WD2-dim-bar template (lift the categorical-selection lookup once per render; compute per-mark `isDashboardDimmed = dashboardDimActive && !isCrossFilterActive(...)`; multiply the mark's existing `fillOpacity` baseline by 0.4 when dimmed) applies uniformly, with two per-renderer carve-outs that mirror the WD2-wiring-rest-cat dispatch carve-outs: Waterfall's running-total bars never dim (synthetic summary rows, not categorical marks the user can filter to), and Combo's secondary-axis line never dims (continuous trend; categorical dim would render as a gappy interleave that breaks the line's visual coherence).

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ArcRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ArcRenderer.tsx). `isCrossFilterActive` added to the crossFilter import; lifted `dashboardFilters / xFilterSel / dashboardDimActive` triplet on `labelCh.field` right after `useDashboardTileContext()`. Inside `pie.arcs.map`, `isDashboardDimmed = dashboardDimActive && !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, labelCh.field, arc.data.rawKey)`. Slice `<path>` gains `fillOpacity={isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1}` (no prior baseline; matched slices stay at 1).
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/FunnelRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/FunnelRenderer.tsx). Lifted on `enc.x.field`; per-stage `isDashboardDimmed` checks `s.rawLabel`. Stage `<rect>` fillOpacity composes `0.85 * (isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)` — preserves the existing 0.85 baseline that visually distinguishes the funnel's translucent funnel-walls geometry from a solid pie.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BoxRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BoxRenderer.tsx). Lifted on `enc.x.field`; per-box `isDashboardDimmed` checks `s.rawCategory`. Box `<rect>` fillOpacity composes `0.4 * (isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)` — preserves the existing 0.4 baseline (box rects are deliberately translucent so the user can see the underlying IQR overlap). Whiskers, the median line, and the box stroke stay full opacity — they're structural geometry the user needs to read the distribution shape, not the filterable mark, and dimming them would hide the IQR / range information for non-matching categories that the user might still want to compare visually.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/WaterfallRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/WaterfallRenderer.tsx). Lifted on `enc.x.field`; per-bar `isDashboardDimmed = dashboardDimActive && !b.isTotal && !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, enc.x.field, b.rawCategory)`. The `!b.isTotal` AND-gate is symmetric with the WD2-wiring-rest-cat dispatch gate (`clickable = dashboardTile && !b.isTotal`) — running-total bars are synthetic summary rows, not categorical marks, so neither click nor dim treats them as filterable. Bar `fillOpacity` composes `0.85 * (isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)`.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ComboRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ComboRenderer.tsx). Lifted on `xCh.field`; per-bar `isDashboardDimmed` checks `rawX` (the type-original x value preserved alongside the band-scale lookup string). Bar `fillOpacity` composes `0.85 * (isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)`. The secondary-axis `<LinePath>` stays at full opacity AND click-inert — the WD2-wiring-rest-cat invariant is that the bar mark is the categorical click target and the line stays inert; WD2-dim-cat preserves that separation. The docstring comment explicitly names why: a continuous line dimmed by a categorical filter would render as a visually broken sequence (each path segment crosses categorical boundaries, so half a segment would be at 0.4 and half at 1, producing a gappy interleave).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimCat.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimCat.test.ts) (new, ~290 LOC). 27 tests across 6 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Each per-renderer suite pins (a) `isCrossFilterActive` import, (b) lifted-locals triplet on the renderer-specific x-field, (c) per-mark `isDashboardDimmed` expression with the renderer-specific raw value, (d) fillOpacity composition shape (including the per-renderer baseline 0.85 / 0.4 / 1). Two renderer-specific carve-outs pinned in their own tests: Waterfall's `!b.isTotal` AND-gate (running totals stay full opacity), and Combo's `<LinePath>` not wiring `isDashboardDimmed` anywhere in its body. A cross-cutting suite pins that the lifted locals live ABOVE each renderer's per-mark `.map(...)` so the categorical-selection lookup runs once per render not per mark.

  **Why this design.** The fan-out was deliberately one atomic wave rather than five separate per-renderer waves for three reasons. First: **the dim factor logic is mechanical once WD2-dim-bar established the template**. Each renderer is a ~10–15 LOC edit (one import widening + the lifted triplet + the per-mark guard + the fillOpacity composition) and the variation point per renderer is purely (a) the x-field expression name and (b) the raw-value identifier — both of which the WD2-wiring-rest-cat dispatch site already records, so no new naming was introduced. Second: **the carve-outs (Waterfall totals, Combo line) are coupled to the dispatch carve-outs from WD2-wiring-rest-cat** — landing them in the same wave keeps the dim/dispatch parallel visible in a single diff, so a future reader doesn't have to git-blame to find why the totals + line stay full opacity. Third: **per-renderer waves would have shipped a ~10 LOC code change against a ~80 LOC test file each**, the test-to-code ratio inflates without buying any atomicity since none of the renderers depend on each other. Splitting later (say, when an Arc-only refactor lands) is easy; bundling now keeps the doc footprint compact. Alternative considered: a shared `useDashboardDimFactor(xField: string)` hook returning `(rawValue: unknown) => 0.4 | 1`. Rejected because (a) hooks must be called at component-body top-level not inside the per-mark map, so the hook would still need to return a closure each renderer captures (no real ergonomic win); (b) the lifted-locals pattern is 6 lines of code per renderer — abstracting it would save 30 LOC total across five renderers at the cost of indirection. Defer until at least 3 more renderer waves need the same shape.

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-cat (27 new in `wd2DimCat.test.ts`) + WD2-dim-bar (16 pre-existing) + WD2-dim-foundation (13 pre-existing) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing — `isCrossFilterActive` signature widening is transparent) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing) + WD2-wiring-rest-cat (36 pre-existing — dispatch wiring untouched) all green. Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical to pre-WD2-dim-foundation baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical to pre-WD2-dim-foundation baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Pie label dimming.** Arc slices' inside-slice `<text>` labels stay full opacity. The labels are small (only render at ≥5% slice share) and dimming them with the slice would compound to 0.16 opacity on a 0.4-dimmed slice — visually invisible. Deferred to a future wave if there's user feedback that dimmed slices' labels feel jarring.
    - **WD2-dim-rect** (RectRenderer heatmap, two-dim dim). The heatmap cell sits at the intersection of `rowCh` + `colCh` so the dim contract is OR-of-row-OR-col, not the single-dim shape this wave uses. Pairs naturally with the WD2-wiring-rest-rect two-dim dispatch shape but ships as its own atomic.
    - **WD2-dim-trend** (Line + Area). Continuous-x renderers need a different dim shape — typically per-series dim when a `colorCh.field` filter is active, not per-x dim on the trend axis (a trend with a numerical x-axis has no categorical x to dim against). Ships as its own atomic.
    - **WD2-dim-point** (PointRenderer scatter). Conditional on `colorCh` (same gating as WD2-wiring-rest-point's dispatch). Ships as its own atomic.
    - **WD2-dim-echarts** (5 ECharts marks). ECharts dim is via `itemStyle.opacity` per dataItem or `select` / `emphasis` mechanisms inside `buildOptions(echarts, theme)`, not a post-render mutation of a visx fillOpacity. The build-level mechanic diverges enough from the visx pattern to warrant its own wave.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-bar · BarRenderer dims non-matching bars under an active dashboard cross-filter.** First renderer wave on the WD2-dim-* family. WD2-dim-foundation (earlier today) extended [`dashboardTileContext`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.tsx) with an optional `filters?: ActiveChartFilters` slot so renderers can read the active dashboard-wide cross-filter via `useDashboardTileContext()`; WD2-dim-bar is the first consumer of that slot. The visual feedback gap WD2-dim-* closes is the "filtered tiles dim non-matching marks instead of removing them" UX from the [1000x master plan](/Users/tida/.claude/plans/go-through-the-entire-partitioned-yao.md) Workstream 4 brief: pre-WD2-dim, clicking a bar on Tile A dispatched `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT`, `DashboardView` toggled `globalFilters`, and Tile B *removed* every row whose value wasn't in the active selection. That's hostile to the user's mental model of "I want to see what the brushed value looks like across every tile" — disappearing bars feel like data loss rather than scope-narrowing. WD2-dim-bar replaces "remove" with "dim to 0.4 opacity" on the bar mark.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx). One import widened (`isCrossFilterActive` added to the named-import from `@/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter` alongside `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue` from WD2-wiring-bar). Three locals lifted once per render right after the existing `useDashboardTileContext()` call:
      ```ts
      const dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters;
      const xFilterSel = dashboardFilters?.[enc.x.field];
      const dashboardDimActive =
        !!xFilterSel &&
        xFilterSel.type === "categorical" &&
        xFilterSel.values.length > 0;
      ```
      The triple guard (`selection exists` + `categorical` + `values.length > 0`) is load-bearing for three different empty-state edges: (a) `dashboardFilters` could be `undefined` outside a dashboard tile, so the optional chain falls through cleanly; (b) the user might have a date or numeric range filter on the x-field (`type !== "categorical"`) — cross-filter dim is explicitly a discrete-value concern; (c) the user might have just toggled the last categorical value off — `values.length === 0` is a legitimate empty selection that should revert every bar to full opacity, not dim everything. Inside the `cells.map` body, a new per-bar local computes membership:
      ```ts
      const isDashboardDimmed =
        dashboardDimActive &&
        !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, enc.x.field, c.outerRaw);
      ```
      The non-null assertion is safe because `dashboardDimActive` is true only when `xFilterSel` is non-null, which means `dashboardFilters` is non-null. The `fillOpacity` ternary extends from `(isFiltered ? 1 : grid.inGrid && grid.filter ? 0.4 : 1)` to `(isFiltered ? 1 : grid.inGrid && grid.filter ? 0.4 : isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)` — the chat/explorer (`grid.inGrid`) branch stays first because `grid.inGrid` and `dashboardTile` are mutually exclusive contexts (the WD2-wiring-bar foundation already enforces that), so the new branch only fires when the chat/explorer one doesn't. No outline / stroke is added for dashboard-matching bars (the existing `isFiltered` stroke is chat/explorer-only) — on a multi-tile dashboard where multiple tiles render the matched value at the same time, outlining everywhere would be visually noisy.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts). `isCrossFilterActive(global, column, value)` signature widened from `value: string | number | boolean | null | undefined` to `value: unknown`. The function body already passes `value` to `toFilterValue(value)` which accepts `unknown` (per the WD2-wiring-bar widening), so the signature narrowing was the only narrowing point — widening it to match lets renderers pass `BarCell.outerRaw` (typed `unknown`) without a narrowing cast. Doc-comment extended to name the precedent so a future refactor doesn't narrow it back. The existing 29 `crossFilter.test.ts` assertions stay green: every test passes values that are assignable to `unknown` (the wider type).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimBar.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimBar.test.ts) (new, ~170 LOC). 16 tests across 6 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **Import shape** (1): `isCrossFilterActive` named-imported alongside `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`.
      - **Lifted locals + render-time placement** (4): `const dashboardFilters = dashboardTile?.filters;`; `const xFilterSel = dashboardFilters?.[enc.x.field];`; the triple-guard expression on `dashboardDimActive` (pinned exactly); structural pin that the lifted locals live ABOVE the `cells.map` JSX so the categorical-selection lookup runs once per render not per bar.
      - **Per-bar gate** (2): `isDashboardDimmed` is `dashboardDimActive && !isCrossFilterActive(dashboardFilters!, enc.x.field, c.outerRaw)`; `c.outerRaw` is passed directly without an intermediate `toFilterValue(...)` wrap (pin against double-coercion refactors). The second test reads forward 200 chars from the FIRST `isCrossFilterActive(` call site (the second `c.outerRaw` appears in the unrelated dispatchCrossFilter site at line ~744, so a global doesNotMatch would false-positive).
      - **fillOpacity branches** (3): the full ternary shape `(isFiltered ? 1 : grid.inGrid && grid.filter ? 0.4 : isDashboardDimmed ? 0.4 : 1)`; the dim factor is 0.4 (matches the chat/explorer dim factor); no `stroke="hsl(var(--foreground))"` and no `strokeWidth=` predicated on `isDashboardDimmed` (opacity-only).
      - **isCrossFilterActive widening** (3): `value: unknown` in the signature; body still calls `toFilterValue(value)`; doc-comment names the WD2-wiring-bar precedent.
      - **Documentation comment** (1): the lifted-locals doc-comment names the chat/explorer `grid.filter` parallel and the mutual exclusion so future Claude doesn't try to consolidate them.

  **Why this design.** The fundamental shape choice — "dim non-matching at 0.4 vs. remove" — was set by the master plan and not re-litigated. The three local-shape choices are worth pinning. First: **lift the categorical-selection lookup once per render** instead of doing it per bar. A typical bar chart on a dashboard has 6–20 bars; doing 6–20 `dashboardFilters[enc.x.field]` lookups + `.type === "categorical"` checks per render is a wasteful 12–60 property accesses per render, all returning the same answer. The lifted const captures the answer once. Second: **non-null assertion `dashboardFilters!` inside `isCrossFilterActive(...)`**, rather than a separate `if (!dashboardFilters) return false;` early-return. The non-null assertion is type-system-only — at runtime `dashboardFilters` is non-null whenever `dashboardDimActive` is true (the latter is the AND of `!!xFilterSel` and two facts about `xFilterSel`, and `xFilterSel` can only be truthy if `dashboardFilters` was non-null). Adding an early return would have the same runtime behaviour but a slightly slower hot path (one extra branch). Third: **widen `isCrossFilterActive` instead of casting at the call site**. Both options work; widening is preferred because (a) `toFilterValue` is already widened and (b) the narrower signature was the only narrowing point in the helper's path. Future renderer dim waves (WD2-dim-cat / -rect / -trend / -point / -echarts) will all want to pass `unknown`-typed raw values; widening once here means none of them carry an awkward cast. Alternative considered: pre-coerce the bar's `outerRaw` to a string outside the loop and compare against `xFilterSel.values` directly. Rejected because `isCrossFilterActive` is the canonical predicate — having two parallel implementations of "is this value in the selection?" would drift over time (especially for null / Date handling).

  **Tests.** Server test suite: WD2-dim-bar (16 new in `wd2DimBar.test.ts`) + crossFilter (29 pre-existing — `isCrossFilterActive` widening is transparent to existing call shapes) + dashboardTileContext (16 pre-existing post-WD2-dim-foundation) + wd2DimFoundation (13 pre-existing) all green (72 across the four suites). Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical to pre-WD2-dim-foundation baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical to pre-WD2-dim-foundation baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Other renderers.** WD2-dim-bar is the first renderer wave; WD2-dim-cat (Arc/Funnel/Box/Waterfall/Combo), WD2-dim-rect (heatmap, needs two-dim filter check since cells sit at row×col), WD2-dim-trend (Line+Area, dim points that don't match the current x-axis filter), WD2-dim-point (scatter, dim color groups that aren't in the active filter set), and WD2-dim-echarts (the 5 ECharts marks via `itemStyle.opacity` per dataItem or `select/emphasis` at the `buildOptions` level) all follow the same template but each has at least one renderer-specific call.
    - **Configurable dim factor.** A user-tweakable `0.4 → 0.3` opacity multiplier could ship as a theme token in a future visual-design wave. Pinned in the test at 0.4 for now; the value is symmetric with the chat/explorer dim case.
    - **Outline / glow on matched bars.** As above — opacity-only because outlining matched bars across every dashboard tile would be visually noisy. A future wave could add a subtle outline at the brushed-tile level (sourceTileId === this tile's id) but that's a different UX concept.
    - **Dim factor on the secondary-axis line in ComboRenderer.** Combo's bar mark is the categorical click target (per WD2-wiring-rest-cat); the line stays click-inert and the dim factor follows the same separation — bars dim, line doesn't. To be confirmed in the WD2-dim-cat wave.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-dim-foundation · `dashboardTileContext` carries optional `filters` for the upcoming dim-non-matching-marks family.** The WD2-wiring family (10 visx renderers + 5 ECharts renderers, finalised earlier today by WD2-wiring-echarts) closed the *input* half of the dashboard cross-filter loop: clicking a mark dispatches `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT`, `DashboardView` applies the toggle, and the dashboard-wide filter map updates. The *visual feedback* half — "filtered tiles dim non-matching marks instead of removing them" per the [1000x master plan](/Users/tida/.claude/plans/go-through-the-entire-partitioned-yao.md) Workstream 4 UX — has been blocked by a structural mismatch: each renderer needs to read the active filter for its `enc.x.field` (or equivalent encoding field) so it can call the already-shipped [`isCrossFilterActive(global, column, value)`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts) helper and decide if the mark it's about to render matches. But the `useDashboardTileContext()` hook only exposes `{ tileId }`, so renderers had no `ActiveChartFilters` map to call the helper against. The pre-WD2-dim options were (a) thread a new `filters` prop through every renderer's call site — a wide-blast-radius change on a god-object-adjacent ChartRenderer surface; (b) read `globalFilters` off a dashboard React context — there isn't one; the filter map lives in `DashboardView`'s `useState` and is forwarded as a prop; or (c) extend the existing `dashboardTileContext` (already mounted at the chart-tile boundary, already read by every wired renderer) with an optional filters slot — single touch point, single import. This wave ships option (c).

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.tsx). `DashboardTileContextValue` gains `filters?: ActiveChartFilters` (the same `ActiveChartFilters` map already in [`client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts`](../client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts); type-only import so the runtime bundle is untouched — dashboardTileContext is mounted on every dashboard tile and changes to its bundle ripple through SplitView code-splitting). `DashboardTileProviderProps` gains a matching optional `filters?: ActiveChartFilters` prop. The `useMemo` body spreads `filters` conditionally: `() => ({ tileId, ...(filters !== undefined ? { filters } : {}) })` so callers that omit filters (tests, legacy mounts) get a value byte-identical to the pre-wave shape — important because upcoming dim-renderer guards can rely on `value.filters !== undefined` as a "dashboard-side context" sentinel rather than threading a second context. Dependency array becomes `[tileId, filters]` so a `DashboardView` re-render that changes `globalFilters` propagates a fresh value down through every tile. The default context value remains `null` (pre-existing invariant for chat / explorer / share-preview surfaces where there's no tile wiring).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.tsx). Two-character JSX edit: `<DashboardTileProvider tileId={tile.id}>` → `<DashboardTileProvider tileId={tile.id} filters={filters}>`. The `filters: ActiveChartFilters | undefined` prop has been on `ChartTileBody` since WI2-wire-bind (it's already passed to `ChartTilePivotView` and the legacy `ChartRenderer`), so the forward is just consuming an existing prop in one more place — no new prop on `ChartTileBody` itself.
    - File header on `dashboardTileContext.tsx` extended to name *why* the field grew — the WD2-dim-* follow-on family (bar / cat / rect / trend / point / echarts), the `isCrossFilterActive` consumption pattern, the ~0.4 opacity multiplier the dim renderers will apply, and the `grid.inGrid` vs `dashboardTile` mutual exclusion that keeps the chat / explorer dim path untouched (the pre-existing `grid.filter` dim case in chat/explorer ChartGrid uses a different code path; the two contexts are mutually exclusive because a chart can't simultaneously be in a chat-grid AND a dashboard-tile).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimFoundation.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2DimFoundation.test.ts) (new, ~143 LOC). 13 tests across 4 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **DashboardTileContextValue extension** (4): type-only `ActiveChartFilters` import (pinned so a future refactor doesn't drag the runtime bundle); `DashboardTileContextValue` includes both `tileId: string` and `filters?: ActiveChartFilters`; `DashboardTileProviderProps` mirrors the optional prop alongside `children: ReactNode`; the function destructures `tileId, filters, children` in the props arg.
      - **Memoisation shape** (3): `useMemo` deps include both `tileId` and `filters`; the body uses the spread-conditional form `() => ({ tileId, ...(filters !== undefined ? { filters } : {}) })` (pin against a future refactor that ships `filters: undefined` straight into the object); default context value still `null` (pre-existing invariant).
      - **ChartTileBody pass-through** (2): the JSX is `<DashboardTileProvider tileId={tile.id} filters={filters}>` exactly; the `ChartTileBody` `filters` prop type is still `ActiveChartFilters | undefined` (sanity pin for the optionality the provider relies on).
      - **Documentation comment** (2): file header references both `WD2-dim-foundation` and `isCrossFilterActive` consumption; file header names the `grid.inGrid` / `dashboardTile` mutual exclusion so chat/explorer dim semantics are explicitly out of scope.
    - [docs/architecture/charting.md](architecture/charting.md). Recent-changes line appended.
    - [server/package.json](../server/package.json). `wd2DimFoundation.test.ts` appended to the explicit test list per invariant #4.

  **Why this design.** The split-first approach (foundation alone, ~50 LOC, no renderer touched) was chosen over a fat WD2-dim-foundation+bar wave for two reasons. First, the foundation extension is type-system-load-bearing across at least 6 follow-on waves (WD2-dim-bar / -cat / -rect / -trend / -point / -echarts) — getting it wrong forces re-litigating the foundation inside every follow-on. Splitting first lets the type shape land + bake + get verified before any renderer wave is started. Second, the foundation is contract-only and so trivially atomic that landing it alone keeps the next renderer wave focused on a single concern (the dim factor math + the opacity composition) rather than mixing context plumbing with rendering semantics. The spread-conditional pattern (`undefined → omit`) was preferred over `filters: filters ?? {}` because the upcoming dim-renderer guard wants to distinguish "rendered inside a dashboard tile but no filters yet" (provider mounted with `filters={undefined}` while DashboardView's filter map is still empty) from "rendered outside any dashboard tile" (the `useDashboardTileContext()` returns `null`). The current shape conflates these two cases at the *value* level — both produce an object with `value.filters === undefined` — but the `null`-vs-non-null at the *context* level is preserved (a dashboard-mounted provider always returns a non-null value, even with no filters), so renderers can still discriminate "dashboard tile context active" via `!!dashboardTile`. Alternative considered: a separate `DashboardFiltersProvider` distinct from the tile provider. Rejected because (a) it would require every renderer to consume *two* contexts, doubling the touch points; (b) the filter snapshot is conceptually tile-scoped — the same filter map applies to every mark inside a given tile — so co-locating it with the tile context matches the data shape.

  **Tests.** 13/13 new + 14/14 pre-existing dashboardTileContext tests passing (29 total in the two suites after two assertions in `dashboardTileContext.test.ts` were re-pinned to match the new memo shape + provider JSX). Server `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors (identical to pre-WD2-wiring-echarts baseline); client reports 53 errors (identical to pre-WD2-wiring-echarts baseline). Zero new errors from this wave.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Renderer-side dim factor computation.** WD2-dim-foundation only ships the context plumbing. WD2-dim-bar will be the first renderer wave: BarRenderer's existing `fillOpacity` composition (line 711–719 of [BarRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx)) needs a parallel dim factor — when `dashboardTile.filters` has an active categorical selection for `enc.x.field` AND the bar's `outerRaw` isn't in it, multiply opacity by ~0.4. Each subsequent renderer wave (WD2-dim-cat for Arc/Funnel/Box/Waterfall/Combo, WD2-dim-rect for the two-dim heatmap case, WD2-dim-trend for Line+Area, WD2-dim-point for scatter on `colorCh.field`, WD2-dim-echarts for the 5 ECharts marks) follows the same template.
    - **chat/explorer dim semantics.** The `grid.filter` dim case in chat/explorer `ChartGrid` is untouched — `grid.inGrid` and `dashboardTile` are mutually exclusive contexts, so the two dim paths can't double-dim a single mark.
    - **A `useDashboardFilters()` ergonomic alias.** A `useDashboardFilters()` helper that returns `useDashboardTileContext()?.filters ?? {}` would shave a line per renderer site. Deferred — the foundation wave's job is the type extension; ergonomic sugar can land in the first renderer wave once the usage pattern is concrete.

 The visx renderer family (WD2-wiring-bar through WD2-wiring-rest-point, 10 marks) finished earlier today. The ECharts specialty pack — 8 marks lazy-loaded via [`EChartsBase`](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/EChartsBase.tsx) — was the deliberately deferred follow-on: ECharts mounts its own canvas instance and exposes events through `instance.on('click', handler)` rather than per-mark `<svg onClick={...}>`, so the click-handling shape diverges from every visx renderer the WD2-wiring family touched. This wave threads a single optional `onChartClick` prop through `EChartsBase` and wires the 5 specialty marks with a meaningful categorical click target (treemap, sunburst, sankey, calendar, candlestick). Parallel coordinates, choropleth (stub), and gauge stay unwired — they have no categorical filter target, same invariant as KPI / Radar / Regression on the visx side.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/EChartsBase.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/EChartsBase.tsx). New optional prop `onChartClick?: (params: unknown) => void` on `EChartsBaseProps`. A ref-tracked callback (`const onChartClickRef = useRef<EChartsBaseProps["onChartClick"]>(onChartClick)` + a tiny `useEffect([onChartClick])` that writes `onChartClickRef.current = onChartClick`) makes a single mount-time bind pick up the latest handler on every render without an unbind/rebind cycle — the existing mount effect runs once with empty deps, and closing over the initial `onChartClick` directly would lose every subsequent update. Inside the `init()` async block, after `inst.setOption(buildOptions(echarts, theme) as never)` lands the options, the wave inserts a single `inst.on("click", (params: unknown) => { onChartClickRef.current?.(params); })`. ECharts requires the instance to be initialised + options applied before event binding takes effect, so the placement after `setOption` is load-bearing. Cleanup uses the existing `inst.dispose()` — ECharts removes every bound handler in one shot.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/TreemapRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/TreemapRenderer.tsx). New imports: `useCallback` (already had `useMemo`), `useDashboardTileContext`, `dispatchCrossFilter`, `toFilterValue`. Body reads `const dashboardTile = useDashboardTileContext()` before the `tree` memo and builds a per-call `onChartClick = useCallback((params: unknown) => {...}, [dashboardTile, labelCh.field])`. The handler narrows `params` to `{ data?: { name?: unknown; children?: unknown[] } }`, computes `isLeaf = !Array.isArray(p?.data?.children) || p.data.children.length === 0`, and dispatches `{ column: labelCh.field, value: toFilterValue(name), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId }` only when `isLeaf && name != null`. Parent-group clicks (the color encoding's value when present) are NOT dispatched — the dispatch column would be different from a leaf click, and treemap with `nodeClick: false` already disables the built-in zoom-on-parent behaviour, so adding a parent dispatch would surprise the user. `onChartClick={dashboardTile ? onChartClick : undefined}` passes the handler conditionally so chat / explorer / share-preview surfaces stay click-inert at the ECharts instance level.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/echartsRenderers/SpecialtyRenderers.tsx). Shared imports: `useCallback` + `useDashboardTileContext` + `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. Four renderers gain per-renderer handlers:
      - **`SunburstRenderer`** — identical leaf-only pattern to Treemap (sunburst's hierarchical data is built the same way). `onSunburstClick` reads `params.data.name` for leaves and dispatches on `labelCh.field`. Parent-ring (groupCh / color) clicks are skipped for the same reason as Treemap.
      - **`SankeyRenderer`** — node-clicks only (`params.dataType === 'node'`, edges skipped because edges have no single categorical value to filter on). Dispatch column is `sourceCh.field` — source / target are typically two columns of the same dimension in practice (e.g. Region → Region), so dispatching on source covers both endpoints. Cross-column sankeys would need a richer decode and are flagged in the comment as deferred.
      - **`CalendarRenderer`** — cell clicks. `params.data` is the ECharts `[yyyy-mm-dd, value]` tuple the renderer built in the series memo. Handler reads `params.data[0]` (the ISO date string), dispatches on `dateCh.field`. Downstream `applyCrossFilter` already installs categorical filters on date columns as discrete-value selections (same shape as a temporal-axis BarRenderer click).
      - **`CandlestickRenderer`** — bar clicks. `params.value` is the OHLC `[open, close, low, high]` tuple — NOT the categorical key. The categorical key for a candlestick bar is the time label on the x-axis; the handler reads `xs[params.dataIndex]` (the `xs` array was already built for the x-axis category data) with a bounds check and dispatches on `xCh.field`.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringEcharts.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringEcharts.test.ts) (new, ~225 LOC). 23 tests across 7 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **EChartsBase onChartClick prop** (4): optional `onChartClick?: (params: unknown) => void`; the ref-tracking pattern (`useRef` + tiny `useEffect([onChartClick])`); the `inst.on('click', ...)` bind placed AFTER `inst.setOption(...)` (regex pins source-index ordering, not regex inside string); the ref delegation in the bound handler.
      - **TreemapRenderer leaf-click** (5): imports; context read; leaf-only guard pinned by exact `!Array.isArray(...).children) || .length === 0` source; dispatch shape (`column: labelCh.field`, `value: toFilterValue(name)`, `sourceTileId`); conditional pass-through (`dashboardTile ? onChartClick : undefined`).
      - **SunburstRenderer leaf-click** (3): cross-filter imports + leaf-only pattern + conditional pass-through.
      - **SankeyRenderer node-click** (3): the `dataType === 'node'` gate (edges skipped); dispatch on `sourceCh.field`; conditional pass-through.
      - **CalendarRenderer cell-click** (2): reads `params.data[0]` (the ISO date string), dispatches on `dateCh.field`; conditional pass-through.
      - **CandlestickRenderer bar-click** (3): looks up `xs[dataIndex]` (NOT `params.value`); dispatches on `xCh.field`; conditional pass-through.
      - **Skipped renderers** (3): per-function-body assertion that `dispatchCrossFilter(` is absent from `ParallelRenderer`, `ChoroplethRenderer`, and `GaugeRenderer`.
      - 23/23 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **One generic prop on EChartsBase, not 5 specialty wrappers.** The natural alternative would be to introduce a per-renderer `EChartsCrossFilterWrapper` that injects `useDashboardTileContext` + `dispatchCrossFilter`. But that doubles the renderer count and risks divergence between marks. Putting the prop on EChartsBase keeps the base shell mark-agnostic (it just forwards the click) and pushes the `params`-shape decoding into each renderer where the encoding-specific knowledge already lives.
    - **Ref-tracking instead of off-then-on.** ECharts' mount-effect runs once with empty deps (the existing pattern), so a closure over `onChartClick` would capture the initial value forever. Two fixes: (1) add `[onChartClick]` to the mount-effect deps — but then a callback identity change would re-create the entire ECharts instance, losing animation state and re-running the canvas init; or (2) bind once with a ref that's updated on every render — single bind, no re-init, always-fresh callback. Option 2 is the standard React idiom for this "external system needs the latest callback" shape.
    - **`inst.on` after `setOption`, not before.** ECharts validates event subscriptions against the chart's series types at bind time. Calling `inst.on('click', ...)` before `setOption` is a no-op for the eventual click events. Pinned by test via source-index ordering (`indexOf("inst.setOption") < indexOf("inst.on")`).
    - **Leaf-only dispatch on hierarchical marks (treemap / sunburst).** A treemap with a `groupCh` shows two levels — parent groups and leaf items. A click on a parent group could plausibly dispatch on the group's field, but then the dispatch column flips between two clicks of the same mark, which is hostile UX. Skipping parent clicks and only dispatching on leaves means every dispatch from a treemap targets the same column — `labelCh.field`. Two-column dispatch (mirroring the RectRenderer row+col approach from WD2-wiring-rest-rect) is a follow-on if a use case appears.
    - **Source-only dispatch on sankey.** The natural alternative is "click a node, dispatch on the column the node belongs to" — but ECharts' params shape doesn't carry that information directly; it would need a side-table lookup. In practice every sankey use case at Marico's scale has same-dimension source / target (e.g. `Channel` → `Channel`, `Brand` → `Brand`), so dispatching on `sourceCh.field` covers both endpoints. Cross-column sankeys (e.g. `Brand` → `Channel`) would need the richer decode — flagged in the comment.
    - **Candlestick reads `xs[dataIndex]` not `params.value`.** ECharts' candlestick params.value is the 4-tuple `[open, close, low, high]`. None of those are the categorical key (the bar's x-axis label). The renderer already built an `xs` array for the x-axis category data — the same array the chart uses for axis labels. Using `dataIndex` to look up the matching `xs` entry is the canonical way to get the categorical key from an ECharts axis-bound series.
    - **Calendar dispatches ISO date string verbatim.** `applyCrossFilter` already handles date columns as categorical selections (discrete value lists). The date string `yyyy-mm-dd` is the canonical wire format the renderer built; round-tripping it through `Date.parse` + re-format would risk a TZ-offset bug. Pass the string straight through.
    - **`onChartClick={dashboardTile ? handler : undefined}` for every renderer.** A `useCallback(() => {...}, [dashboardTile, ...])` always returns a function — even when `dashboardTile` is null. Without the conditional ternary, the EChartsBase mount effect would bind `inst.on('click', ...)` unconditionally, which means a click in a chat / explorer / share-preview surface would invoke the handler, hit the `if (!dashboardTile) return` guard, and no-op. That works but is wasteful — the cleaner shape is to pass `undefined` when there's no consumer, so the bind doesn't happen at all. Mirrors the visx renderers' `interactive` flag pattern.

  **Verified.** New tests 23/23 pass. Sibling WD2 tests stay green (`crossFilter.test.ts` 29/29 + `dashboardTileContext.test.ts` 18/18 + `wd2WiringRestCat.test.ts` 36/36 + `wd2WiringRestRect.test.ts` 11/11 + `wd2WiringRestTrend.test.ts` 18/18 + `wd2WiringRestPoint.test.ts` 13/13 = 125/125 in the WD2 family). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to the WI3 baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `12f06b50`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Parallel coordinates dispatch.** Each parallel-axis line crosses every dim; clicking the line could plausibly dispatch on the highest-variance dim, but that's heuristic and the user can't see what'll happen before clicking. Deferred until a concrete UX motivates a per-line dispatch design. Test pins the absence to prevent regression.
    - **Choropleth dispatch.** The renderer is a stub — it falls back to an info card explaining that geographic data registration is required. When `echarts.registerMap('world', geoJson)` lands in a future wave + the renderer becomes real, dispatching on the region field will be a straightforward addition.
    - **Gauge dispatch.** A gauge is a single-value KPI; there's no categorical click target. Same invariant as KpiRenderer on the visx side. Test pins the absence.
    - **Two-column dispatch on treemap / sunburst parent rings.** Mirrors what RectRenderer does for row+col on heatmaps (WD2-wiring-rest-rect). For treemap / sunburst this would dispatch on the group field when the parent ring is clicked and on the label field when the leaf is clicked. Two clicks of the same mark dispatching on different columns is borderline-hostile UX, but a small follow-on could carry both columns and dispatch both (toggle both) per click. Defer until a use case demands it.
    - **Edge clicks on sankey.** An edge connects a source node to a target node; dispatching on both columns at once is the natural two-column shape (same as the heatmap pattern). But sankeys with same-dimension source / target would dispatch the same column twice. Without a use case for cross-dimension sankeys, deferred.
    - **`isCrossFilterActive` opacity dimming on ECharts marks.** The visx-side dormancy-debt item (renderers dim non-matching marks when a cross-filter is active) applies equally to ECharts. ECharts series have a `select` / `emphasis` mechanism that could carry the dim effect via the dataItem's `itemStyle.opacity`. Atomic follow-on, ~80 LOC across the 5 wired renderers.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WI3 · Sources footer on `TileInsightFooter` (regen citations array).** WI2-server's `extractInsightCitations(text)` walks the regen prose with the same regex W22 uses on the server narrator, returns the unique pack-id matches, and ships them as `InsightRegenEntry.citations: string[]` on the response body. Pre-WI3 that array was dead-loaded on the client — `useInsightRegen` placed it on the cache, the cache held it for 5 minutes, but no consuming surface read it. The inline `[N]` superscript hover-cards INSIDE the prose worked transitively through `MarkdownRenderer`'s WQ3 integration (the renderer pre-walks every line via `extractCitations` + `buildCitationIndex` to assign stable 1-based superscript numbers per unique pack id), so for prose that contains the backtick tokens the visual was already correct. But users who skim past the inline `[1]` `[2]` markings — or whose dashboard is dense enough that the small superscripts blur into the body text — had no discoverable surface for "which packs is this insight grounded in?". WI3 closes that gap with a single explicit "Sources:" row.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx). New import: `CitationHoverCard` from `@/components/CitationHoverCard` (the WQ3 component that renders a single pack id as a `<sup>[N]</sup>` Radix HoverCard with a metadata-only popover). Pre-WI3 the regen branch rendered three blocks in order: `<MarkdownRenderer>` for the prose, an "Updated <relative> · <tier> confidence" metadata `<div>`, then the action `<div>` with the Re-explain button + error span. WI3 inserts a fourth block between the metadata and the action: a `flex flex-wrap items-center gap-1 text-[11px] text-muted-foreground` row containing the literal "Sources:" label and the citations array `.map((packId, i) => <CitationHoverCard key={packId} packId={packId} index={i + 1} />)`. Gated on `regen?.entry?.citations && regen.entry.citations.length > 0` so missing arrays AND empty arrays short-circuit to no render — the row never appears for charts whose regen prose has no domain-pack citations. A comment above the `<MarkdownRenderer>` documents that inline backtick-wrapped pack ids inside the regen text continue to render via `MarkdownRenderer`'s WQ3 path; the new Sources row is purely a discoverable list, not a replacement.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooterWI3.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooterWI3.test.ts) (new, ~95 LOC). 8 source-inspection tests in one suite; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **TileInsightFooter sources footer** (8): import shape for `CitationHoverCard`; the truthy-AND-non-empty gate (`regen?.entry?.citations && regen.entry.citations.length > 0`); the literal `<span>Sources:</span>` label; the `.map((packId, i) => <CitationHoverCard key={packId} packId={packId} index={i + 1} />)` shape with the `i + 1` 1-based superscript convention; the structural ordering by `indexOf` (metadata line → sources row → Re-explain button); the `flex flex-wrap` container class so long citation lists wrap rather than overflow; the `regen?.entry?.citations` optional-chaining that handles the regen-absent case; the documentation comment that names `MarkdownRenderer` and `WQ3` so future maintainers don't try to wire inline rendering twice.
      - 8/8 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Surface the citations array, don't replace the inline rendering.** The `MarkdownRenderer` WQ3 integration is the canonical inline-citation surface — it works for narrator prose in the chat, for dashboard insights, and now (transitively, without code change) for WI2-server-generated regen text. Removing or replacing that path would force every consumer to re-implement the inline hover-card logic. The Sources row is *additive*: a separate, discoverable list for users who don't visually parse the `[1]` superscripts. Two surfaces for two reading patterns.
    - **Reuse `CitationHoverCard` rather than build a new chip component.** `CitationHoverCard` already encodes the "this is a verifiable citation" visual language across the app — the dotted-underline `[N]` superscript, the Radix HoverCard popover with pack label / canonical id / explanatory note. Adopting it in the Sources row keeps the visual identity consistent: a user who sees `[1]` in narrator prose recognises the same `[1]` in a tile insight, and hovers expecting the same metadata. Building a new chip would diverge the language without adding capability.
    - **Truthy AND length-gate avoids the empty array.** `InsightRegenEntry.citations` is `string[] | undefined` on the schema. The server may return an empty array when `extractInsightCitations(text)` finds no backtick tokens (the W22 hyphen rule filters generic spans). Without the length check, the row would render with just the "Sources:" label and no chips — visually broken. The `&& length > 0` lights up only when there's something to show.
    - **`flex flex-wrap` for long citation lists.** A regen response can cite up to ~4 packs in practice (the WI2-server prompt is biased toward conciseness, but doesn't cap citations). Four `[1] [2] [3] [4]` superscripts fit in a tile footer of typical width; six or seven would overflow without wrap. `flex-wrap` keeps the visual stable across citation counts without imposing a hard cap.
    - **1-based index passed explicitly via `i + 1`.** `CitationHoverCard` renders `[{index}]`, so passing `i + 1` (instead of `i`) gives users `[1] [2] [3]` rather than `[0] [1] [2]`. The 1-based convention matches the existing `MarkdownRenderer`-driven inline rendering (which uses `buildCitationIndex` returning `map.size + 1`).
    - **Place between metadata and action row.** The visual flow on a regen-populated footer is: prose → "Updated 2 min ago · medium confidence" → sources → action. Reading the prose primes the reader, the metadata says "fresh and trustworthy", the sources qualify the trust ("grounded in haircare-portfolio + kpi-glossary"), and only then the action button invites further interaction. Reordering would break the rhythm.
    - **Key by `packId`, not by `i`.** The citations array is expected to be already deduped by the server-side `extractInsightCitations` (it walks the prose left-to-right and adds each pack id to a set). Keying by `packId` is stable across re-renders even if the array order changes; keying by index would cause React to re-mount HoverCards on reorder, losing any open hover state. Both approaches work for the current usage but `packId` keying is the future-proof choice.

  **Verified.** New tests 8/8 pass. `TileInsightFooter.vitest.test.ts` (DR18B sessionStorage tests) stays green — WI3 doesn't touch the open/closed persistence path. `useInsightRegen.test.ts` 22/22 stays green — the hook's contract is unchanged. `ChartTileBody.test.ts` 19/19 stays green — the binding wave's prop wiring is unchanged. `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to the WI2-wire-bind baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `89c06919`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Pack body in the hover-card popover.** `CitationHoverCard`'s popover currently shows the humanised label + canonical id + an "Admin · Domain Context for the full pack body" pointer. Threading the actual pack body (a paragraph of FMCG / haircare priors) into the popover would let users read the citation without leaving the dashboard. Needs a pack-body fetcher in the session envelope or a lazy `/api/admin/domain-packs/:id` call from the hover-card. WQ3's "Out of scope" already named this — same defer applies here.
    - **Numbering parity between inline `[1]` and Sources `[1]`.** Currently the MarkdownRenderer-driven inline rendering builds its own `citationIndex` per content string, and the Sources row uses array-position `i + 1`. If the LLM emits pack ids in a different order in prose vs. citations array, the inline `[2]` and the Sources `[1]` could point at different packs for the same visual number. The server-side `extractInsightCitations` walks the prose left-to-right so in practice they line up, but a regression test pinning this would be valuable. ~20 LOC follow-on.
    - **Citations on the static fallback `insight` string.** When `regen.entry` is absent, the static `keyInsight` renders. Static insights might also contain backtick-wrapped pack ids — those render inline through `MarkdownRenderer` as expected, but there's no `citations` array to surface in a Sources row. A future wave could call `listCitedPackIds(insight)` from `@/lib/citationTokens` to derive the Sources row from the static prose too. Defer until UX evidence shows users want it.
    - **Right-aligned Sources / inline beside metadata.** Current layout puts Sources on its own row. A more compact alternative would inline "Sources:" beside the "Updated …" metadata as a trailing chip group. Saves a footer row at the cost of horizontal density. UX call; not load-bearing.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WI2-wire-bind · ChartTileBody binds `useInsightRegen` + filtered rows (closes the WI2 trilogy at the consumer level).** WI2-wire (earlier today) shipped the consumer-agnostic surface — a `useInsightRegen` hook + an optional `regen?: {...}` prop on `TileInsightFooter` — but nothing called them. The "Out of scope" of that wave named two follow-ons: thread the chart spec / filtered data through `ChartTileBody`, and hold a shared cache instance at `DashboardView` mount level. This wave does both in one atomic change. The load-bearing risk the previous wave flagged was filteredData plumbing — "ChartShim / PremiumChart may need a new prop the renderers can call back into, or a getFilteredData accessor exposed on a ref" — which turned out to be unnecessary: the existing pure helper `applyChartFilters(rows, filters)` in [`client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts`](../client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts) consumes the `tile.chart.data` array directly and returns the filtered rows, so the wave sidesteps any ChartShim refactor.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardView.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardView.tsx). New import: `createInsightRegenCache` from `../lib/insightRegenCache`. One new line inside the function body: `const insightRegenCache = useMemo(() => createInsightRegenCache(), []);` — the empty dep array pins a single cache instance for the dashboard session so re-toggling between explored filter combos within the session hits the cache instead of re-firing the LLM. The cache is forwarded as a new `insightRegenCache={insightRegenCache}` prop on the `<DashboardTiles>` mount.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardTiles.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardTiles.tsx). New `import type { InsightRegenCache }` from `../lib/insightRegenCache`. New optional prop `insightRegenCache?: InsightRegenCache` on `DashboardTilesProps`; destructured from props and forwarded verbatim as `insightRegenCache={insightRegenCache}` on the `<ChartTileBody>` mount (line 806). The component is a thin pass-through — no shape change between the DashboardView mount and the ChartTileBody consumer; making it optional keeps every existing call site backwards-compatible.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.tsx). The load-bearing component. New imports: `useCallback, useMemo` from React; `applyChartFilters` alongside `type ActiveChartFilters` from `@/lib/chartFilters`; `useInsightRegen, type InsightChartSpecLite, type InsightRegenRow` from `../hooks/useInsightRegen`; `type InsightRegenCache` from `../lib/insightRegenCache`. New optional prop `insightRegenCache?: InsightRegenCache` on `ChartTileBodyProps`. Four new locals before `return`:
      - `const specLite: InsightChartSpecLite = useMemo(...)` — derives `{ type, title, x, y }` directly from `tile.chart` (the `InsightChartSpecLite` field set is a strict subset of `ChartSpec`, so the mapping is field-for-field) plus `seriesColumn` / `aggregate` via spread-conditional inclusion so undefined optionals don't ship to the strict zod request schema. Dep array is the same six load-bearing fields so the lite spec recomputes when the chart's identity changes but stays stable across irrelevant re-renders.
      - `const filteredRows = useMemo<InsightRegenRow[]>(() => applyChartFilters((tile.chart.data ??
