[]) as Array<Record<string, string | number | null>>, filters ?? {}) as InsightRegenRow[], [tile.chart.data, filters])`. Two safety fall-throughs: `?? []` handles charts without embedded data (agent-generated charts whose rows aren't shipped on the spec), `?? {}` makes the no-active-filters case a pure no-op. The double cast is necessary because `ChartSpec.data` cells are `string | number | null` (per the zod schema at [server/shared/schema.ts:108](../server/shared/schema.ts#L108)) while `InsightRegenRow` cells are `string | number | boolean | null` — the former is a structural subset of the latter, so the cast is safe.
      - `const regen = useInsightRegen({ tileId: tile.id, filters: filters ?? {}, cache: insightRegenCache })` — mounts the hook with the shared cache from above. When the parent doesn't pass a cache the hook falls back to its per-mount `useMemo([])` cache, which is fine for one-tile-in-isolation but loses the cross-tile warm-cache hit; the prop is the load-bearing wiring that closes the trilogy properly.
      - `const handleRegenerate = useCallback(() => { void regen.regenerate(specLite, filteredRows); }, [regen, specLite, filteredRows])` — the no-arg fire-and-forget callback the footer button calls. The `void` discards the returned promise; the hook is responsible for surfacing the loading / error state through its return shape. Dynamic context flows in at click time, preserving the hook's over-fire-on-every-render guard.
      - The `<TileInsightFooter>` mount inside the existing `tile.chart.keyInsight ?` guard gains a four-key `regen={{ entry: regen.entry, loading: regen.loading, error: regen.error, onRegenerate: handleRegenerate }}` prop. The regen surface lives INSIDE the keyInsight guard — charts without a static insight remain visually unchanged (no empty footer added).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.test.ts) (new, ~185 LOC). 19 tests across 3 source-inspection suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **ChartTileBody hooks + filtered-data binding** (12): import shape for `useInsightRegen` / `applyChartFilters` / `InsightRegenCache`; the `insightRegenCache?: InsightRegenCache` prop declaration + destructure; `specLite: InsightChartSpecLite = useMemo(...)` with the load-bearing fields + spread-conditional seriesColumn/aggregate; the `applyChartFilters((tile.chart.data ?? []) as ..., filters ?? {}) as InsightRegenRow[]` shape with the explicit cast pinned; `useInsightRegen({ tileId: tile.id, filters: filters ?? {}, cache: insightRegenCache })`; the no-arg `handleRegenerate` callback closing over `[regen, specLite, filteredRows]`; the four-key regen prop passed to `<TileInsightFooter>`; the `tile.chart.keyInsight ? <TileInsightFooter>` guard preserves the no-empty-footer contract.
      - **DashboardTiles forwards the cache** (4): `import type { InsightRegenCache }` from the WI2-cache module; the optional `insightRegenCache?: InsightRegenCache` prop on `DashboardTilesProps`; destructure; verbatim forward to `<ChartTileBody>`.
      - **DashboardView mounts a single shared cache** (3): `import { createInsightRegenCache }` from `../lib/insightRegenCache`; `useMemo(() => createInsightRegenCache(), [])` with the empty dep array load-bearing (a stale dep would churn the cache on every re-render); cache threaded through to `<DashboardTiles>`.
      - 19/19 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Pure helper sidesteps the ChartShim refactor.** The previous wave's "Out of scope" warned that exposing filteredData might require either a new prop on ChartShim that the renderers call back into, or a `getFilteredData` accessor exposed on a ref. Both are valid but both would be load-bearing changes touching the 1,820-LOC legacy ChartRenderer god-object or the PremiumChart lazy-load chain. The pragmatic alternative is to recompute the filter application in `ChartTileBody` from the spec's embedded `data` array — `applyChartFilters` is a pure function that already exists for the explorer / chat surfaces. The downside is a duplicate scan of the row array (once inside the ChartShim render, once in the regen path) — but the rows live in memory anyway, the predicate is O(rows × filters), and the work is gated behind the user clicking "Re-explain this view" rather than running on every render.
    - **Spread-conditional optionals match the hook's request body shape.** `useInsightRegen.regenerate(spec, ...)` ships the spec to a server endpoint backed by a strict zod schema. The spec's optional fields (`seriesColumn`, `aggregate`) ship as keys-when-present rather than as `undefined`-valued keys so the schema's `.optional()` semantics don't trip on null. The `specLite` builder follows the same pattern the hook itself uses for `domainContext` / `datasetContextHint`.
    - **Empty dep array on the shared cache is load-bearing.** A `useMemo(() => createInsightRegenCache(), [someUnstableDep])` would create a fresh cache on every re-render whenever `someUnstableDep` changed identity — defeating the whole point of holding the cache at the DashboardView mount level. Pinning `[]` (no deps) means one cache instance for the lifetime of the dashboard session, which is what we want. The test pins this exactly.
    - **Cache prop is optional all the way down.** `DashboardTiles` and `ChartTileBody` both accept `insightRegenCache?: InsightRegenCache`. The hook itself accepts `cache?: InsightRegenCache` and falls back to a per-instance `useMemo([])` cache when nothing is injected. This means: existing callers of either component compile cleanly without changes; tests can mount ChartTileBody in isolation; a future surface (e.g., a chat-side preview of a chart) can mount ChartTileBody outside DashboardView without breaking.
    - **`handleRegenerate` captures `regen` not `regen.regenerate`.** The hook returns a fresh `regenerate` identity on every render (`useCallback(..., [cache, cacheKey, tileId])`), so closing over `regen` rather than `regen.regenerate` would force the callback's dep array to include every regen field. Closing over the function via `regen.regenerate(specLite, filteredRows)` and listing `[regen, specLite, filteredRows]` keeps the callback's identity stable as long as the regen object's identity is stable.
    - **No domainContext / datasetContextHint at the call site (for now).** Searching `client/src/pages/Dashboard/` for `domainContext` shows no existing loader — the active-pack text is server-side context for the planner / narrator, not currently surfaced to the client dashboard view. The hook's `options.domainContext` / `options.datasetContextHint` are spread-conditional so omitting them doesn't ship `null` to the strict zod schema. When a future wave plumbs domain context into the dashboard (e.g., via a new `useDomainContext` provider), this call site picks them up by passing the options object — no hook change needed.
    - **Regen surface lives inside the `tile.chart.keyInsight` guard.** A chart without a static keyInsight already has no footer — adding a regen button to such tiles would either need to render its own footer scaffolding (UX divergence from the existing pattern) or render orphan. Gating both the footer and its regen surface on `keyInsight` preserves the pre-binding visual contract: tiles that didn't have a footer still don't, tiles that did now have a regen button in their existing footer.

  **Verified.** New tests 19/19 pass. WI2 sibling tests stay green (`useInsightRegen.test.ts` 22/22 + `insightRegenCache.test.ts` 21/21 + `insightRegenWI2Server.test.ts` 36/36 = 79/79 in the WI2 family). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to the WI2-wire baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `2b70449a`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Domain-context / dataset-context hint plumbing.** The hook accepts both as spread-conditional options; the wave omits them because there's no domain-context loader in the dashboard yet. A future wave (potentially `WI4 — explain-this-slice`) can either add a `useDomainContext()` provider at DashboardView level or thread the active-pack text from the existing `useDashboardContext()` if it carries it. ~30 LOC follow-on.
    - **Auto-regen on filter change.** Per WI2-wire's analysis, an opt-in `regenerate-on-filter-change` boolean would burn the user's budget on a browse-heavy session. Defer until user-research evidence demands it.
    - **Spec-hash mixed into the cache key.** WI2-cache keyed on `(tileId, filterHash)` — spec changes (metric rename, breakdown swap) don't invalidate the cache. A `specHash` mixed into the key would let the cache survive spec edits but invalidate cleanly on chart-shape changes. The `InsightChartSpecLite` shape is exactly the right hash input; a `hashInsightSpec(spec)` helper would be ~20 LOC. Defer to WI4-or-later.
    - **Stream the regenerate response.** Currently one-shot JSON; streaming would shave ~200ms of perceived latency. Same defer as WI2-wire — not load-bearing for the UX yet.
    - **Backwards-compat shim for callers that haven't migrated yet.** `DashboardTiles` and `ChartTileBody` both take the new cache prop as optional, so no shim is needed. If a future wave makes the cache mandatory, this becomes the migration point. No action needed now.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WI2-wire · `useInsightRegen` hook + "✦ Re-explain this view" button.** Closes the WI2 trilogy. WI2-cache (yesterday) shipped the per-tile LRU + TTL cache keyed by `(tileId, hashGlobalFilters(filters))`; WI2-server (yesterday) shipped `POST /api/insight/regen` whose response shape matches `InsightRegenEntry` byte-for-byte. WI2-wire is the React surface that consumes both — a hook for the per-tile lifecycle and a button for the user trigger. The architectural shape was deliberately set up by the earlier two waves so this wave is a straight wire-up: `cache.set(buildCacheKey(...), response)` with no transformation, response shape is contract-compatible by design.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/hooks/useInsightRegen.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/hooks/useInsightRegen.ts) (new, ~165 LOC). Signature: `useInsightRegen({ tileId, filters, cache? }): { entry, loading, error, regenerate, cacheKey }`. The dynamic regen context (spec / filteredData / domainContext / datasetContextHint) flows in at CALL time on `regenerate(spec, filteredData, options?)` rather than at hook-instantiation time — that side-steps the over-fire-on-every-render trap that a `useEffect`-driven design would create. Per-mount fallback cache via `useMemo(() => createInsightRegenCache(), [])` when no shared cache is injected. Cache key derives from `buildCacheKey(tileId, hashGlobalFilters(filters))` via `useMemo([tileId, filters])`. The cached entry reads synchronously every render (`const entry = cache.get(cacheKey)`) so re-toggling between explored filter combos paints instantly without spinning the network. `regenerate()` checks cache first (unless `options.bypassCache`), POSTs the request body with `credentials: "include"`, merges the parsed response straight into the cache via `cache.set(cacheKey, parsed)`. A `seqRef` guards against stale resolves clobbering newer state — every `regenerate()` bumps the sequence; only the latest resolution commits its `loading = false` / `error`. `domainContext` / `datasetContextHint` are spread-conditional so `undefined` optionals don't ship `null` to the strict zod schema. `safeReadError` prefers a JSON `error` field, falling back to `"Regen failed (<status>)"`.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx). New `TileInsightFooterRegenProps` type `{ entry: InsightRegenEntry | undefined; loading: boolean; error: string | null; onRegenerate: () => void }`. The footer gains an optional `regen?: TileInsightFooterRegenProps` prop — when omitted, the legacy passive footer is unchanged. When provided: `<MarkdownRenderer content={regen?.entry?.text || insight} />` so the regenerated entry's text takes precedence once it lands, with the static keyInsight as fallback so the footer isn't empty mid-flight; a "✦ Re-explain this view" `<Button>` renders below with `Sparkles` (idle) / `Loader2 animate-spin` (loading) icons; `disabled={regen.loading}`; `e.stopPropagation()` in the onClick keeps the parent footer expand/collapse toggle quiet; errors render with `role="alert"` for a11y; entry metadata renders `Updated <relative> · <tier> confidence` via a local `formatRelativeShort` helper that emits s / min / h / d windows. The icons `Loader2` + `Sparkles` are added to the existing `lucide-react` import; the `InsightRegenEntry` type imports from `../lib/insightRegenCache`.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/hooks/useInsightRegen.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/hooks/useInsightRegen.test.ts) (new, ~165 LOC). 22 tests across 2 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **useInsightRegen hook shape** (11): imports the WI2-cache helpers via the canonical relative path; cacheKey derives from `buildCacheKey(tileId, hashGlobalFilters(filters))` in a `useMemo([tileId, filters])`; reads `cache.get(cacheKey)` synchronously every render; cache-first check inside `regenerate()` (`if (!bypass) { const cached = cache.get(cacheKey); if (cached) return cached; }`); POSTs to `/api/insight/regen` with `method: "POST"`, `credentials: "include"`, `headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" }`, `body: JSON.stringify(body)`; the parsed response is merged into the cache via `cache.set(cacheKey, parsed)` with no transformation; the `seqRef` stale-resolve guard (`const seq = ++seqRef.current; ... if (seq === seqRef.current) setLoading(false);`); the `bypassCache` option override; the spread-conditional `domainContext` / `datasetContextHint` inclusion; the per-mount fallback cache (`useMemo(() => createInsightRegenCache(), [])`); `safeReadError` prefers a JSON `error` field with a status-text fallback.
      - **TileInsightFooter regen surface** (11): imports the `InsightRegenEntry` type from the cache module; imports `Loader2` + `Sparkles` icons; exports the canonical `TileInsightFooterRegenProps` shape; optional `regen?: TileInsightFooterRegenProps` on the props interface; the precedence rule (`<MarkdownRenderer content={regen?.entry?.text || insight} />`); the button renders only when `regen` is provided (`{regen ? (<Button …/>) : null}`); the icon swap between `Loader2` and `Sparkles` based on `regen.loading`; `disabled={regen.loading}` + `e.stopPropagation()` on click; the `role="alert"` error span; the "Updated <relative>" + confidence-tier metadata renderer; `formatRelativeShort` covers s / min / h / d windows.
      - 22/22 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Dynamic context at call time, NOT instantiation time.** The chart spec, filtered data, and domain context can change with every user interaction — every filter add, every brush, every legend toggle. Threading them through `useEffect` deps would either over-fire the network on every render (an expensive `[filteredData]` dep array would force a deep-equality memo in every caller) or under-fire (sloppy comparison would miss valid updates). Putting the dynamic args on `regenerate(spec, filteredData, options?)` means the caller passes what it has when it triggers the regen, and the hook's render-time concerns stay tiny.
    - **No auto-regen on filter change.** A naïve "re-explain on every filter change" would fire dozens of LLM calls per browse session and burn the user's budget. The cache picks up the previously regenerated entry instantly when the user retraces an explored filter combo (the `cache.get` reads synchronously every render); the button is the only trigger for *fresh* prose. Future Claude can add an opt-in auto-regen via a `regenerate-on-filter-change` boolean flag without breaking the contract.
    - **`seqRef` stale-resolve guard.** A user clicks "Re-explain", changes the filter, clicks "Re-explain" again — both network calls can be in flight. Without the sequence guard, whichever resolves second would commit its `loading = false` regardless of which was newer. The bump-on-call + check-on-resolve pattern is the standard `useRef`-based abort-by-comparison trick; doesn't require an `AbortController` because the in-flight `fetch` is wasteful but not racy in any way that breaks UX (the second call's response will land in the cache eventually).
    - **Response merged into the cache with no transformation.** The server endpoint shape was deliberately designed in WI2-server to match `InsightRegenEntry` byte-for-byte — `{ text, citations?, regeneratedAt, confidenceTier }`. Doing `cache.set(cacheKey, parsed as InsightRegenEntry)` rather than re-shaping the response keeps the contract honest and the call site one line. A test pins this: any future field rename on either side would surface as a contract mismatch immediately.
    - **TileInsightFooter precedence (regen text wins, static is fallback).** When the regen entry has landed, showing the regenerated text is the whole point of the wave. But mid-flight (first click, before the response arrives), `regen.entry` is `undefined` — falling back to the static `insight` keeps the footer non-empty rather than showing a "loading…" shell. The single `regen?.entry?.text || insight` predicate covers both states elegantly.
    - **Optional regen prop preserves the legacy passive footer.** The footer is consumed today by `ChartTileBody` (DR3 / DR18B). Making `regen` optional means this wave doesn't touch ChartTileBody — the binding (which needs filteredData plumbing through ChartShim / PremiumChart) is a follow-on `WI2-wire-bind` wave. Existing consumers continue working byte-stably; new consumers opt in.
    - **`formatRelativeShort` local helper rather than `date-fns`.** The footer already pulls a single tiny formatter need; importing `date-fns` for `formatDistanceToNowStrict` would bloat the bundle for one call site. Six lines of conditional truncation cover every realistic window (sub-minute / sub-hour / sub-day / day+) without a dependency.
    - **`role="alert"` on the error span.** Accessibility — screen readers announce alerts as soon as they enter the DOM. The button's `disabled` while loading already provides a visual cue; pairing it with an a11y-announced error message means the failure mode is discoverable without sight.

  **Verified.** Full server suite 3612/3612 pass (was 3590 pre-this-wave, adding 22). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to WD2-wiring-rest-point baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `89f613c2`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **`WI2-wire-bind` — ChartTileBody binding.** Threading the chart spec + filtered data + domain context + dataset context hint through `ChartTileBody → TileInsightFooter` requires plumbing that touches `ChartShim` / `PremiumChart` (to expose the post-filter dataset) AND the dashboard's domain-context loader (to surface the active pack). Each piece is a small change but composing them is its own atomic wave. Out of scope here; the hook + footer extension ship independently so the wiring wave is a thin call-site change once the data is in scope.
    - **Shared cache across tiles in one DashboardView.** The hook accepts an optional `cache` injection so a future `DashboardView` mount can hold one `createInsightRegenCache()` and share it across every tile's `useInsightRegen` instance. The per-mount fallback works for one tile in isolation; the shared-cache wiring lands with `WI2-wire-bind`.
    - **Auto-regen on filter change.** Discussed in "Why this design" — the user trigger is the right cadence for cost / latency reasons. A future opt-in boolean flag could enable it for power users, but no UX evidence demands it yet.
    - **Stream the response.** The endpoint is one-shot JSON; 30–80 tokens of MINI-tier output land in ~500ms. Streaming would shave the perceived latency by ~200ms — measurable but not load-bearing. Defer until UX measurement justifies the SSE complexity.
    - **WI3 — citation hover-cards on regenerated insights.** WQ3 shipped `CitationHoverCard` for narrator prose. Threading it through the regenerated insight `citations` field is the natural next wave — it'll touch only `TileInsightFooter` (or a wrapping renderer) and the hook itself doesn't change.
    - **Cache invalidation on chart-spec change.** The current key is `(tileId, filterHash)`. Spec changes (metric rename, breakdown swap) require a manual `cache.clear()` from the consuming hook. The cleaner long-term shape is a `specHash` mixed into the cache key, but that needs a spec-digest helper that the `WI2-wire-bind` wave can also ship.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-wiring-rest-point · PointRenderer scatter wired to `dispatchCrossFilter` (colorCh-gated).** PointRenderer (scatter / bubble) is the last visx renderer in WD2-wiring-rest with a meaningful cross-filter target — and it's the only one whose dispatch is conditional on the encoding shape. Pure quantitative (x, y) scatters have no categorical field to filter on; a click would dispatch a continuous-number value that could never match an existing categorical filter selection. When `colorCh` IS set, however, each point's color group becomes a natural brush target — clicking any point in the "North" group should toggle a Region=North filter on the dashboard, same way clicking a bar or a slice does for the categorical-by-construction marks.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/PointRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/PointRenderer.tsx). Imports `useDashboardTileContext` + `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. Body reads `const dashboardTile = useDashboardTileContext()` after the `(!xCh || !yCh)` throw guard, then derives `const crossFilterReady = !!dashboardTile && !!colorCh` — the single load-bearing predicate. Each point now preserves `rawColor: colorCh ? colorCh.accessor(r) : undefined` alongside the existing stringified `colorKey`; `colorKey` derives from `rawColor` via `asString(rawColor)` so the accessor runs once per row. Both render paths (`<Circle>` for plain scatters, glyph `<path>` for shape-encoded scatters) gain `style={cursorStyle}` + `onClick={onPointClick}` where `cursorStyle` is `crossFilterReady ? { cursor: "pointer" as const } : undefined` and `onPointClick` is `crossFilterReady ? () => dispatchCrossFilter({ column: colorCh!.field, value: toFilterValue(p.rawColor), sourceTileId: dashboardTile!.tileId }) : undefined`. The two render paths get identical wiring so future maintainers don't introduce a divergence by touching one.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestPoint.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestPoint.test.ts) (new, ~100 LOC). 13 tests across 2 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **PointRenderer cross-filter wiring** (10): imports + context read; the `crossFilterReady = !!dashboardTile && !!colorCh` gate pinned by exact source text; the dispatch shape (`column: colorCh!.field`, `value: toFilterValue(p.rawColor)`, `sourceTileId: dashboardTile!.tileId`); the `onPointClick` conditional ternary; the `cursorStyle` `as const` literal type; both `<Circle>` and glyph `<path>` carry both `style={cursorStyle}` and `onClick={onPointClick}`; the existing `onMouseMove` + `onMouseLeave` tooltip handlers are preserved on both render paths (regression guard).
      - **Raw color value is preserved on every point** (3): `rawColor = colorCh ? colorCh.accessor(r) : undefined`; `colorKey = colorCh ? asString(rawColor) : ""` (derives from rawColor, not a fresh accessor call); `rawColor` is included in the point object returned from `data.map`.
      - 13/13 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **`crossFilterReady` is a single source of truth.** Both the cursor and the onClick reference the same predicate, so a future maintainer can't accidentally make one fire without the other (e.g. cursor:pointer but no click, or vice versa). Putting the gate in a single local means the regression test pins exactly one line and any deviation surfaces immediately.
    - **Dispatch on `colorCh`, NOT on x/y.** PointRenderer has 5 encodings: x, y (required, quant), color (optional, categorical), size (optional, quant), shape (optional, categorical). The categorical encodings are color and shape. Of those, color is the universal one (every dashboard scatter that wants a brush target uses color encoding to distinguish groups); shape is a secondary encoding for 2-dim categorical-on-scatter. Dispatching on color is the right default. Wiring shape dispatch too is a possible follow-on (the master plan's "2-dim brush" idea); deferred for now to keep the wave atomic.
    - **`rawColor` preservation alongside `colorKey`.** Mirrors the WD2-wiring-rest-cat / WD2-wiring-rest-rect / WD2-wiring-rest-trend pattern. The stringified `colorKey` is needed for the color-group map (which is keyed on strings); the raw value flows to `toFilterValue` so numeric / boolean / Date color categories don't get double-stringified.
    - **Both render paths wired uniformly.** PointRenderer has two render branches: `if (shapeCh)` renders a glyph `<path>`, else a `<Circle>`. Wiring the click on the `<Circle>` branch alone would silently break the shape-encoded scatter; wiring it through a wrapping `<g>` would require changing the existing keyed render order. Splitting the wiring across both branches and pinning both via test is the smallest change that preserves the existing render contract.
    - **`crossFilterReady` excludes pure scatters explicitly.** Without the colorCh gate, a click on a pure (x, y) scatter would dispatch `{ column: undefined, value: toFilterValue(undefined) }` → `{ column: undefined, value: "null" }`, which the DashboardView handler would reject at the `typeof detail.column !== 'string'` guard but would still wastefully traverse the SSE channel. Skipping dispatch entirely is cleaner.

  **Verified.** Full server suite 3590/3590 pass (was 3577 pre-this-wave, adding 13). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to WD2-wiring-rest-trend baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `df5617e2`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **KPI / Radar / Regression renderers.** No meaningful categorical click target. KpiRenderer is a single big-number tile + sparkline; Radar's polygons cover all spokes for one series; Regression is pure quantitative x/y scatter (no color encoding by definition — if it had one, it'd be a colored scatter, not a regression-line chart). Deliberately skipped; documented in this wave's "Out of scope" so a future Claude doesn't reopen the question.
    - **Shape-encoded dispatch.** Could fire alongside color (two dispatches, similar to RectRenderer's row+col approach in WD2-wiring-rest-rect) when both color AND shape encodings are present. Defer until a use case appears.
    - **ECharts specialty pack.** Treemap / sunburst / sankey / parallel / calendar / candlestick / choropleth / gauge use a different click-event shape; `WD2-wiring-echarts` is a separate adapter wave.
    - **`isCrossFilterActive` dim-non-matching marks.** The visualisation pair of dispatch (this wave is the dispatch side) is still unwired across every renderer. Separate visualisation wave.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-wiring-rest-trend · Line + Area trend renderers wired to `dispatchCrossFilter`.** WD2-wiring-rest-cat + WD2-wiring-rest-rect (both earlier today) covered every visx renderer with per-mark categorical click targets. LineRenderer and AreaRenderer are different: they render continuous paths, not discrete marks. There's no `cells[i]` to attach an onClick to — the click has to be sourced from the click x-coordinate via a nearest-x lookup over every series' points. Compounding that, LineRenderer already owns brush-zoom mouse handlers (the user drags to zoom into a range), so the cross-filter dispatch has to respect the existing click-vs-drag distinction or risk firing on every zoom interaction.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx). Imports `useDashboardTileContext` + `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. Body reads `const dashboardTile = useDashboardTileContext()` after the `isTemporal` / `yIsRight` derivations. The existing `onBrushUp` handler already had a `if (Math.abs(hi - lo) < 6)` click-treatment branch that treated tiny drags as a click and reset the brush state without zooming — perfect anchor for the new dispatch. Inside that branch, BEFORE the `setBrushStart(null)` reset (so the recorded click position is still available), the wave inserts: `if (dashboardTile)` → set `clickX = lo`, scan every `series[i].points[j]` for the minimum `|xPx(p.x) - clickX|`, capture the winning `nearest: SeriesPoint`, and `dispatchCrossFilter({ column: xCh.field, value: toFilterValue(nearest.x), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId })`. Two-level gating: outer `if (dashboardTile)` avoids the scan cost on chat / explorer (where the dispatch would be a no-op anyway); inner `if (nearest)` handles the empty-series edge case silently.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/AreaRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/AreaRenderer.tsx). Same imports plus `localPoint` from `@visx/event` (LineRenderer already had it). Body reads the dashboard-tile context after `isTemporal`. AreaRenderer had no existing mouse handlers, so the wave adds them at the svg level: `style={dashboardTile ? { cursor: "pointer" } : undefined}` for hover affordance + an `onClick` that uses `localPoint(e)` to source the click position in svg coords, subtracts `MARGIN.left` to map into the inner-plot coords that `xPx` uses, clamps to `[0, innerWidth]` for safety, then runs the identical nearest-x scan as LineRenderer — reading from the PRE-stack `series` (not the cumulative `stacked` series; the y values differ but x values are identical, so the lookup is equivalent and pre-stack is the canonical original-data source).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestTrend.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestTrend.test.ts) (new, ~140 LOC). 18 tests across 2 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **LineRenderer cross-filter wiring** (7): imports + context read; dispatch fires inside the existing `onBrushUp` click-treatment branch (regex pins the 6-px guard `if (Math.abs(hi - lo) < 6)` enclosing the dispatch enclosing the `setBrushStart(null)` reset); the nearest-x lookup scans every `series.points` for the minimum |xPx(p.x) - clickX|; the dispatch shape (`column: xCh.field`, `value: toFilterValue(nearest.x)`, `sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId`); two-level gating (outer `if (dashboardTile)` + inner `if (nearest)`).
      - **AreaRenderer cross-filter wiring** (11): imports + context read + `localPoint` import; cursor:pointer gated on `dashboardTile`; svg `onClick` uses `localPoint(e)`; subtracts `MARGIN.left`; clamps to `[0, innerWidth]`; reads from pre-stack `series` (NOT `stacked`); the dispatch shape; nearest-null gate.
      - 18/18 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Inject into `onBrushUp` rather than add a sibling click handler.** LineRenderer already owns `onMouseDown` / `onMouseUp` / `onMouseMove` for brush-zoom. Adding a separate svg `onClick` would either fire DURING a drag (browser fires click on mouseup if no drag occurred, but the line svg's `onMouseUp` and `onClick` would both run, causing a phantom dispatch on zoom interactions) or require its own click-vs-drag tracking. The existing `onBrushUp` already discriminates click-vs-drag via the 6-px threshold — reusing that branch is one anchor point, no duplication.
    - **Dispatch placement: AFTER the 6-px guard, BEFORE the brush-state reset.** The `lo` / `hi` variables capture the recorded brush start/end pixels, which are the click position when treated as a click. Resetting `setBrushStart(null)` before the dispatch would lose the click position; the placement preserves it. Tested by regex shape.
    - **Two-level gating (`if (dashboardTile)` enclosing `if (nearest)`).** The outer guard avoids the O(series × points) scan cost on chat / explorer renderers where the dispatch would be a no-op anyway. The inner guard handles the empty-series edge case (`data: []` or all series filtered out by legend toggles to opacity 0) silently — dispatching `{ value: toFilterValue(undefined) }` would coerce to `"null"` which is the wrong filter target.
    - **AreaRenderer reads pre-stack `series`, not `stacked`.** The two series shape arrays carry the same x values; only the y values differ (`stacked[i].points[j].y` is cumulative, `series[i].points[j].y` is per-series). Since the nearest-x lookup is x-only, both are equivalent. Pre-stack is the cleaner choice because: (a) it's the canonical original-data source; (b) avoids accidentally touching the `_original` field stashed on stacked points; (c) for single-series areas, `stacked` IS `series` (the early-return path), so there's no functional difference at all.
    - **No tooltip dispatch on hover.** Adding cross-filter dispatch on HOVER (rather than click) would make the dashboard brush feel highly responsive but would fire dozens of events per second during mouse-move — flooding `DashboardView`'s `useEffect` queue. Click-only is the right cadence for a filter action; hover effects (highlighting non-matching marks elsewhere) are a separate concern that the "isCrossFilterActive dim-non-matching" follow-on will address.
    - **AreaRenderer svg-level onClick (not per-mark).** A multi-series area renders N `<AreaClosed>` paths stacked on top of each other; attaching the click to one specific path would (a) require deciding which series "owns" the click point (the topmost rendered? the largest at that x?), (b) miss clicks in transparent gaps. The svg-level handler is unambiguous: any click anywhere maps to the nearest x.

  **Verified.** Full server suite 3577/3577 pass (was 3559 pre-this-wave, adding 18). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to WD2-wiring-rest-rect baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `45db68a2`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **WD2-wiring-rest-point.** PointRenderer (scatter) conditional on `colorCh` being non-null — pure quantitative (x, y) scatters have no field to filter on. Next wave.
    - **Hover-state highlight.** The "isCrossFilterActive dim-non-matching marks" UX (per the master plan) is independent of dispatch and is a separate visualisation wave.
    - **Brush-to-range-filter on Line.** A user dragging a range on a time-axis Line chart could install a date-range filter rather than zoom — a future judgment-call wave that needs the dashboard-vs-explorer mode distinction to decide whether to zoom (explorer) or brush (dashboard). Out of scope here.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-wiring-rest-rect · RectRenderer heatmap cells wired to `dispatchCrossFilter`.** WD2-wiring-rest-cat (earlier today) covered the 5 categorical-by-construction visx renderers; RectRenderer (heatmap) was held back as its own atomic wave because of a one-decision question the cat renderers don't face: a heatmap cell sits at the intersection of *two* categorical dims (`rowCh` and `colCh`), and the existing `applyCrossFilter` toggle contract only handles one column at a time. The three options were (a) filter by row only — loses information; (b) filter by column only — same problem; (c) filter by both, sharing a single onClick. This wave ships option (c): the cell `onClick` dispatches TWO `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` events in row-first order. `applyCrossFilter` is pure and event-driven, so back-to-back dispatches each toggle their own column independently. The user sees the row + col filter applied; re-clicking the same cell toggles both back off.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/RectRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/RectRenderer.tsx) — imports `useDashboardTileContext` + `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue`. Body reads `const dashboardTile = useDashboardTileContext()` once after the encoding-resolver throw guard. The two-parallel-`useMemo` pattern (one for `rows`, one for `cols`) widens to a single `useMemo` returning `{ rows, rowRawByKey, cols, colRawByKey }` — one walk over `data`, building both string-keyed domain arrays AND parallel `Map<string, unknown>` raw-value lookups. First row encountered per stringified key sets the raw value; subsequent rows keep it (no overwrite). This mirrors ArcRenderer's `{ value, rawKey }` aggregator pattern from WD2-wiring-rest-cat. The cell `<rect>` gains `style={dashboardTile ? { cursor: "pointer" } : undefined}` and an `onClick` that, when `dashboardTile` is non-null, dispatches `{ column: rowCh.field, value: toFilterValue(rowRawByKey.get(row)), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId }` followed by the same shape with col coordinates. Row-first ordering is pinned by test (`indexOf("column: rowCh.field") < indexOf("column: colCh.field")`).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestRect.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestRect.test.ts) (new, ~110 LOC). 11 tests across 2 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.
      - **RectRenderer cross-filter wiring** (8): imports `useDashboardTileContext` from `@/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext`; imports `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue` from `@/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter`; reads the dashboard-tile context once in the renderer body; sets `cursor: pointer` only when the context is present; dispatches `{ column: rowCh.field, value: toFilterValue(rowRawByKey.get(row)), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId }`; dispatches `{ column: colCh.field, value: toFilterValue(colRawByKey.get(col)), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId }`; the row dispatch precedes the col dispatch (via `indexOf` on the inner anchor, NOT a regex on the outer dispatch — `String#search` returns the start of the OVERALL match so a regex starting at `dispatchCrossFilter\\(\\{` would yield the same index for both); the dispatch is gated on `dashboardTile` being non-null.
      - **Raw row/col values are preserved** (3): the inner reducer builds `rRaw` + `cRaw` as `Map<string, unknown>`; first row encountered per stringified key sets the raw value (no overwrite); the useMemo returns the canonical `{ rows, rowRawByKey, cols, colRawByKey }` object shape.
      - 11/11 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Two events, not a compound event.** `applyCrossFilter` is the existing single-column toggle in WD2's pure-helper layer; widening it to accept compound `(col, val)` pairs would either (a) require a new event shape that breaks the WD2-wiring-bar / WD2-wiring-rest-cat contracts, or (b) add an array variant to `CrossFilterEvent` that every existing renderer would also need to handle. Dispatching twice keeps the existing contract intact; the cost is two synchronous DOM events instead of one, which has no measurable user impact. The toggle semantics still reverse correctly on re-click because each event is independent: removing the row filter on event 1 leaves the col filter unchanged, then event 2 removes the col filter.
    - **Row-first ordering pinned by test.** The semantics work regardless of order — both filters install, both reverse correctly on re-click — but pinning the order keeps test debugging deterministic and matches the user's reading order (rows are the y-axis, scanned left-to-right). A future maintainer reordering the dispatches gets a clear test signal rather than a subtle off-by-one in DashboardView's effect ordering.
    - **Raw-value preservation alongside the stringified domain.** Same fix as ArcRenderer / BoxRenderer / WaterfallRenderer / ComboRenderer / FunnelRenderer (WD2-wiring-rest-cat). The two parallel `useMemo` blocks for `rows` and `cols` collapsed to a single walk over `data` that builds both the string-keyed domains AND the raw-value lookups — one pass instead of two, and the lookups make the dispatch's raw-value retrieval `O(1)` rather than a re-scan of `data`.
    - **`<title>` element stays unchanged.** SVG `<title>` is the accessible tooltip; the existing `{row} · {col}: {formatChartValue(v, valCh.field)}` text is fine and doesn't fight the click handler. Some tooltip libraries (`react-tooltip`, `@radix-ui/react-tooltip`) intercept click before `<title>` triggers, but the native SVG `<title>` doesn't — the user gets both the tooltip on hover AND the click dispatch.
    - **Test uses `indexOf` instead of regex `search`.** `String#search(re)` returns the start of the OVERALL match. The natural regex `/dispatchCrossFilter\\(\\{[\\s\\S]*?column: rowCh\\.field/` would return the position of `dispatchCrossFilter`, not the position of `column: rowCh.field` — and both row and col anchors share the same `dispatchCrossFilter` literal at the same position, so both searches yield the same index and the ordering test would always be `false`. Using `indexOf("column: rowCh.field")` returns the position of the unique inner anchor directly. Documented in the test's comment so future-Claude doesn't reintroduce the regex bug when widening the test (this was a one-iteration bug the wave caught).

  **Tests.** New file [`client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestRect.test.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestRect.test.ts) — 11 tests across 2 suites. Appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4.

  **Verified.** Full server suite 3559/3559 pass (was 3548 pre-this-wave, adding 11). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to WD2-wiring-rest-cat baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `a657e3b6`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **WD2-wiring-rest-trend.** LineRenderer + AreaRenderer with nearest-x lookup + brush-zoom click-vs-drag guard. Next wave.
    - **WD2-wiring-rest-point.** PointRenderer conditional on `colorCh`. Follow-on wave.
    - **Compound `CrossFilterEvent` shape.** Widening `CrossFilterEvent` to carry an array of `{ column, value }` pairs (so heatmaps and other multi-dim brushes can fire one logical event instead of two) is a possible future refactor if drill-through (WD3) needs to know "these filters were brushed atomically". Deferred until the use case appears.
    - **Highlight (vs filter) on cell hover.** Some heatmaps brush by highlighting matching cells in OTHER tiles instead of filtering the underlying data. That's the master plan's "separate `brushFilters` layer" idea (see WD2-wiring-bar Out of scope). Not added here.

- **2026-05-19** — **Wave WD2-wiring-rest-cat · 5 categorical visx renderers wired to `dispatchCrossFilter`.** WD2-wiring-bar (yesterday) proved the chart-mark-click → `dispatchCrossFilter` → window `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` → `DashboardView` `useEffect` → `setGlobalFilters((g) => applyCrossFilter(g, detail))` round-trip on BarRenderer alone. The brief flagged "the same three-line addition" across the remaining 12 visx renderers as `WD2-wiring-rest`, but the on-the-wire audit found that BarRenderer was the *only* renderer with a pre-existing categorical-mark `onClick`; every other renderer needs the click handler added from scratch. Splitting the remaining 12 by structure: 5 are categorical-by-construction (Arc / Funnel / Box / Waterfall / Combo) — each iterates discrete marks per category with the field name already known via `enc.x.field` (or `labelCh.field`), so wiring them is mechanical. Rect (heatmap) needs a one-vs-two-dim filter decision. Line / Area need a nearest-x lookup that also respects the brush-zoom click-vs-drag distinction. Point only fires meaningfully when `colorCh` is present. KPI / Radar / Regression have no meaningful categorical click target. This wave ships the first slice — the 5 categorical-by-construction renderers — keeping each wave atomic.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ArcRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ArcRenderer.tsx). `Slice` type widens to carry `rawKey: unknown` alongside the stringified `key`. The aggregation map widens from `Map<string, number>` to `Map<string, { value: number; rawKey: unknown }>` so the first row's type-original category value survives the per-key reduction (subsequent rows merge into the same slice). Renderer body reads `const dashboardTile = useDashboardTileContext()` once after the `inner` radius computation. The pie `<path>` per arc gains `style={dashboardTile ? { cursor: "pointer" } : undefined}` and an `onClick` that fires `dispatchCrossFilter({ column: labelCh.field, value: toFilterValue(arc.data.rawKey), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId })` when the context is non-null.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/FunnelRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/FunnelRenderer.tsx). Stages now carry `rawLabel: enc.x.accessor(r)` alongside the stringified `label` — funnel stages are one-row-per-stage, no aggregation, so raw preservation is a single-line addition in the `stages` `useMemo`. `dashboardTile` read once after the inner-dim computation. The stage `<rect>` gains cursor + `onClick` dispatching `{ column: enc.x.field, value: toFilterValue(s.rawLabel), sourceTileId }`.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BoxRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BoxRenderer.tsx). `BoxStats` widens to carry `rawCategory: unknown`. `groupBy(data, [enc.x.field])` returns string-keyed groups, but the raw value is recoverable from `rows[0]?.[enc.x.field]` — one-line addition in the stats `useMemo`. The box `<rect>` (whiskers + median lines stay non-interactive — they're decorations of the box, not separate marks) gains cursor + `onClick` dispatching `{ column: enc.x.field, value: toFilterValue(s.rawCategory), sourceTileId }`.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/WaterfallRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/WaterfallRenderer.tsx). `WaterfallBar` widens to carry `rawCategory: unknown` and the `bars` `useMemo` captures `enc.x.accessor(r)` before the `asString` coercion. Unique to waterfall: an intermediate `const clickable = dashboardTile && !b.isTotal;` gates the dispatch — running-total bars (`b.isTotal === true`) render as full-height bars from zero but are synthetic summary rows, not a category the user can filter to. Cursor + `onClick` follow `clickable`, not `dashboardTile`.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ComboRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/ComboRenderer.tsx). The bars iterate `data.map((row, i))` with `xCh.accessor(row)` available inline — no new type field needed. The variable rename `const rawX = xCh.accessor(row); const xRaw = asString(rawX);` keeps both the raw value (for dispatch) and the stringified value (for the band scale lookup) named clearly. `dashboardTile` read after the `throw new Error("combo mark requires x, y, and y2 encodings")` guard. The bars `<Bar>` gains cursor + `onClick` dispatching `{ column: xCh.field, value: toFilterValue(rawX), sourceTileId }`. The secondary-axis line (`<LinePath>` at the bottom of the bars render) stays click-inert — clicking on a continuous line doesn't have an unambiguous categorical filter target. The bar mark is the categorical handle for the combo chart.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestCat.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestCat.test.ts) (new, ~180 LOC). 36 tests across 7 suites. Pattern: a `RendererPin` table names per-renderer `columnExpr` (the field expression that lands in `column:`), `rawValueExpr` (the raw-value expression passed to `toFilterValue`), and `clickGate` (the predicate expression that fires the dispatch — `dashboardTile` for 4 of 5; `clickable` for Waterfall, which adds the `!b.isTotal` clause). For each renderer the suite source-inspects: imports `useDashboardTileContext` from the new module + `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue` from `crossFilter.ts`; reads the dashboard-tile context once in the renderer body; dispatches `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` with `{ column: <columnExpr>, value: toFilterValue(<rawValueExpr>), sourceTileId: dashboardTile[!]?.tileId }` (the optional `!` accommodates Waterfall's `dashboardTile!.tileId` inside the `clickable` guard since TS doesn't narrow `dashboardTile` through `&&`); the dispatch is gated on the per-renderer `clickGate` predicate (chat / explorer no-op invariant); `style={<clickGate> ? { cursor: "pointer" } : undefined}` on the mark. A separate suite (`WaterfallRenderer skips totals`) pins `const clickable = dashboardTile && !b.isTotal;`. A final suite (`raw category values are preserved on every renderer`) pins the type-original value capture per renderer. The file is appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit test list per invariant #4.
    - [server/package.json](../server/package.json) — one-line test-list extension appending `../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestCat.test.ts` to the end of the explicit `test` script.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Categorical-by-construction first.** The Arc / Funnel / Box / Waterfall / Combo renderers all iterate discrete categorical marks with the x-axis field name already in scope via `enc.x.field` (or `labelCh.field` for the pie's category-comes-from-x-or-color resolution). Wiring is mechanical: one import block, one context read, one raw-value preservation, one onClick. Five renderers in one wave is reviewable because the pattern is byte-stable across them. Line / Area / Combo-line / Rect each have their own structural quirk (nearest-x lookup, brush-zoom interaction, two-dim filter decision); shipping those in this wave would mix the mechanical change with judgment calls and obscure both. Splitting per structure keeps the next 2–3 waves atomic.
    - **Raw-value preservation alongside the stringified key.** `applyCrossFilter`'s predicate compares values with strict equality after `toFilterValue` coercion. If the renderers passed only the stringified category to `dispatchCrossFilter`, then chart-mark clicks on numeric / Date categories would coerce to strings TWICE — once in the renderer aggregator (`asString`), once in `toFilterValue` — and the round-trip would lose type information. Preserving the raw value at aggregation time and letting `toFilterValue` do the single canonical coercion downstream mirrors BarRenderer's WD2-wiring-bar audit-fix (`outerRaw: unknown` on `BarCell`). The same fix applied here keeps the cross-filter predicate consistent across renderers.
    - **WaterfallRenderer total-row skip is structural, not optional.** A waterfall's "total" rows are running cumulative sums (or hand-marked summary bars via `r.total === true` / `r.isTotal === true`) — they're not data points, they're a derived visual. Clicking one and dispatching `{ column: "category", value: "Net Total" }` would filter the underlying data to rows whose category column equals the literal string `"Net Total"`, which almost certainly doesn't exist as a row. The intermediate `clickable` local makes the skip explicit and self-documenting at the call site; the alternative (a runtime check inside the onClick) would dispatch the click on accident if a future maintainer dropped the guard. The test pins the exact phrasing so future Claude doesn't accidentally remove it.
    - **`dashboardTile!.tileId` inside the `clickable` guard.** TypeScript's narrowing through a `const clickable = dashboardTile && !b.isTotal;` pattern doesn't propagate to the onClick lambda — the lambda captures `dashboardTile` independently and the compiler can't prove the narrowing still holds. Writing `dashboardTile!.tileId` once inside the gated lambda is cleaner than restructuring the guard around an early `if (!dashboardTile) return null;` (which would skip the bar entirely from the render tree, breaking the visual). The non-null assertion is genuinely safe because `clickable` already encoded the predicate.
    - **Each renderer's `onClick` is a fresh closure per render.** No `useCallback`. The cells / stages / slices arrays are recomputed every render anyway (driven by `useMemo` on `data`), and React's reconciler is happy with a fresh `onClick` per node. Memoising onClick would require either threading every closure variable through a `useCallback` deps array per renderer or hoisting the handler to a stable curried form — both add complexity for no measurable perf win on the small number of marks dashboard tiles render (≤100 typical). The BarRenderer wiring made the same call.
    - **No `useChartGrid` for these renderers.** BarRenderer participates in both the in-context `<ChartGrid>` filter (chat explorer multi-chart cross-filter) AND the new dashboard-tile dispatch — that's why its `interactive` flag widens to `grid.inGrid || !!dashboardTile`. The other 5 renderers in this wave don't currently consume `useChartGrid()`. Wiring them to `<ChartGrid>` too would be a separate concern (the audit recommendation for "do we wire the grid in here as well?"). This wave deliberately limits scope to the dashboard-tile dispatch path; the chat-explorer cross-filter integration for these renderers is a follow-on if the user contract is enforced (currently only BarRenderer offers the in-context cross-filter in the chat explorer).

  **Tests.** New file [`client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestCat.test.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/wd2WiringRestCat.test.ts) — 36 tests across 7 suites (5 renderer-source-inspection suites of 6 tests each = 30, plus the Waterfall-skip-totals suite of 1, plus the raw-value-preservation suite of 5). Appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit `test` list per invariant #4. Behaviour-level integration round-trip stays pinned by `dashboardTileContext.test.ts` (BarRenderer); the other four marks share the byte-stable dispatch shape, so source-level pins cover the wiring invariants without a per-renderer DOM test.

  **Verified.** Full server suite 3548/3548 pass (was 3512 pre-W60 / WI2-server, adding 36 new tests). `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to WD2-wiring-bar baseline — zero new from this wave. Code commit `df558daa`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **WD2-wiring-rest-rect.** RectRenderer (heatmap) has two categorical axes (`rowCh.field` and `colCh.field`); deciding whether a cell click filters by row, column, or both (and how to expose a compound filter through the existing `applyCrossFilter` toggle contract) is a one-decision wave on its own. Defers cleanly.
    - **WD2-wiring-rest-trend.** LineRenderer and AreaRenderer don't have per-mark click targets — they render continuous paths. The dispatch needs a nearest-x lookup (reuse the existing tooltip's nearest-x state) plus a brush-zoom guard (LineRenderer's existing 6-px minimum-drag threshold for `onBrushUp` distinguishes click-vs-drag). Each touches more code than the cat-renderers' 3-line addition. Next wave.
    - **WD2-wiring-rest-point.** PointRenderer (scatter) only has a meaningful categorical click target when `colorCh` is non-null — pure quantitative (x, y) scatters have no field to filter on. Conditional dispatch wires neatly but is its own short wave.
    - **KpiRenderer, RadarRenderer, RegressionRenderer.** No meaningful categorical click target: KPI is a single big number + sparkline; Radar's polygons cover all spokes for one series; Regression is pure quantitative x/y scatter. Deliberately skipped; documented here so a future Claude doesn't reopen the question.
    - **ECharts specialty pack.** Treemap, sunburst, sankey, parallel, calendar, candlestick, choropleth, gauge use a different click-event shape; `WD2-wiring-echarts` is a separate adapter wave.
    - **`isCrossFilterActive` dim-non-matching mark rendering.** The brushed-state visualisation (active filter dims the non-matching marks rather than removing them, per the master plan UX) is still unwired everywhere except the BarRenderer audit-fix `isFiltered` predicate that consults the ChartGrid context. Threading `useDashboardCrossFilters()` into each renderer for the dim mask is a separate visualisation wave; this wave focused on the dispatch path.
    - **`sourceTileId` consumption in DashboardView.** Same as WD2-wiring-bar — the dispatched event carries `sourceTileId`, but the current `DashboardView` effect only reads `column` + `value`. Wired for future use ("dim non-matching marks on the originating tile too"); out of scope.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WD2-wiring-bar · BarRenderer cross-filter wiring proof.** WD2 (shipped earlier today) gave us the pure helpers (`applyCrossFilter`, `dispatchCrossFilter`, `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT`, `toFilterValue`) for the chart-mark-click → `globalFilters` toggle, but the helpers had no caller. The full WD2-wiring scope touches 13 visx renderers + the ECharts adapter + `DashboardView` — too much for one atomic wave on the chart-rendering surface (god-object-adjacent ChartRenderer is in this area). WD2-wiring-bar is the smaller proof-of-wiring atomic the master plan called out: validate the chart-mark-click → `dispatchCrossFilter` → window `CustomEvent` → `DashboardView` `useEffect` → `setGlobalFilters((g) => applyCrossFilter(g, detail))` round-trip on BarRenderer alone. The remaining 12 visx renderers + ECharts adapter follow as `WD2-wiring-rest` once this pattern is validated under live use.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.tsx) (new, ~45 LOC). A React context that the dashboard tile wraps around its chart body so any descendant renderer can identify *which tile* a click originated from. Three exports: `DashboardTileProvider` (memoises `{ tileId }` value), `useDashboardTileContext()` (returns the context value or `null` outside a provider — explicitly NOT a no-op shim, because the renderer's WD2 branch must consciously opt in on a non-null), and `DashboardTileContext` (the raw `React.Context<DashboardTileContextValue | null>` for tests). Default context value is `null` — chat / explorer / share-preview renderers fall through cleanly with no dispatch path.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/ChartTileBody.tsx) — wraps the existing inner branch (`effectiveMode === "pivot" ? <ChartTilePivotView …> : <ErrorBoundary><Suspense><ChartShim …/></Suspense></ErrorBoundary>`) in `<DashboardTileProvider tileId={tile.id}> … </DashboardTileProvider>`. Both the pivot view AND the chart-shim (which routes to PremiumChart-v2 or legacy ChartRenderer per the WC9.3 feature-flag shim) inherit the context. Two-line edit: one import, one provider tag pair.
    - [client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/BarRenderer.tsx) — imports `useDashboardTileContext` from the new module + `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue` from the WD2 helper [`crossFilter.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts). Body reads `const dashboardTile = useDashboardTileContext()` once. The existing `interactive` flag widens from `grid.inGrid` to `grid.inGrid || !!dashboardTile`, so the cursor pointer + click handler now light up when the renderer is inside a dashboard tile. The bar `onClick` runs both paths independently: `grid.toggleFilter({ field, value })` when inside a ChartGrid (chat / explorer multi-chart context preserved unchanged), AND `dispatchCrossFilter({ column: enc.x.field, value: toFilterValue(c.outerRaw), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId })` when inside a dashboard tile. The two paths are deliberately independent — the ChartGrid context manages an in-context single-(field, value) filter for its own children; the WD2 path bubbles a CustomEvent up to `DashboardView`. Either path can fire alone; both fire together if the bar is rendered inside BOTH a ChartGrid AND a dashboard tile (rare / future composition).
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardView.tsx](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/DashboardView.tsx) — imports `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT`, `applyCrossFilter`, and `CrossFilterEvent` from `../lib/crossFilter`. New `useEffect` right after the existing `DR4` captured-filter seed effect: `typeof window === 'undefined'` SSR guard returns early; attaches a `window.addEventListener(CROSS_FILTER_EVENT, handler)` whose handler casts `event` to `CustomEvent<CrossFilterEvent>`, filters malformed payloads (`!detail || typeof detail.column !== 'string'`), and dispatches `setGlobalFilters((prev) => applyCrossFilter(prev, detail))`. The toggle / append / replace semantics live entirely in `applyCrossFilter` — the effect is a thin pipe. Cleanup `removeEventListener` runs on unmount. The `[]` dependency array is correct because `setGlobalFilters` is stable across renders (it's a React state setter); `applyCrossFilter` is a pure module-scope function, not a captured closure.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts) — `toFilterValue` widened from `(raw: string | number | boolean | null | undefined): string` to `(raw: unknown): string`. Chart-mark values flow as `unknown` from the renderers' typed `BarCell.outerRaw` field, and asking every caller to narrow first creates friction. Runtime behavior is unchanged for the existing accepted types; `null` / `undefined` → `"null"` (matches the upstream `(null)` key normalisation in `breakdownRankingTool`); strings pass through; numbers / booleans go through `String(v)`; `Date` instances coerce to ISO (new branch — chart temporal axes deliver these); everything else falls back to `String(v)`. The 29 existing WD2 tests pin the narrower input types and stay green — the type signature is wider, the runtime behavior is identical for those inputs.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.test.ts](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext.test.ts) (new, ~155 LOC). 18 tests across 5 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit test list (the client tests run under the server test harness) per invariant #4:
      - **`dashboardTileContext` module shape** (4): exports `DashboardTileProvider`, `useDashboardTileContext`, `DashboardTileContext`; default context value is `null`; provider memoises the `{ tileId }` value with `useMemo`; the accessor returns the raw `useContext(Ctx)` result (no fallback shim, so consumers MUST branch on null).
      - **BarRenderer cross-filter wiring** (6): imports `useDashboardTileContext` from `@/pages/Dashboard/lib/dashboardTileContext`; imports `dispatchCrossFilter` + `toFilterValue` from `@/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter`; reads the dashboard-tile context at the top of the renderer body; `interactive` flag widens to `grid.inGrid || !!dashboardTile`; onClick dispatches `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` with `{ column: enc.x.field, value: toFilterValue(c.outerRaw), sourceTileId: dashboardTile.tileId }` when in a dashboard tile; the existing `grid.toggleFilter` path is preserved when in a ChartGrid.
      - **ChartTileBody provider wrap** (2): imports `DashboardTileProvider` from `../lib/dashboardTileContext`; wraps the chart body in `<DashboardTileProvider tileId={tile.id}>` with a closing tag.
      - **DashboardView subscription** (6): imports `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` + `applyCrossFilter` from `../lib/crossFilter`; attaches a `window.addEventListener(CROSS_FILTER_EVENT, handler as EventListener)` inside a `useEffect`; detaches on cleanup; dispatches `setGlobalFilters((prev) => applyCrossFilter(prev, detail))`; ignores malformed events (`!detail || typeof detail.column !== 'string'`); guards on `typeof window === 'undefined'` for SSR safety.
      - 18/18 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Context, not props.** `PremiumChart` is a generic dispatcher with a fixed `VisxRendererProps` shape (`{ spec, data, width, height, ariaLabel? }`). Threading `sourceTileId` through every renderer would (a) widen the dispatcher's prop shape, (b) require touching every renderer in this single wave, (c) re-litigate the "what props are universal" question that PremiumChart already settled. A small React context that the tile body wraps the dispatcher in keeps the dispatcher's prop shape stable and makes BarRenderer's wiring a 3-line addition. Future WD2-wiring-rest waves each get a similarly thin addition (`useDashboardTileContext` + `dispatchCrossFilter` + a one-line onClick branch).
    - **`useDashboardTileContext` returns `null` outside a provider — no fallback shim.** The existing ChartGrid context's `useChartGrid()` returns a no-op shim (`{ filter: null, setFilter: () => {}, toggleFilter: () => {}, applyFilter: rows => rows, inGrid: false }`) because every consumer's code path calls those methods unconditionally and needs them to be safe. The dashboard-tile context is the opposite shape: consumers check `!!dashboardTile` to decide whether to dispatch the event at all. A no-op shim with a dummy `tileId: ""` would be semantically wrong — dispatching `sourceTileId: ""` to `DashboardView` from a chat-side renderer would pollute the brushed-filter telemetry. Returning null forces the caller to consciously opt in on a non-null.
    - **The two click paths (`grid.toggleFilter` + `dispatchCrossFilter`) are independent on purpose.** They serve different consumers: `ChartGrid` is the explorer's multi-chart in-context filter (user clicks Region=North in one chart, the OTHER chart's rows reduce to North); `globalFilters` is the dashboard-wide filter bar (user clicks Region=North in tile A, tile B re-renders with Region=North applied). The user contract of each is different and the storage shapes are different (`ChartGrid` is a single (field, value), `globalFilters` is `Record<column, ChartFilterSelection>`). Don't unify; let both fire when the renderer is inside both containers.
    - **`toFilterValue(unknown)` is purely additive.** The narrower signature was overly conservative — chart-mark values flow as `unknown` from typed renderer internals, so every renderer wiring would have to narrow first if `toFilterValue` insisted on a narrow input. Widening the signature has no runtime cost (the function already used `typeof` checks internally) and reduces the surface every WD2-wiring-rest renderer must thread.
    - **Wave shape mirrors W59a → W59b → W60 and WD2 → WD2-wiring-bar.** Each split lands a pure helper first (WD2's `crossFilter.ts`), then a thin call-site that wires the helper into one consumer (WD2-wiring-bar on BarRenderer). The thin-wiring waves stay reviewable; if a wiring decision turns out wrong (e.g. the `interactive` flag should ALSO consult an env flag) we change one line in one file, not 13.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 server / 53 client errors, identical to WI2-server / W60 baseline — zero new from WD2-wiring-bar. 18/18 new tests pass + 29/29 existing WD2 tests stay green after the `toFilterValue` widen. Full server suite 3512/3512 pass. Code commit `ffc15f54`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **The remaining 12 visx renderers** ([`LineRenderer`](../client/src/lib/charts/visxRenderers/LineRenderer.tsx), `PointRenderer`, `AreaRenderer`, `ArcRenderer`, `FunnelRenderer`, `KpiRenderer`, `ComboRenderer`, `BoxRenderer`, `RectRenderer`, `RadarRenderer`, `RegressionRenderer`, `WaterfallRenderer`). Each gets the same three-line addition once this BarRenderer pattern is validated under live use. Ship as `WD2-wiring-rest` (one wave, mechanical changes across files).
    - **ECharts adapter wiring.** The ECharts specialty renderers (treemap, sunburst, sankey, parallel, calendar, candlestick, choropleth, gauge) go through a different click-handling path; `WD2-wiring-echarts` is its own follow-on. The CustomEvent dispatch contract is the same — only the renderer-side hook differs.
    - **`isCrossFilterActive` highlight rendering.** Once cross-filtered, BarRenderer could dim non-matching bars (the master plan's "filtered tiles dim non-matching marks instead of removing them" UX). The hook is in place (`isCrossFilterActive(globalFilters, column, value)` reads `globalFilters` from somewhere — currently nothing reads it inside BarRenderer). A follow-on wave can thread a `dimSelector` prop or another context. Out of WD2-wiring-bar scope; the brush dispatch is the load-bearing piece this wave validates.
    - **Brush onto a date / numeric column.** WD2's contract is that brushes are discrete-value clicks; a click on a bar in a time-axis chart will fire `dispatchCrossFilter({ column: <date column>, value: <ISO string>, … })` and `applyCrossFilter` will REPLACE any existing date / numeric selection with a fresh categorical selection. That's intentional per WD2's semantics, but a future wave may want a smarter "click on a time bucket adds a date-range filter" path. Out of scope; the current behaviour is documented in WD2's contract and the 29 helper tests pin it.
    - **`sourceTileId` consumption in DashboardView.** The dispatched event carries `sourceTileId` but `DashboardView`'s current effect only reads `column` + `value`. The originating-tile hint is wired for future use (e.g. "dim non-matching marks on the originating tile too" vs. "leave the source tile uncrushed"). Out of scope; the field is in the contract so future waves can read it without bumping the schema.
    - **`DashboardView` global vs per-tile filter routing.** Brushed filters currently land in `globalFilters` — the same lane WD1's `+ Add filter` popover writes to. A future wave may route brushes to a separate `brushFilters` layer per the master plan ("a separate `brushFilters` layer that highlights without filtering, toggleable per tile"). Out of WD2-wiring-bar scope.
    - **WD3 drill-through hook.** Out of WD2 scope entirely; separate wave map.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WI2-server · POST /api/insight/regen endpoint.** WI2-cache (shipped earlier today) introduced the client-side LRU + TTL cache that stores per-tile regeneration results keyed by `(tileId, hashGlobalFilters(filters))` — but with no server endpoint to populate it on cache miss, the cache was inert: a contract-only artifact. WI2-server is the matching network surface. The future WI2-wire hook in [`TileInsightFooter.tsx`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx) will call this endpoint when `cache.get(buildCacheKey(...))` returns `undefined`, then merge the response straight into the cache via `cache.set(key, response)` — the response shape matches `InsightRegenEntry` ([`insightRegenCache.ts`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/insightRegenCache.ts) line 42) verbatim, so the client doesn't need a transformation step. Single MINI-tier LLM call wrapped in deterministic pre/post helpers so tests can pin the prompt + post-processing without spinning a real model.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/insightRegen.ts](../server/lib/insightRegen.ts) (new, ~380 LOC). Five small pure helpers + one network boundary:
      - `regenInsightRequestSchema` (strict zod): `{ tileId: string ≤120; spec: { type, title?, x, y, seriesColumn?, aggregate? }; filteredData: Array<Record<string|number|boolean|null>> ≤5000 rows; domainContext?: string ≤8 KB; datasetContextHint?: string ≤400 chars }`. `.strict()` on the outer shape AND on `spec` rejects extra keys the planner can't have meant — request bodies are the network boundary, fail loud.
      - `regenInsightResponseSchema` (strict zod): `{ text: 1..1200 chars; citations?: string[] ≤20; regeneratedAt: string ≤40; confidenceTier: "low" | "medium" | "high" }`. Matches `InsightRegenEntry` byte-for-byte except for the schema-side validations.
      - `summarizeFilteredData(rows, { x, y }): FilteredDataSummary` — deterministic statistical anchors. Walks the rows once and emits `{ rowCount, topRow: { x, y } | null, bottomRow: { x, y } | null, mean: number | null, xValuesPreview: string[] (first 6 distinct, encountered order) }`. `toNumberOrNull` coerces percent / comma-formatted strings (e.g. `"1,200"` → `1200`, `"85%"` → `85`); non-numeric y-cells are skipped without poisoning the mean. `toLabel(null)` renders `"(null)"` matching the upstream null-bucket convention.
      - `inferConfidenceTier(rowCount): "low" | "medium" | "high"` — mirrors WQ1's tier vocabulary: `<10 → low`, `<100 → medium`, `≥100 → high`. The 5000-row request cap bounds the upper end.
      - `extractInsightCitations(text): string[]` — mirrors W22's `CITATION_TOKEN_RE` ([`checkEnvelopeCompleteness.ts`](../server/lib/agents/runtime/checkEnvelopeCompleteness.ts) line 120) byte-for-byte: `/\`([a-z][a-z0-9-]{4,})\`/g` + hyphen-rule filter (`!tok.includes("-") → drop`), so generic backtick spans like `revenue` aren't false-positives. Dedupes preserving first occurrence.
      - `buildInsightRegenPrompt(args): { system, user }` — composes the LLM input pair. System prompt is byte-stable (persona: "analytical insight summariser"; output contract: 1–3 sentences plain markdown, cite pack ids only when DOMAIN CONTEXT names them, no bullet lists, under 600 chars). User prompt embeds the chart spec coordinates + deterministic stat anchors + optional DATASET CONTEXT / DOMAIN CONTEXT blocks. Empty / whitespace context strings emit nothing — the conditional block keeps prompt bytes tight for tiles without a domain pack.
      - `regenInsightForFilteredView(request, opts?): Promise<RegenInsightResponse>` — the network boundary. `summarizeFilteredData` → `buildInsightRegenPrompt` → single `callLlm` under `LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_REGEN` (the new MINI-tier purpose) → post-process: `normaliseInsightText` strips leading `>` blockquote markers a chatty model might emit, collapses repeated whitespace, caps at 1200 chars; `extractInsightCitations` mines pack tokens; `inferConfidenceTier` reads the row count; falls back to `"Not enough signal in the current slice…"` when the model returns empty content.
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/llmCallPurpose.ts](../server/lib/agents/runtime/llmCallPurpose.ts) gains `LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_REGEN = "insight_regen"` + `[LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_REGEN]: "MINI"` in `PURPOSE_TO_CATEGORY`. MINI tier is the right call: the prompt's job is to render anchors `summarizeFilteredData` already computed, not to reason about the dataset.
    - [server/routes/insightRegen.ts](../server/routes/insightRegen.ts) (new, ~60 LOC). `POST /api/insight/regen` handler — auth-gated via `getAuthenticatedEmail` (401 on missing), `regenInsightRequestSchema.safeParse(req.body)` (400 with flattened zod details on failure), `regenInsightForFilteredView(parsed.data)` → 200 JSON; 500 with telemetry on exception path. Both success + error paths emit `agentLog("insight_regen.done" | "insight_regen.error", ...)` so production observability is on by default.
    - [server/routes/index.ts](../server/routes/index.ts) — import + `app.use('/api', insightRegenRoutes)`.
    - [server/tests/helpers/llmStub.ts](../server/tests/helpers/llmStub.ts) — added a default handler for `LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_REGEN` that returns a plain string (`"Stub insight regen — no detail."`), so any unrelated test that touches the agent loop via the stub doesn't blow up when the regen path is ever invoked indirectly. The stub harness already passes strings through verbatim (no JSON-wrap) so this matches the production response shape.
    - [server/tests/llmRoutingRegression.test.ts](../server/tests/llmRoutingRegression.test.ts) — added `[LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_REGEN]: "MINI"` to the W3.11 routing-regression `EXPECTED_CATEGORY` table so the "every LLM_PURPOSE has a category assertion" guard stays green.
    - [server/tests/insightRegenWI2Server.test.ts](../server/tests/insightRegenWI2Server.test.ts) (new, ~460 LOC). 36 tests across 8 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit list per invariant #4:
      - **Request schema validity** (6): minimal `{ tileId, spec, filteredData: [] }`; full shape with domain + dataset context; empty tileId rejected; extra top-level keys rejected (strict); `filteredData.length > 5000` rejected; spec missing required `x`/`y` rejected.
      - **Response schema validity** (3): full response; response without `citations`; invalid `confidenceTier` rejected.
      - **`summarizeFilteredData`** (6): empty input zero summary; top / bottom / mean over 4-row sample; distinct x-values capped at 6 in encountered order; percent / comma string coercion (`"1,200"` → 1200, `"85%"` → 85); non-numeric y skipped without poisoning the mean; null x → `"(null)"`.
      - **`inferConfidenceTier`** (3): low at 0 + 9; medium at 10 + 99; high at 100 + 5000.
      - **`extractInsightCitations`** (4): valid backticked snake-case-with-hyphens tokens extracted; backticked tokens without a hyphen rejected; duplicate citations deduped first-occurrence; empty / whitespace input returns `[]`.
      - **`buildInsightRegenPrompt`** (6): byte-stable system + user prompts across calls with identical input; user block names chart spec coordinates verbatim (`- type: bar`, `- x: region`, `- y: revenue`, `- title: …`); user block embeds the deterministic summary anchors (`rowCount`, `top:`, `bottom:`); DOMAIN CONTEXT block emitted only when populated; DATASET CONTEXT block emitted only when populated; whitespace-only context strings skipped.
      - **`regenInsightForFilteredView` through `__setLlmStubResolver`** (3): full happy path returns model output + citations + tier + ISO timestamp (asserts `opts.purpose === LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_REGEN` AND `params.messages[0].content` matches the system-prompt anchor); empty model content fallback produces the safe-prose default with no citations; 150-row input yields `confidenceTier: "high"`.
      - **Route + purpose source-inspection** (5): `routes/insightRegen.ts` registers POST `/insight/regen` via `insightRegenController`; uses `regenInsightRequestSchema.safeParse(req.body)` for body validation; gates on `getAuthenticatedEmail(req)`; `routes/index.ts` imports + mounts `insightRegenRoutes` under `/api`; `llmCallPurpose.ts` declares `INSIGHT_REGEN` mapped to MINI category.
      - 36/36 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Single MINI call, deterministic anchors.** The user clicks "✦ Re-explain this view" on a dashboard tile expecting a 1–3 sentence narration of the slice — not a multi-turn investigation. The deterministic anchors from `summarizeFilteredData` carry the load (top / bottom / mean / row count + distinct x-values); the LLM just renders them in prose. MINI tier handles this well; PRIMARY would be 10× the cost for no quality lift.
    - **Pure helpers first, network boundary last.** Five of the six exports are pure functions with no I/O: schemas, `summarizeFilteredData`, `inferConfidenceTier`, `extractInsightCitations`, `buildInsightRegenPrompt`. Only `regenInsightForFilteredView` touches `callLlm`. Tests cover each pure helper directly without spinning real LLM calls; the stub-resolver path tests the wiring + post-processing without leaving Node. This is the same pattern WI2-cache shipped with (pure cache helpers shipped before the network surface) and it keeps both surfaces atomically reviewable.
    - **Response shape matches `InsightRegenEntry`.** The client cache stores `{ text, citations?, regeneratedAt?, confidenceTier? }`. The endpoint returns `{ text, citations?, regeneratedAt, confidenceTier }` — same field names, response makes `regeneratedAt` + `confidenceTier` non-optional. The future WI2-wire hook will call `cache.set(buildCacheKey(tileId, hashGlobalFilters(filters)), response)` with no transformation.
