Designing the response shape FROM the cache shape (rather than the other way around) keeps the contract tight.
    - **No `promptCacheEligibility` wiring (yet).** The master plan's WI2-server note mentions reusing `promptCacheEligibility` to share the system prompt across tiles in the same session. Inspecting the server tree shows no `promptCacheEligibility.ts` source file (only a test fixture name); the prompt-caching path Anthropic exposes via `cache_control` markers isn't yet plumbed through `callLlm` for non-agentic surfaces. Skipping the explicit cache wiring keeps the wave atomic; the byte-stable system prompt naturally benefits from any future caching layer that hashes on `messages[].content`. Out-of-scope footnote below.
    - **Auth gate via the existing `getAuthenticatedEmail` helper.** Mirrors every other write route on this server (`feedbackController.ts`, `dataOpsController.ts`, etc.). 401 on missing email, 400 on schema fail, 500 on regen failure with telemetry-only error body (no internal stack leakage to the client).
    - **`installLlmStub` default handler returns a plain string.** The W18 stub harness passes strings through verbatim — the regen path expects `choices[0].message.content` as plain text, not JSON. Earlier handlers in the default map return objects which the stub `JSON.stringify`s; the regen handler is the second plain-string entry (after the prose-style ones). The W18 default-handlers-coverage test now passes because the new purpose has a handler; the W3.11 routing-regression test now passes because the new purpose has an `EXPECTED_CATEGORY` entry. Both tests are intentional gates the wave updates by design.
    - **`citations` is optional on the response, NOT always present as `[]`.** When the model emits no `[pack-id]` tokens, the response omits the field entirely (zod's `.optional()` accepts missing). The client cache's `InsightRegenEntry.citations?` is also optional. Saving the bytes avoids an `[]` rendering ambiguity on the client (an empty array might suggest "we tried and got nothing" while undefined means "no citations claimed"); the contract is "absent means none claimed".
    - **`text` length cap at 1200 chars.** The footer UI is space-constrained; longer prose would either wrap badly or get truncated by CSS. Capping at the response-schema level keeps the contract honest. `normaliseInsightText` slices to 1199 + appends `…` so the cap is visible to the user when it fires.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors, identical to W60 baseline — zero new from WI2-server. 36/36 new tests pass under `node --import tsx --test tests/insightRegenWI2Server.test.ts`. Full server suite 3494/3494 pass after the W3.11 + W18 maps were updated for the new purpose. Code commit `7cf4b6e7`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Client WI2-wire hook + footer button.** `useInsightRegen(tileId, filters)` in [`TileInsightFooter.tsx`](../client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx) — owns the WI2-cache instance via `useMemo`, calls `POST /api/insight/regen` on `cache.get(...) → undefined`, merges the response back into the cache, renders the "✦ Re-explain this view" button + spinner + result. Separate atomic wave; depends on this endpoint shipping first.
    - **Prompt-cache `cache_control` markers.** The Anthropic SDK supports per-message `cache_control` breakpoints; the byte-stable system prompt is the ideal place to set one so the same `(tile, filterHash)` query in the same session reuses the cached prompt. `callLlm` doesn't expose the cache-control parameter through its wrapper yet; threading it would touch every other caller. Deferred to a dedicated cache-telemetry wave (master plan Workstream 2, W69).
    - **Per-tile prompt-cache hit-rate telemetry.** Once the cache_control wiring lands, an SSE row + admin dashboard surface for hit rate would close the observability loop. Deferred.
    - **Reuse `generateChartInsights`.** The existing `insightGenerator.ts` (~700 LOC) computes a much richer set of anchors (percentiles, stdev, multi-series top performers, dual-axis y2 handling) and emits a fuller business commentary. Reusing it for WI2 would (a) inherit the PRIMARY-tier `LLM_PURPOSE.INSIGHT_GEN` cost — wrong tier for the regen lane; (b) require gutting / forking the prompt to fit the 1–3-sentence contract; (c) couple the regen lane to chart-key-insight evolution. Building a separate small surface keeps the regen lane optimisable independently.
    - **Citation hover-card UI on regenerated insights.** WQ3's `CitationHoverCard` ships on narrator prose; wiring it into `TileInsightFooter.tsx` for the insight regen `citations` field is the WI3 wave. Out of WI2-server scope.
    - **Streaming response.** The endpoint returns a one-shot JSON body. Streaming the 1–3 sentences would shave perceived latency but the model returns ~30–80 tokens — perceptible latency is dominated by RTT + model start, not token emission. Defer until UX measurement justifies the complexity.
    - **Per-tile feedback (thumbs up/down on insight quality).** Reusing the `pastAnalysisFeedback` schema for insight feedback would close the loop on regen quality. Out of scope; depends on the WI2-wire UI shipping first.
    - **Cache invalidation on chart-spec change.** The current cache key is `(tileId, filterHash)`. Spec changes (metric rename, breakdown swap) require a manual `cache.clear()` from the consuming hook. The cleaner long-term shape is a `chartSpecHash` mixed into the cache key, but that needs spec-digest plumbing the WI2-wire wave can ship.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave W60 · register `execute_metric_query` tool dispatcher.** Closes the W56 + W57 + W58 + W59a + W59b semantic-layer chain end-to-end. W59b activated the catalog as informational grounding: every planner LLM call now sees a byte-stable `## Semantic catalog` markdown manifest between the WW1 hints block and the P-A1 RAG block, so the planner can see canonical metric labels (`net_sales = SUM(value_sales) - SUM(returns)`), dimension declarations (`region: categorical`), and hierarchies (`country → region → city`). But the planner had no way to *call into* the catalog — every metric query still had to be hand-translated back to raw `execute_query_plan` shape against schema columns, which leaves Cube's predicted ~70 % of the eventual ~300 % accuracy lift on the floor. W60 promotes the catalog to a first-class dispatch path: the planner emits `{ metric, breakdownBy?, filters?, sortBy?, limit? }` against semantic NAMES, the W58 compiler translates to `QueryPlanBody`, and dispatch goes through the existing `execute_query_plan` executor (DuckDB-first, in-memory fallback) — same observability, same workbench artifact lane, same overclaim / aggregation-floor verifiers.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/executeMetricQueryTool.ts](../server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/executeMetricQueryTool.ts) (new, ~200 LOC).
      - `executeMetricQueryArgsSchema` — strict zod schema mirroring `CompileMetricQueryInput` minus the `model` (read from `ctx.exec.chatDocument?.semanticModel`). Top-level keys: `metric` (snake_case string, ≤80), `breakdownBy` (string[], ≤8), `filters` (each `{ dimension, op, values, match? }`, ≤20), `sortBy` (`{ by, direction }`, strict), `limit` (1..50000). The inner `semanticFilterSchema` mirrors W58's `SemanticFilter` op enum byte-for-byte (`in`, `not_in`, `eq`, `neq`, `lt`, `lte`, `gt`, `gte`, `between`) and the W58 `match` enum (`exact`, `case_insensitive`, `contains`), so any value the compiler accepts the args schema accepts and vice versa. `.strict()` on the outer schema + every nested object prevents the planner from sneaking `windowAggregations` or `computedAggregations` past the boundary — those shapes belong to raw `execute_query_plan`, not the metric-query semantic API.
      - `compiledPlanToQueryPlanBody(plan: CompiledQueryPlan): QueryPlanBody` — exported pure helper that bridges the W58 compiler's output to the executor's input. The shapes are structurally near-identical; the bridge exists to (a) deep-copy every nested array so downstream mutation cannot bleed back into the compiler's output (each aggregation / filter / sort entry is rebuilt; `values: [...f.values]` not `values: f.values`), (b) drop empty optional arrays so the strict `queryPlanBodySchema` doesn't see redundant `[]`s that would imply intent, (c) keep the bridge in one place so future widening of the compiler (perDimension nested aggregations, windowAggregations) only touches this file. Exported so unit tests exercise it directly without spinning a full `AgentExecutionContext`.
      - `registerExecuteMetricQueryTool(registry: ToolRegistry)` — closure captures the registry handle at boot. The executor: (1) hard-stops on `ctx.exec.mode !== "analysis"` with a clear summary — metric queries are analysis-only by construction; (2) safe-parses the args (defence-in-depth — `ToolRegistry.execute` already validates, but the safe-parse here lets us emit a contextual error summary); (3) reads `ctx.exec.chatDocument?.semanticModel`; (4) fail-fast when the catalog is empty (`metrics.length === 0 && dimensions.length === 0 && hierarchies.length === 0`) with summary `"No semantic catalog on this session. Fall back to execute_query_plan with raw column names from the schema."` — gives the planner a deterministic recovery path; (5) calls `compileMetricQuery({ model, metric, breakdownBy, filters, sortBy, limit })`; on `!ok` returns the compiler's `error` verbatim — unknown metric, unknown breakdown dimension, expression with disallowed characters all surface their root cause; (6) `agentLog("execute_metric_query.compiled", { metric, breakdownCount, filterCount, sortBy, aggregationCount, computedAggregations })` for production observability before dispatch; (7) `registry.execute("execute_query_plan", { plan }, ctx)` — single point of dispatch through the existing executor, inheriting DuckDB-first routing + the QL6 hard-fail safety net + the aggregation-without-groupBy verifier; (8) re-titles the returned `workbenchArtifact` to `execute_metric_query(<metric>)` on success so the user-visible workbench lane distinguishes catalog-routed queries from raw ones.
      - Manifest description tells the planner: "Args reference catalog METRIC and DIMENSION names (not raw schema columns); the compiler translates to QueryPlanBody and dispatches through execute_query_plan (DuckDB-first). Prefer this over execute_query_plan whenever the question's measure matches a catalog metric — the catalog encodes the canonical aggregation (e.g. `net_sales = SUM(gross_sales) - SUM(returns)`) so the planner cannot pick the wrong column / aggregation pair. Fall through to execute_query_plan only when no catalog metric covers the measure or you need shape it doesn't yet support (windowAggregations, percent_change, perDimension nested aggregations)." `argsHelp` carries the strict JSON shape and the canonical reminder "refer to SEMANTIC_CATALOG names ONLY; no raw schema columns".
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/registerTools.ts](../server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/registerTools.ts) — two lines: import `registerExecuteMetricQueryTool` from `./executeMetricQueryTool.js`, invoke `registerExecuteMetricQueryTool(registry)` at the bottom of `registerTools` after the F3 significance-tests registration. Honours invariant #8 (single-file-per-tool + central registration); the duplicate-name guard in [`toolRegistry.ts`](../server/lib/agents/runtime/toolRegistry.ts) will throw at boot if a future wave double-imports.
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/planner.ts](../server/lib/agents/runtime/planner.ts) — single system-prompt bullet added under the existing TOOL_ROUTER_HINT line (before `${formatSkillsManifestForPlanner()}`). The bullet names `SEMANTIC_CATALOG`, points the planner at the manifest block W59b inlines, says PREFER `execute_metric_query` over `execute_query_plan` when a catalog metric covers the measure, and lists the three shape-only exceptions (`windowAggregations`, `percent_change`, `perDimension`) that legitimately fall through to raw `execute_query_plan`. **System prompt edit is bundled with tool registration on purpose** — the WW1+WW2+WQ2 prompt-cache breakpoints sit on the system-prompt boundary, so any byte drift there invalidates the prompt cache for the rest of the session. Doing the tool reg + the directive line in one wave means cache invalidates ONCE, not twice. W59b deliberately deferred this edit; W60 completes it.
    - [server/tests/executeMetricQueryToolW60.test.ts](../server/tests/executeMetricQueryToolW60.test.ts) (new, ~340 LOC). 28 tests across 7 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](../server/package.json)'s explicit test list per invariant #4:
      - **Args schema — valid shapes** (3): minimal `{metric}`; full shape with breakdownBy + filters + sortBy + limit; every filter op the compiler emits parses (`in`, `not_in`, `eq`, `neq`, `lt`, `lte`, `gt`, `gte`, `between`).
      - **Args schema — rejections** (7): empty metric; extra top-level keys; extra keys inside a filter; unknown filter op; empty filter values; breakdownBy > 8; extra keys inside sortBy.
      - **`compiledPlanToQueryPlanBody` shape roundtrip** (9): aggregations verbatim; groupBy emitted only when non-empty (empty `[]` dropped); computedAggregations forwarded; dimensionFilters with `match`; dimensionFilters without `match` omits the key (own-property assertion); sort forwarded; limit forwarded; limit absent dropped.
      - **`compiledPlanToQueryPlanBody` mutation safety** (1): output arrays are not the input arrays; mutating the output groupBy does not affect the compiler input. Pins the deep-copy contract.
      - **registerTools.ts wiring source-inspection** (2): import statement; registration call.
      - **executeMetricQueryTool.ts registration shape source-inspection** (4): tool name literal; dispatch through `registry.execute("execute_query_plan", { plan }, ctx)`; analysis-mode guard; semantic-model read path.
      - **planner.ts SEMANTIC_CATALOG rule source-inspection** (2): bullet text contains `SEMANTIC_CATALOG (when present in the user message)` + `execute_metric_query`; prefer-over phrasing matches.
      - 28/28 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Dispatch through `execute_query_plan`, not a parallel executor.** The W58 compiler already emits a `QueryPlanBody`; re-implementing DuckDB execution + the QL6 hard-fail rules + the temporal-facet promotion + the aggregation-without-groupBy verifier would duplicate ~400 LOC of executor logic and create a divergence risk. By calling `registry.execute("execute_query_plan", { plan }, ctx)`, every fix to the underlying executor (PD3 perDimension repairs, T3 trend-bucket guards, RNK1 leaderboard repairs) is automatically inherited. The tool stays thin.
    - **Closure capture vs. global registry.** `registerExecuteMetricQueryTool(registry)` captures the registry in a closure rather than reaching for a module-global, so the executor can invoke `registry.execute(...)` without threading the registry through `ToolRunContext`. This avoids widening the `ToolRunContext` interface (which would touch every other tool) and preserves the single-instance correctness story — there's exactly one registry per process, captured at boot. Tests construct the registry directly when they need to exercise the dispatch path; the unit tests in this wave skip the dispatch path entirely and exercise `compiledPlanToQueryPlanBody` + the args schema directly.
    - **Args mirror `CompileMetricQueryInput` minus `model`.** The args are deliberately the same shape as W58's input so the planner's mental model is "speak about metrics" with one extra constraint ("model is implicit; it's the session catalog"). The `model` arg is removed not just for ergonomics but for security: the planner cannot inject a synthetic semantic model from the args. The model is *always* the session's `ChatDocument.semanticModel`.
    - **Fail-fast when no catalog.** Returning `ok: false` with `"No semantic catalog on this session. Fall back to execute_query_plan..."` (vs. silently falling through to a `compileMetricQuery` call that would emit "Unknown metric") gives the planner a deterministic, single-step recovery: drop the `execute_metric_query` step and re-emit `execute_query_plan` with raw schema columns. Pre-W57 uploads (where `semanticModel` is undefined on the chat document) hit this path cleanly. W57 inference can also yield an empty model on indicator-light datasets; same recovery applies.
    - **Re-title the workbench artifact.** `execute_query_plan` writes a generic title `"execute_query_plan"` on its `workbenchArtifact`. Without overriding, the user-visible workbench lane would lose the signal that this was a catalog-routed query. Re-titling to `execute_metric_query(<metric>)` keeps the lane self-documenting and lets a future admin-UI lane filter by routed-vs-raw without inspecting plan JSON.
    - **System-prompt edit lives in `planner.ts`, not in a SEMANTIC_CATALOG `Rules:` constant.** The existing `Rules:` block in the planner system prompt is a long inline template literal; adding the bullet inline is a single-line surgical edit, while extracting the rules into a named constant would risk reformatting the surrounding bullets and drifting prompt-cache byte boundaries. The source-inspection test pins the bullet's existence + content; any future refactor that moves it must update the test.
    - **No effect-size or windowAggregation pass-through (yet).** The current compiler accepts `breakdownBy` / `filters` / `sortBy` / `limit`. Window aggregations, perDimension nested aggregations, and `percent_change` are intentionally NOT exposed through `execute_metric_query` — those shapes need raw-column semantics that aren't expressible against a catalog metric (a metric's expression is fixed at definition time; `percent_change` over a metric would require time-window definition, which is the eventual W64 cache-key story). Planner is explicitly told to fall through to `execute_query_plan` for those shapes. Future waves can widen.
    - **No skill manifest entry.** Skills wrap multi-tool composites; `execute_metric_query` is a primitive on par with `execute_query_plan`. The tool manifest entry alone is sufficient for the planner to pick it up; no skill needed.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors, identical to WI2-cache / W59b / WD2 / W59a baseline — zero new from W60. 28/28 new unit tests pass under `node --import tsx --test tests/executeMetricQueryToolW60.test.ts`. Full server suite 3458/3458 pass (initial run flaked on one cache-concurrency test; re-ran clean). Code commit `d6c87dd7`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **End-to-end integration test with a real session.** The 28 tests cover args validation, the pure plan-conversion helper, and source-inspection wiring. An integration test that builds a full `AgentExecutionContext` with a populated chatDocument + semanticModel + summary, registers tools, and dispatches through `execute_metric_query` against a DuckDB session would catch executor-level integration regressions. Deferred — relies on the existing live-golden-replay harness picking up the new tool naturally, plus the next end-of-phase α evaluation pass.
    - **Live golden replay fixtures for metric-routed questions.** Per the master plan's W62 (semantic-layer fixtures q06–q10), the live replay harness will pin: same metric question, raw-SQL vs. metric-compiled, both pass with metric-compiled having higher score. Out of W60 scope; W62 is the dedicated wave.
    - **`validateModel` warnings + planner-picked-raw drift gate (W63).** When the planner picks `execute_query_plan` against a raw column even though a viable catalog metric exists, the master plan calls for an SSE `flow_decision` row + a warning surface in the admin UI. Out of W60 scope; depends on a deterministic drift detector and the admin UI lane.
    - **Metric query result cache (W64).** Keyed by `(modelVersion, metricName, dimensions, filters, window)`, hits skip the LLM entirely. Out of W60 scope; depends on cache-invalidation infrastructure that the master plan parks in Workstream 8.
    - **Admin UI for editing the model (W61).** Lets the data team review / edit the inferred model. Out of W60 scope; the renderer is W59a's `formatMetricCatalog`, the persistence is `ChatDocument.semanticModel`, the page is a separate client-side wave.
    - **`run_metric_query` skill wrapper.** A composite skill that runs `execute_metric_query` then `build_chart` would let dashboard-mode plans emit a single skill step instead of two tool steps. Out of W60 scope; the existing primitive composition path already works.
    - **`count_distinct` widening for QueryPlanBody filter targets.** The compiler already emits `count_distinct` aggregations (for `COUNT(DISTINCT col)` in metric expressions) and the executor's `aggOpSchema` accepts it, so no widening was needed in this wave. But the strict args schema today rejects metric expressions outside the existing W58 character-set (no `NULLIF`, no `CASE`); widening the executor's `ALLOWED_EXPRESSION_CHARS_RE` is a future wave when a metric needs those forms.
    - **Tool-router (WT6) recommendation updates.** WT6's `selectTool` deterministic recommender doesn't yet know about `execute_metric_query`. A future wave can add the recommendation lane (intent: `general_analytical` ∩ catalog-has-matching-metric → `execute_metric_query` first). Out of W60 scope; the planner's system-prompt directive already covers the prefer-catalog rule textually.

 WI1 introduced the `chart.insight: InsightSpec` schema with a `generator: { kind: "llm" | "deterministic", args? }` slot meant for dynamic insight regeneration on filter change (master plan Workstream 7). The intended UX: when the user adds a global filter or brushes via WD2, each tile's insight footer offers a "✦ Re-explain this view" action; clicking issues a MINI-tier LLM call with the current filtered data + chart spec + domain context and replaces the insight prose. Re-asking the same `(tile, filter combo)` within a session should return instantly without burning a fresh call — and across N tiles in a multi-filter dashboard, the same global filter combination produces hundreds of identical-context requests if uncached, so caching is critical not optional. WI2 as one wave (cache + server endpoint + client hook + footer UI) is too large; WI2-cache splits the pure data-plumbing concern out first, the same atomic-split pattern as W59a → W59b and WD2 → WD2-wiring.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/insightRegenCache.ts](client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/insightRegenCache.ts) (new, ~145 LOC). Three exports:
      - `hashGlobalFilters(filters: ActiveChartFilters): string` — byte-stable serialisation of the global filter map. Walks `Object.keys(filters).sort()`, then for each column emits one of three shapes: categorical → `column=c:value1|value2|...` (with values sorted), date → `column=d:start..end` (with `undefined` start/end rendering as empty), numeric → `column=n:min..max` (same treatment for undefined bounds). Columns are joined with `;`. The `=`, `;`, `:`, `|`, `..` separators are unambiguous together — no value in the active filter shape contains those literals after the existing chart-filter normalisation. Result: identical filter maps in different insertion / value order yield identical hash strings.
      - `buildCacheKey(tileId: string, filterHash: string): string` — composes the pair as `${tileId}::${filterHash}`. The `::` delimiter is unambiguous because `hashGlobalFilters` uses `=` / `;` / `:` as internal separators.
      - `createInsightRegenCache(opts?: { maxEntries?: number; ttlMs?: number; now?: () => number }): InsightRegenCache` — factory. Default `maxEntries: 64` (per-dashboard ceiling — 8 tiles × 8 filter combos is a sensible upper bound on session interactivity), default `ttlMs: 300_000` (5 min, matches Anthropic's prompt-cache TTL so a regen done at minute 0 is fresh exactly as long as the upstream prompt cache it built against). The `now` injection is for deterministic tests.
      - Returned `InsightRegenCache` is a closure-backed Map with five methods: `get(key) → InsightRegenEntry | undefined` (returns undefined for stale entries + lazily evicts them, refreshes LRU recency on a successful read), `set(key, value)` (evicts the LRU entry when full + replaces an existing entry by delete-then-set so iteration order tracks recency), `has(key)` (false on expired + lazy delete, same as get), `clear()`, `size()`, `evictExpired() → number` (active sweep returning the count of dropped entries; useful for a periodic timer the consuming hook may run).
      - `InsightRegenEntry` interface carries `{ text: string; citations?: string[]; regeneratedAt?: string; confidenceTier?: "low" | "medium" | "high" }` — the minimal shape the future regen endpoint will return + the future footer UI will render. Future schema additions (e.g. effect-size badges, sub-investigation links) extend this interface without breaking the cache contract.
      - **LRU implementation: `Map` insertion order.** ES2015 maps maintain insertion order. `get` refreshes recency by deleting + re-inserting (O(1)). Eviction pops `keys().next().value`, which is the oldest entry. No external dependency needed; testable in pure node:test.
      - **TTL is on `get` / `has`, not on a background timer.** This means stale entries occupy slots until probed; on a 64-slot cache with a 5-min TTL this is bounded and acceptable. The optional `evictExpired()` lets the consuming hook do a periodic active sweep if desired.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/insightRegenCache.test.ts](client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/insightRegenCache.test.ts) (new, ~225 LOC). 21 tests across 6 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](server/package.json) per invariant #4:
      - **`hashGlobalFilters` byte stability** (8): empty map → empty string; identical maps → identical hash; column-order independence; categorical value-order independence; date filter format; numeric filter format; categorical-vs-numeric disambiguation on the same column name (the `c:` / `n:` prefix guarantees no collision); undefined bounds gracefully render as empty.
      - **`buildCacheKey`** (2): standard concat with `::`; empty filterHash → `tileId::`.
      - **`createInsightRegenCache` — basic get/set** (4): unknown key returns undefined; store-then-retrieve roundtrip; re-set overwrites; clear empties.
      - **LRU eviction** (2): full cache evicts oldest on insertion; `get` refreshes recency so previously oldest survives later evictions.
      - **TTL expiry** (3): post-TTL `get` returns undefined + deletes lazily; `evictExpired` returns the eviction count + leaves fresh entries intact; `has` returns false + lazy-deletes for stale entries.
      - **Integration scenario** (2): two clients of the same tile with identical filters share a cache hit (the `(tileId, filterHash)` round-trips); changing one filter value produces a different cache key so the prior hit is invalidated by construction.
      - 21/21 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Pure data-plumbing first.** The eventual WI2 end-to-end touches: a server endpoint that takes `(spec, filteredData, domainContext)` and returns insight prose; a client hook (`useInsightRegen(tileId, filters)`) wired into [`TileInsightFooter.tsx`](client/src/pages/Dashboard/Components/TileInsightFooter.tsx); a "✦ Re-explain this view" button + spinner; a cache between the hook and the network call; integration with WD2's brushing layer so brushed-filter changes also invalidate. Shipping all of it in one wave is god-object-adjacent. Splitting the cache out first means: the cache contract is fixed + tested before the server / UI layers can drift it; the hook wave can be a thin React layer over this contract; the server wave can be a thin LLM-call wrapper that the hook calls when `cache.get(...)` misses.
    - **`hashGlobalFilters` uses string concat, not JSON.stringify.** `JSON.stringify({zone:"A", brand:"X"})` and `JSON.stringify({brand:"X", zone:"A"})` produce different strings — the key-sorting concern would have to live downstream. Doing it explicitly in the helper makes the byte-stability contract obvious in the source, and the resulting hash strings are markedly more compact than equivalent JSON (`region=c:North|South;zone=c:All` is ~25 chars vs the equivalent JSON ~70 chars). Compact keys matter for browser memory + dev-tool readability.
    - **TTL matches Anthropic's prompt-cache TTL.** Prompt-cache hits expire at 5 min; a regen LLM call built against a cached system prompt becomes uncacheable past that. Holding regen results longer than the underlying cache is wasted: the next request would re-build the system prompt anyway. 5 min is the natural ceiling.
    - **`maxEntries: 64` default.** Eight tiles × eight filter combos per session is a generous upper bound; most analytical sessions have <4 tiles and <3 filter combos. Cap exists to prevent a runaway log-tail of stale entries from growing unbounded in long sessions; 64 entries × ~500 bytes each = ~32 KB ceiling.
    - **`now` injection for deterministic tests.** The cache's own time source is injectable; the TTL test advances `t` directly without `await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, ...))` or `vi.useFakeTimers()`. Tests are sub-millisecond + flake-free.
    - **Closure-backed Map, not a class.** The factory returns an object literal with the five methods, all closing over the same `store` Map + `now` closure. Tree-shake-friendly (no `class` keyword in the bundle), easy to instantiate per `useMemo`, indistinguishable from a class instance to TypeScript.
    - **`has` does lazy-delete on expiry.** Consistent with `get`. Both probes return false / undefined for stale entries AND remove them so the cache's `size()` stays accurate after a flurry of probes. The `evictExpired()` active sweep exists for the rare case where the consuming hook wants to periodically reclaim space without probing every key.
    - **Stored values include `citations` + `regeneratedAt` + `confidenceTier`.** Even though those are optional, including them in the interface up-front means the future regen endpoint + footer UI agree on the shape without a schema bump in WI2-wire. The cache becomes the contract.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` on client reports 53 errors, identical to W59b / WD2 / W59a baseline — zero new from WI2-cache. 21/21 new unit tests pass under `node --import tsx --test`. Code commit `40602120`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Server regen endpoint.** A future wave (`WI2-server`) registers `POST /api/insight/regen` that takes `{ spec, filteredData, domainContext, tileId }` and returns `{ text, citations, regeneratedAt, confidenceTier }`. The endpoint will go through the same MINI-tier `callLlm` channel that `generateChartInsights` uses today, with `promptCacheEligibility` set on the system prompt for cache reuse across tiles in the same session.
    - **Client hook + footer UI.** A future wave (`WI2-wire`) ships `useInsightRegen(tileId, filters)` and the "✦ Re-explain this view" button in `TileInsightFooter.tsx`. The hook will own the cache instance via `useMemo` and call the server endpoint on cache miss.
    - **Cache invalidation on chart-spec change.** Today the cache is keyed by `(tileId, filterHash)` only. If the chart's spec (e.g. metric, breakdown) changes mid-session, the cache will incorrectly serve a stale insight. A future wave can extend the hash to include a chart-spec digest, or simply require consumers to call `cache.clear()` on spec-change.
    - **Persistence across sessions.** The cache lives for the dashboard mount and dies with it. A future infra wave could persist hits to localStorage / Cosmos so cross-session re-asks of the same combination are free; deferred until cost telemetry shows it's needed.
    - **Cache-warming on dashboard load.** Pre-computing insights for the "no filters" combo on dashboard mount could eliminate the first-paint regen latency. Deferred until UX shows the latency is noticeable; for now the existing baked-at-creation `keyInsight` / `InsightSpec.default` text covers the no-filter case.
    - **Cross-tile invalidation.** When a global filter changes, every tile's cache key changes — the existing keying already invalidates correctly. But a global filter that doesn't apply to a given tile (because the tile's chart doesn't use that column) should ideally NOT invalidate that tile's cache. The cache as-shipped is conservative: any global filter change invalidates every tile. A future wave can introduce per-tile filter relevance projection so tiles whose data is unchanged share cache hits across filter combos.
    - **Citation hover-card surface inside regenerated insights.** The `citations` field on `InsightRegenEntry` carries pack ids; the footer UI can render them with the existing WQ3 `CitationHoverCard` component. Wiring lives in WI2-wire, not in the cache.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave W59b · wire `formatMetricCatalog` into the planner user prompt.** The semantic-layer chain (W56 schemas + W57 upload-time inference + W58 compiler + W59a manifest helper) has been merged for two waves but the planner has been blind to it — `ChatDocument.semanticModel` is populated at upload and never consumed in any LLM call. W59b is the activation wave: a minimal `planner.ts` edit inlines the W59a manifest into the planner's user prompt, between the WW1+WW2 hints block and the upfront RAG block. The planner now sees a per-dataset catalog of metric labels (`Net Sales = SUM(value_sales)`), dimension columns (`region`, `channel`), and hierarchies (`country → region → city`) as a first-class block — same byte position every turn, byte-stable across identical models so the prompt-cache breakpoints established by WW1+WW2+WQ2 don't drift.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/semantic/prompt.ts](server/lib/semantic/prompt.ts) gains `buildSemanticCatalogPromptBlock(model, opts?)` (~25 LOC including JSDoc). Thin wrapper over W59a's `formatMetricCatalog`: returns the empty string when `model` is `null` / `undefined` (legacy uploads pre-W57, or inference yielded nothing); otherwise returns the manifest followed by a `\n\n` paragraph break so the block concatenates cleanly with the rest of the user prompt. Options pass-through (`includeHidden`) lets the admin UI reuse the same wrapper.
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/planner.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/planner.ts) edit (3 lines added):
      - New import: `import { buildSemanticCatalogPromptBlock } from "../../semantic/prompt.js";` placed right after the WW1 `plannerHintsBlock` import to keep grouping coherent.
      - New local `semanticBlock` constant computed before the user-prompt template literal: `const semanticBlock = buildSemanticCatalogPromptBlock(ctx.chatDocument?.semanticModel);`. The `?.` chain handles two empty cases (no chatDocument, no semanticModel on chatDocument); the helper handles the `null` / `undefined` case downstream.
      - Inline insertion: `${hintsResult.block}${semanticBlock}${ragBlock}` — the catalog sits between the deterministic hints block (WW1) and the upfront RAG hits block (P-A1). Rationale below.
      - **System prompt deliberately untouched.** The system prompt is the cached portion (per Anthropic's prompt-caching guidance + WW1's cache-breakpoint placement). Any byte drift in the system prompt invalidates the cache for the rest of the session. W59b is read-only grounding; W60 (the `execute_metric_query` tool registration wave) is the natural place to add a SEMANTIC_CATALOG directive line to the system prompt.
    - [server/tests/semanticPlannerBlockW59b.test.ts](server/tests/semanticPlannerBlockW59b.test.ts) (new, ~135 LOC). 9 tests across 5 suites; appended to [server/package.json](server/package.json) per invariant #4:
      - **Null / undefined input** (2): both return the empty string.
      - **Populated model** (2): manifest starts with `## Semantic catalog` and ends with `\n\n` (paragraph break); empty-marker manifest (zero exposed entries) also ends with `\n\n` and renders the `_(empty —` line with version embedded.
      - **Options pass-through** (1): `includeHidden: true` includes draft metrics; default omits them.
      - **Byte stability** (1): two identical models produce identical output (regression guard for the prompt-cache contract).
      - **`planner.ts` source-inspection wiring** (3): the import statement is present at the canonical path; the helper is called with `ctx.chatDocument?.semanticModel`; the user-prompt template inlines `${semanticBlock}` between `${hintsResult.block}` and `${ragBlock}`. Any future refactor that drops or re-orders the block will trip these tests.
      - 9/9 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Minimal `planner.ts` diff.** `planner.ts` is 976 LOC and already heavily edited (WW1, WW2, WQ2). A larger refactor — extracting the user-prompt template into a builder function, for instance — would entangle the wave with restructuring concerns and risk cache drift. The 3-line atomic edit keeps the diff surface small and the prompt structure unchanged for the call sites the cache breakpoints rely on.
    - **Position: between hints and RAG.** The hints block (WW1+WQ2) is a deterministic intent + tool recommendation under the question; it's the highest-leverage routing signal and stays first. RAG hits (P-A1) are upfront semantic retrieval against the question text; they come second. The semantic catalog is meta-info about the dataset — same shape every turn for the session — so it sits right after the per-turn routing hints but before the per-turn retrieval context. This ordering also makes the catalog the "dataset definition" that the rest of the user-prompt blocks (memory recall, hypothesis register, prior observations, working memory, handoff log, context summary) can implicitly cite.
    - **Read-only activation, not tool dispatch.** Without an `execute_metric_query` tool the planner can't directly call into the W58 compiler. But the catalog still adds value: the planner sees `Net Sales = SUM(value_sales)` and learns the canonical name for the column the user calls "sales" or "revenue"; it sees `region` declared as a categorical dimension and avoids guessing about cardinality; it sees `geo: country → region → city` and naturally drills the right way. Cube's benchmark suggests ~30 % of the accuracy lift comes from catalog visibility alone, before tool wiring. W60 captures the remaining ~70 %.
    - **`buildSemanticCatalogPromptBlock` lives in `semantic/prompt.ts`, not `planner.ts`.** The helper is a thin null-coalescing wrapper but it's also the place a future wave will add a `maxLength` cap, a default `includeHidden: false` policy, or a domain-pack citation hint. Keeping it adjacent to `formatMetricCatalog` means future tweaks to the manifest rendering policy ship in one module.
    - **Wave separation from W59a.** W59a was the byte-stable manifest renderer; W59b is the planner wiring. Splitting them lets each have its own atomic commit + paired docs commit + test surface. Failures localise: a prompt-cache regression points at W59b; a manifest-formatting bug points at W59a.

  **Verified.** `npm run typecheck` reports 98 errors, identical to W59a / WD2 baseline — zero new from W59b. 9/9 new unit tests pass under `node --import tsx --test`. Code commit `f46e4c75`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **`execute_metric_query` tool registration (W60).** The compiler is ready (W58 ships `compileMetricQuery({metric, breakdownBy, filters})`) but the planner doesn't have a tool name to call. W60 registers the tool wrapper in [`registerTools.ts`](server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/registerTools.ts) and adds it to the tool manifest. Until then the catalog is informational.
    - **System-prompt SEMANTIC_CATALOG directive.** A natural addition is a `Rules:` line in the system prompt saying "When a metric matches the question's outcome, prefer the catalog name". Deferred to W60 to bundle with the tool registration so the system prompt edit happens once, not twice.
    - **Admin UI for editing the model (W61).** `buildSemanticCatalogPromptBlock` is the rendering primitive an admin preview tooltip will reuse. The admin page itself is a separate client-side wave.
    - **Manifest size budget.** Pathological models (200 metrics × 200 dimensions, per the schema caps) could blow the planner's prompt budget. W59a's inline notes flag this; W59b doesn't enforce a cap. Most W57-inferred models are <20 entries each so it's not a present concern.
    - **Per-step semantic-context refresh.** The catalog is built once per planner call. If a mid-turn data-ops step (e.g. `add_computed_columns`) introduces a new column, the semantic model isn't updated until the next upload-time reinference. A future wave can plumb an incremental update path through the per-step `updateSessionAnalysisContext` channel.
    - **Drift-gate for catalog-vs-raw-query planner choice (W63).** When the planner picks `execute_query_plan` against a raw column even though a viable catalog metric exists, the master plan calls for an SSE `flow_decision` row + a `validateModel` warning surface in the admin UI. Out of W59b scope; depends on W60 ship + a deterministic drift detector.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WD2 · cross-filter brushing — pure helper module.** The [1000x master plan](/Users/tida/.claude/plans/go-through-the-entire-partitioned-yao.md) Workstream 4 has cross-filter brushing as the second wave (`WD2`): clicking a bar / point / segment in a dashboard tile should dispatch a cross-filter event that flows into the dashboard-wide `globalFilters` state (in place from `WD1`), and other tiles dim non-matching marks rather than dropping them. End-to-end that touches every chart renderer (~13 visx renderers + ECharts), `DashboardView`, and the global filter bar's render path — too much for one atomic wave on a god-object-adjacent surface. WD2 ships the pure-helper data-plumbing concern first: a small, well-tested module that exposes the toggle / coerce / dispatch primitives any future renderer-wiring wave can call without re-litigating semantics. Same atomic-split shape as W59a's `formatMetricCatalog` shipping before W59b's planner-wiring.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts](client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.ts) (new, ~155 LOC). New directory created — first file under `Dashboard/lib/`. Pure helpers around the existing `ActiveChartFilters = Record<string, ChartFilterSelection | undefined>` shape from [`client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts`](client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts):
      - `CrossFilterEvent` interface: `{ column: string; value: string | number | boolean | null | undefined; sourceTileId?: string }`. The `sourceTileId` is wired but not yet consumed — a future wave will use it for "dim non-matching marks on the originating tile too" vs. "leave the source tile uncrushed" UX decisions.
      - `toFilterValue(raw)` — canonical string coercion. `null` / `undefined` → the literal `"null"` (matches the upstream `(null)` key normalisation in [`breakdownRankingTool.ts`](server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/breakdownRankingTool.ts) and the existing chart filter UI's null-bucket rendering). Numbers / booleans → `String(v)`. Strings pass through unchanged.
      - `isCrossFilterActive(global, column, value)` — membership test. Returns `false` when the column has a non-categorical selection (date / numeric) — those shapes cannot encode a discrete value match.
      - `applyCrossFilter(global, event)` — the toggle contract:
        - column with no selection → install fresh `{ type: "categorical", values: [v] }`
        - column with a categorical selection that lacks `v` → append `v`
        - column with a categorical selection that contains `v` → remove `v`; if the selection becomes empty, drop the column entirely (`delete next[column]`)
        - column with a date / numeric selection → REPLACE with a fresh categorical `[v]`. A chart brush is explicitly a discrete-value action; the user's last action wins
      - `removeCrossFilter(global, column, value)` — surgical remove. No-op (returns identity reference) when the value is not present or the column is non-categorical. Drops the column on last-value removal.
      - `clearCrossFilter(global, column)` — drops the column entirely. No-op identity-return when the column has no selection.
      - `listActiveCrossFilters(global)` — flattens categorical columns into a sorted `[{ column, value }]` array. Column-sorted then value-sorted so chip rendering is stable across re-renders. Skips non-categorical selections.
      - `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT = "marico:cross-filter"` exported constant — the CustomEvent name the renderer-wiring wave will use.
      - `dispatchCrossFilter(event)` — browser-guarded helper. Returns `false` (no-op) when `typeof window === "undefined"` or `typeof CustomEvent === "undefined"` so the module is safe to import in SSR / server-test contexts. Returns `true` after a successful `window.dispatchEvent`.
      - **Mutation-free contract.** Every state-modifying helper (`applyCrossFilter`, `removeCrossFilter`, `clearCrossFilter`) clones first (`{ ...global }`) before modifying. The test `does not mutate the input global map` pins this.
      - **Toggle vs. last-action.** The contract is asymmetric on purpose: clicking a categorical-active value toggles it off; clicking a non-categorical column installs a new categorical filter (does NOT preserve the prior date/numeric selection). This matches the user's intuition that a chart brush is a one-shot "show me only this discrete value" action — restoring a date range is the responsibility of the global filter bar UI.
    - [client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.test.ts](client/src/pages/Dashboard/lib/crossFilter.test.ts) (new, ~205 LOC). 29 cases across 10 suites; appended to [`server/package.json`](server/package.json)'s explicit test list (the client tests run under the server test harness) per invariant #4:
      - **`toFilterValue` coercion** (4): strings pass through; numbers stringify; booleans stringify; null/undefined → "null".
      - **`isCrossFilterActive`** (5): empty map; value present; value absent; non-categorical selections return false; numeric/null clicks coerce before comparison.
      - **`applyCrossFilter` — toggle on categorical column** (4): install fresh on empty column; append when value missing; remove on toggle-off; drop column entirely on last-value removal.
      - **`applyCrossFilter` — non-categorical column** (2): replaces date selection with categorical; replaces numeric selection with categorical.
      - **`applyCrossFilter` — purity** (1): two sequential applies do not mutate the input map (pinned via JSON-snapshot comparison).
      - **`applyCrossFilter` — value coercion** (2): null click → `"null"`; numeric click → string.
      - **`removeCrossFilter`** (4): value removed; column dropped on last-value; no-op identity-return when value absent; no-op when column is non-categorical.
      - **`clearCrossFilter`** (2): column removed; no-op identity-return when column absent.
      - **`listActiveCrossFilters`** (3): empty map → empty list; flattened in column-sorted then value-sorted order; non-categorical selections skipped.
      - **`dispatchCrossFilter`** (2): non-browser env → returns `false` (no `window`); `CROSS_FILTER_EVENT` constant equals canonical literal.
      - 29/29 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Atomic split: data plumbing first, wiring second.** The end-to-end WD2 in the master plan touches every visx renderer (`BarRenderer.tsx`, `LineRenderer.tsx`, `PointRenderer.tsx`, `AreaRenderer.tsx`, `ArcRenderer.tsx`, `FunnelRenderer.tsx`, `KpiRenderer.tsx`, …) plus the ECharts adapters, the `DashboardView`'s `useState<ActiveChartFilters>`, and the dim-vs-filter visual treatment. Putting all of that in one wave is a god-object-adjacent change that would carry risk of cross-renderer drift. WD2 splits the smaller pure-data concern out first — the wiring wave can then be a thin call-site change in each renderer (one line each: `onClick={() => dispatchCrossFilter({ column: enc.x.field, value: c.outerRaw, sourceTileId })}`) without re-litigating the toggle / coercion semantics. Same playbook as W59a / W59b.
    - **CustomEvent vs. context / pub-sub library.** A new context for cross-filter state would require every renderer to consume it (and we'd need to thread it through chart compilation paths). A pub-sub library is overkill for a one-listener channel. Plain `window.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent(...))` + a single `window.addEventListener` in `DashboardView` is the cheapest plumbing: zero deps, zero context boundaries, naturally bubbles past iframes / portals. The trade-off is "global event channel" — but the channel is namespaced (`marico:cross-filter`) and the receiver is well-defined (`DashboardView`), so the risk is low. SSR safety is handled by the `typeof window` guard.
    - **String coercion is one-way.** Categorical filter values are stored as strings (per [`chartFilters.ts`](client/src/lib/chartFilters.ts) `CategoricalFilterSelection`). `toFilterValue` is the one-way coercion at the boundary — the helper never reads-back-and-parses, so downstream renderers must format numeric values the same way (`String(42) === "42"`, not e.g. `"42.0"`). A future wave that introduces a typed-value store (e.g. distinguishing `42` from `"42"`) would need to extend the categorical schema, not just the helper.
    - **Null bucket maps to literal `"null"`.** The upstream tool layer normalises null-grouping rows to `(null)` in aggregations, and the existing chart filter UI surfaces a "(null)" chip when a categorical option is the null sentinel. Mapping `null` / `undefined` → `"null"` here keeps the cross-filter round-trip stable: clicking a null bar in the chart applies a filter whose stringified value matches the renderer's bucket key.
    - **Toggle-off drops the column.** When a categorical selection becomes empty, the helper deletes the column from the global map rather than leaving `{ type: "categorical", values: [] }`. The empty-array form would be a separate filter state ("show no rows") that the rest of the codebase doesn't handle uniformly — explicit deletion keeps the contract crisp: "no entry for column → no filter on column".
    - **Date / numeric → categorical is a replace, not a merge.** A user with an active date range who clicks a specific date bar wants to filter to that date (not keep both filters AND-ed). The merge form is "filter UI semantics" and lives in the global filter bar, not the brush helper.
    - **`listActiveCrossFilters` returns a flat array, not a Map.** Chip rendering needs a stable enumeration; React reconciliation needs stable order. Column-sorted then value-sorted gives both for free without burdening the caller with `Object.keys(...).sort()` logic.

  **Verified.** `npm run typecheck` on server reports 98 errors, identical to W59a baseline. `npx tsc --noEmit` on client reports 53 errors, identical to client baseline. Zero new from WD2. 29/29 new tests pass under `node --import tsx --test`. Code commit `12864136`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Renderer wiring.** The thirteen visx renderers + ECharts adapters need to call `dispatchCrossFilter` from their mark `onClick` handlers. The atomic next-wave (call it `WD2.wire`) is a one-line-per-renderer change. Out of WD2's pure-helper scope.
    - **`DashboardView` subscription.** A `useEffect(() => { window.addEventListener(CROSS_FILTER_EVENT, handler); return () => window.removeEventListener(...); }, [])` in `DashboardView` that runs `applyCrossFilter` against the current `globalFilters` and dispatches `setGlobalFilters(...)`. Tiny diff; lives in the wiring wave.
    - **Dim-vs-filter visual treatment.** The master plan calls for filtered tiles to "dim non-matching marks instead of removing them" so the user sees the slice clearly. That's a render-path change in each renderer — separate visual wave.
    - **`sourceTileId` consumption.** The field is wired through the event type and `applyCrossFilter` but no consumer reads it yet. A future wave will let `DashboardView` skip the dim treatment on the originating tile (or render a "brushed by this tile" badge).
    - **Cross-filter chip strip.** `listActiveCrossFilters` is exported so a future wave can render a chip strip ("Brushed by: region · North · ✕  channel · MT · ✕") above the tile grid. Today's `DashboardGlobalFilterBar` already shows global filter chips; the brush layer might merge into the same surface or live alongside.
    - **Per-tile brush mode toggle.** WD2 introduces a global brush; per-tile "this tile's clicks don't propagate" is a separate UX wave.
    - **Brush vs. global-filter precedence.** When a user has an active global filter on `region: [North]` AND clicks a `South` bar in a tile, what should happen? The helper's current behaviour is "append" (region becomes `[North, South]`). A `brushReplacesGlobal` mode could be useful for analytical drill — separate wave.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave W59a · `formatMetricCatalog` pure helper (byte-stable manifest).** W56 (semantic schemas), W57 (`inferModel` upload-time auto-population), and W58 (`compileMetricQuery` `{metric, breakdownBy, filters}` → `QueryPlanBody`) have all been merged for two days, but the chain is dormant: the planner has no idea any of it exists. The semantic layer is the single biggest accuracy lever on the [1000x master plan](/Users/tida/.claude/plans/go-through-the-entire-partitioned-yao.md) Workstream 1 (Cube's paired benchmarks: ~66 % data-error reduction, ~300 % accuracy lift across frontier models), and W59 — the planner prompt rewrite — was the next wave. But `planner.ts` is 976 LOC and already heavily edited by recent waves (WW1 added the TOOL_ROUTER_HINT block; WQ2 added EXTERNAL_CLAIM_MARKERS; WW1+WW2 added PLANNER_CONFIDENCE_DIRECTIVE), so a single-wave rewrite risked entangling the prompt restructuring with the manifest-rendering logic. W59a splits the smaller atomic concern out first: a pure helper that takes a `SemanticModel` and renders a byte-stable markdown manifest suitable for inlining into the planner prompt (W59b), the admin UI (W61), and any narrator-side metric-citation block a future quality wave wires up. W59b becomes a thin call site that just stitches the manifest into the existing prompt scaffolding.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/semantic/prompt.ts](server/lib/semantic/prompt.ts) (new, ~175 LOC). Pure function `formatMetricCatalog(model: SemanticModel, opts?: FormatMetricCatalogOptions): string`. No I/O. No date dependencies. Safe in tests and any runtime context.
      - `FormatMetricCatalogOptions = { includeHidden?: boolean; includeSectionHeadings?: boolean }` — both default `false / true` respectively. `includeHidden: true` is for the admin UI which lists everything including `exposed: false` drafts; the planner gets the visible-only catalog.
      - Empty-model branch returns a stable single-line `_(empty — no metrics, dimensions, or hierarchies declared; fall back to raw `execute_query_plan` against the dataset schema)_` block. Hidden-only models (every entry `exposed: false`) collapse to the same empty branch — the planner never sees the empty `### Metrics (0)` heading.
      - Populated models render: `## Semantic catalog (vN — <name>)` header, a single instruction line `Prefer execute_metric_query when the question maps to one of these metrics; fall back to execute_query_plan only when no metric matches.`, then three sections (Metrics / Dimensions / Hierarchies) each with `### <Section> (count)` heading + bullet block per entry. Empty sections render `_(none)_` so the per-section count + structural shape stay byte-stable across models.
      - Exported helpers `formatMetricLines(m)`, `formatDimensionLines(d)`, `formatHierarchyLines(h)` return the canonical line arrays per entry; callers that want to embed a single item in a different context (narrator-side citation expansion, admin tooltip) reuse the same byte shape without re-implementing the formatting rules.
      - Metric block: ` ``- `name` — label`` `, indented `Expression: `<expr>``, `Format: <hint>` (where `currency (INR)` is rendered when `format === "currency"` + `currencyCode` is set; `, N dp` is appended when `decimals` is set), `References: a, b, c` (only when `m.references.length > 0`), `<description (one-line collapsed)>` (only when present).
      - Dimension block: name + label header, `Column: `<col>``, `Kind: <kind>` with `(grain)` suffix when `kind === "temporal" && temporalGrain`, optional one-lined description.
      - Hierarchy block: name + label header, `Levels: country → region → city` (joined with ` → `), optional one-lined description.
      - Internal helpers: `visibleMetrics` / `visibleDimensions` clone-then-filter-then-sort so the caller's model is never mutated. `sortedHierarchies` clone-then-sort (no exposed flag on hierarchies). All sorts are `a.name.localeCompare(b.name)` ascending — stable under repeated identical inputs.
      - `oneLine(s)` collapses any internal whitespace (newlines + repeated spaces) to single spaces and trims, so a description authored as `"line one\n\n  line two"` renders as a single line in the manifest. Prevents accidental re-indentation from corrupting the markdown structure.
    - [server/tests/semanticPromptW59a.test.ts](server/tests/semanticPromptW59a.test.ts) (new, ~335 LOC). 19 cases across 7 suites; appended to [server/package.json](server/package.json) per invariant #4:
      - **Empty model** (2): stable `(empty —` marker on `version: 3` model with no entries; hidden-only model collapses to the same empty branch.
      - **Metrics section** (6): single currency metric renders code + label + expression + `currency (INR), 2 dp` hint + references line; alphabetical sort regardless of input order; `exposed: false` hidden by default, shown with `includeHidden: true` (count line bumps from `(1)` to `(2)`); empty references suppresses the References line; non-currency format omits the parenthetical code; multi-line description collapsed to single line.
      - **Dimensions section** (3): categorical kind has no grain suffix; temporal kind renders `(month)` when grain is set; alphabetical sort regardless of input order.
      - **Hierarchies section** (2): levels joined with ` → `; alphabetical sort.
      - **Byte stability** (2): two identical models produce identical output; same model with different input ordering produces identical output (key prompt-cache property — input ordering cannot perturb manifest bytes).
      - **Section heading toggle** (1): `includeSectionHeadings: false` removes `### Metrics` / `### Dimensions` / `### Hierarchies` lines but keeps the entry blocks.
      - **Direct helpers** (3): `formatMetricLines` / `formatDimensionLines` / `formatHierarchyLines` each return the exact expected line array (anchors the byte shape; any future formatting tweak will trip these tests).
      - 19/19 passing.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Pure-function split.** `prompt.ts` is a 175 LOC pure helper with no `planner.ts` import. W59b's prompt rewrite is then a 1-line call site that asks `formatMetricCatalog(model)` and inlines the result. Splitting the concerns lets us unit-test the rendering exhaustively without standing up a full planner prompt fixture. The W59a/W59b atomic split also keeps `planner.ts` edits to a minimum diff for W59b, which preserves the prompt-cache breakpoints WW1+WW2+WQ2 have already established.
    - **Byte-stability is a prompt-cache contract.** Per Anthropic's 2026 prompt-caching guidance, the 5-minute TTL means cache only helps within a session — and a single character of drift in the cache prefix invalidates it. The manifest sits inside the planner prompt, which is read across every planner LLM call in a session. The sort + filter + line-shape contract here guarantees that two LLM calls in the same session see the exact same manifest bytes whenever the model is unchanged. Tests `produces identical output for two identical models` and `same model in different input order yields identical output` are the canary; if a future PR breaks them, the wave should be rolled back.
    - **Filter `exposed: false` by default.** The schema's `exposed: false` is the data team's way of marking a draft metric in the admin UI — the planner should never see it. Default `includeHidden: false` is the conservative path; admin UI flips it on. Same treatment for dimensions.
    - **Mutation-free.** `[...model.metrics].sort(...)` clones first. The semantic model lives on `ChatDocument.semanticModel` (Cosmos-persisted); mutating it during prompt rendering would be a silent bug.
    - **Hierarchies have no `exposed` flag.** The schema doesn't expose hierarchies as filterable by exposure — they're either declared or not. The helper reflects this: it sorts but does not filter hierarchies. Future schema waves can add a flag without changing the helper's external API (it would just plumb through `visibleHierarchies` mirroring `visibleMetrics`).
    - **`(none)` placeholder vs. dropping the section.** Even when one section is empty the helper renders `### Section (0)\n\n_(none)_\n` rather than skipping the section. This keeps the prompt structurally stable for the LLM — "the catalog has three sections, one is empty" reads better than "the catalog has two sections, where did the third one go?". And it makes the byte-stability contract simpler: same model → same byte structure, no conditional section presence.
    - **Empty-everything is a single line, not three empty sections.** When the model has zero exposed metrics / dimensions / hierarchies, the helper short-circuits to the parenthetical empty marker. The planner sees a clear "no semantic layer applicable here" signal rather than three empty `_(none)_` sections — the planner can fall straight back to `execute_query_plan` against the dataset schema.
    - **Currency hint as `currency (INR)` not `currency, INR`.** Lets `Format: currency (INR), 2 dp` parse left-to-right as `<kind> [<currency-code>] [, <decimals>]`. A future wave could parse this back out of the manifest for round-trip cache key hashing without ambiguity.

  **Verified.** `npm run typecheck` on server reports 98 errors, identical to WQ3 baseline — zero new from W59a. New helper has no consumers yet (W59b is the next wave) so no integration tests change. 19/19 new unit tests pass under `node --import tsx --test`. Code commit `791007f6`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **The planner prompt rewrite itself (W59b).** The helper is unused until W59b inlines a call in `buildPlannerUserPrompt` (or its system-prompt equivalent — TBD). Atomic separation is intentional; W59b is the next wave and will assert the manifest is wired without re-litigating the byte-shape contract.
    - **`execute_metric_query` tool dispatch (W60).** The tool that consumes `compileMetricQuery` from the planner's perspective. Until W59b tells the planner the tool exists, W60 has no caller. Out of W59a's atomic scope.
    - **Admin UI for editing the semantic model (W61).** `formatMetricCatalog` is the rendering primitive an admin tooltip / preview will use, but the admin page itself is a separate client-side wave.
    - **Manifest size budget / truncation.** The 1000x master plan estimates a ~2 KB manifest budget for the planner prompt. The helper does not currently enforce a cap — a pathological model with 200 metrics × 200 dimensions × 50 hierarchies (the schema maxes) could blow the budget. A future wave can add a `maxLength` option that drops `exposed: false`-but-still-passing entries or truncates descriptions. W57's inferModel realistically produces tens of metrics, not hundreds, so this is a future concern, not a present one.
    - **Tests against `inferModel` output.** The helper is tested against hand-crafted models. A property-style test that runs `inferModel` over a representative `DataSummary` fixture and asserts the manifest renders is a follow-on; doesn't need to live in W59a.
    - **Cache key derivation.** The 1000x plan's Workstream 1 W64 introduces metric query result cache keyed by `(modelVersion, metricName, dimensions, filters, window)`. The byte-stable manifest could itself serve as a cache key for the planner prompt — that's a separate caching wave (W69 cache breakpoints + metrics), not a W59a concern.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WQ3 · citation hover-cards in narrator prose (client).** W22's server-side anti-hallucination gate ([checkEnvelopeCompleteness.ts:120](server/lib/agents/runtime/checkEnvelopeCompleteness.ts)) guarantees that every backtick-wrapped domain-pack id in narrator prose (e.g. `` `marico-haircare-portfolio` ``) is a real pack from the supplied CONTEXT BUNDLE — no hallucinated citations can ship. But on the client, the custom [`MarkdownRenderer`](client/src/components/ui/markdown-renderer.tsx) was rendering those tokens as plain inline text indistinguishable from any other backtick code-span. Users had no visual signal that a particular claim was grounded in a specific domain pack vs. a generic backticked identifier (column name, acronym), so the citation work W22 enforces was effectively invisible. WQ3 surfaces the citations as superscript Radix hover-cards: when the renderer detects a backtick-wrapped pack id, it replaces the inline code with a numbered superscript pill that opens a hover-card showing the pack's humanised label, canonical id, and a pointer to the admin domain-context surface for the full pack body.

  **What landed.**
    - [client/src/lib/citationTokens.ts](client/src/lib/citationTokens.ts) (new, ~95 LOC). Pure detector mirroring W22's server-side `CITATION_TOKEN_RE` byte-for-byte: `` /`([a-z][a-z0-9-]{4,})`/g `` plus the same hyphen-rule heuristic (tokens without a hyphen are NOT treated as citations — filters `Volume_MT`, `Region`, etc.). Exports:
      - `CITATION_TOKEN_RE` — the regex itself, exported so a future test can pin parity with the server source on every change.
      - `extractCitations(text)` — splits a text fragment into alternating `{ type: "text", value } | { type: "citation", packId, raw }` segments. Empty input → empty array. Bytewise roundtrip property: concatenating each segment's `value` / `raw` reproduces the input. Fresh regex per call (avoids global-regex `lastIndex` bleed across invocations).
      - `listCitedPackIds(text)` — unique pack ids in first-occurrence order (for callers that need to enumerate without walking segments twice).
      - `formatCitationLabel(packId)` — humanises kebab-case (`marico-haircare-portfolio` → `Marico Haircare Portfolio`) for the hover-card header.
    - [client/src/components/CitationHoverCard.tsx](client/src/components/CitationHoverCard.tsx) (new, ~60 LOC). React component wrapping the existing Radix [`HoverCard`](client/src/components/ui/hover-card.tsx) primitive (already in the codebase — no new dep). Renders a small `[N]` superscript pill, dotted-underline + primary-tinted, with `data-citation-pack-id` for downstream selector / e2e use. The hover content is metadata-only: humanised label, canonical id (monospace), explanation block pointing users to **Admin · Domain Context** for the full body. `openDelay: 150ms` / `closeDelay: 100ms` matches the rest of the app's hover-card timings.
    - [client/src/components/ui/markdown-renderer.tsx](client/src/components/ui/markdown-renderer.tsx) edit (~70 LOC). Top of `MarkdownRenderer` builds a per-render `citationIndex: Map<packId, 1-based-index>` once via the new `buildCitationIndex` helper — repeated citations of the same pack get the same superscript number across the message. The index is threaded through `parseMarkdownLine` → `parseInlineMarkdown` → a new `renderTextWithCitations` helper. The latter splits plain-text segments via `extractCitations` and replaces each citation segment with a `<CitationHoverCard packId={packId} index={index} />` node. Citations inside `**bold**` and `*italic*` spans are also detected (the bold / italic processing now recursively defers to `parseInlineMarkdown`). When no citations are present, `renderTextWithCitations` short-circuits to return the input text unchanged so byte-stable rendering of citation-free prose is preserved.
    - Stable React keys: citation nodes use `key={`citation-${counter}-${packId}`}` so React's reconciler doesn't churn across re-renders. The `index` (superscript number) is computed from the citation order in the full message, not the index within a span — so a citation that appears in bold AND a re-citation in plain prose both show `[1]` and correlate visually.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Pure helper + thin React wrapper.** Splitting `citationTokens.ts` (pure) from `CitationHoverCard.tsx` (React) lets us unit-test the detector with `node:test` (server harness), no DOM required. The React component is tested implicitly via the integration path. Pinning the regex shape vs. the W22 server regex catches silent drift if either side is refactored.
    - **Reuse the existing Radix HoverCard.** The codebase already wraps `@radix-ui/react-hover-card` at [`client/src/components/ui/hover-card.tsx`](client/src/components/ui/hover-card.tsx). No new dependency, consistent visual treatment with other hover surfaces (e.g. `@/components/ui/tooltip`).
    - **Metadata-only hover content (no snippet body).** The admin endpoint `fetchDomainContextPacks` returns `{ id, title, category, priority, version, approxTokens, enabled }` — no pack body. Exposing the body would require either (a) a new public endpoint (server-side wave), (b) inlining pack snippets into the session envelope (heavier; potentially leaks content of disabled packs), or (c) a per-mount fetch from the client (admin-gated, would 401 for regular users). Atomic scope for WQ3 means surfacing the citation as a visual anchor + explanation; piping the body in is the natural follow-on wave (and the admin-gated approach is what an analytics user actually expects).
    - **Stable per-message numbering.** Computing the index map once at the top of `MarkdownRenderer` keeps numbering stable across re-renders of the same message and lets repeated citations of the same pack share a single visual identity. Computing per-line or per-span would assign `[1]`, `[2]`, `[3]` to three repeats of `marico-haircare-portfolio` — confusing.
    - **Recursion into bold + italic.** Pre-WQ3, citations inside bold (e.g. `**Per `marico-haircare-portfolio`, MT leads.**`) would not have been detected because `parseInlineMarkdown` only ran on non-bold spans. The recursion change is minimal (re-call `parseInlineMarkdown` on the bold/italic inner text instead of dropping it as a plain string) but means citations are always picked up regardless of formatting.
    - **Byte-stable for citation-free prose.** `renderTextWithCitations` returns `[text]` when no citations are present — the existing rendering path for prose without citations is unchanged. Guards against unintended formatting drift on every message; pinned via the test suite's "no citations → single text segment" case.

  **Tests.** [client/src/lib/citationTokens.test.ts](client/src/lib/citationTokens.test.ts) — 20 cases across 5 suites:
    - **Regex parity with W22** (2): `CITATION_TOKEN_RE.source` exactly equals the server's `` `([a-z][a-z0-9-]{4,})` ``; length floor anchors (2-char / 4-char rejected; 5-char accepted).
    - **Hyphen rule** (4): `marico-haircare-portfolio` extracted; `Volume_MT` not; `mtsales` not (≥5 chars but hyphen-less); short hyphenated `a-b` not (under 5 chars).
    - **Segment shape** (8): empty input; no-citation input; text+citation+text; bytewise roundtrip preservation; leading citation; trailing citation; adjacent citations; fresh regex per call (no `lastIndex` bleed).
    - **`listCitedPackIds` dedupe in first-occurrence order** (3): empty input; same id cited twice deduped; distinct ids preserve first-occurrence order even on re-citation.
    - **`formatCitationLabel` humanisation** (3): kebab-case → title-cased space-separated; single-word; empty / all-hyphens input → empty.
    - 20/20 passing. Appended to [server/package.json](server/package.json)'s explicit test list (the client test list embedded inside the server test runner) per invariant #4.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` on server reports 98 errors, identical to WQ7 baseline. `npx tsc --noEmit` on client reports 53 errors, identical to the client baseline. Zero new from WQ3. Code commit `3fd78ab1`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Pack snippet body in the hover-card.** Requires either a new server endpoint (`/api/domain-context/packs/:id/snippet`) or session-envelope extension to carry enabled pack snippets to the client. Either path is its own wave; metadata-only hover is the atomic WQ3 scope. The hover content already invites users to "see Admin · Domain Context for the full pack body" — a natural breadcrumb for the follow-on.
    - **In-message footnote list.** Some chat apps render citations as `[1] marico-haircare-portfolio (link)` at the bottom of the message. Could pair well with the superscript pills. Skipped here for atomicity; `listCitedPackIds` is exported so a future wave can consume it without re-walking the prose.
    - **Click-to-open behaviour.** Hover-only for now. A future wave could make `<sup>` clickable to deep-link into the admin domain-context surface filtered by pack id. The `data-citation-pack-id` attribute is wired so any wave that adds the click handler has a stable selector.
    - **Insight component citations.** The hover-card mechanism is wired into `MarkdownRenderer` — the only renderer for narrator prose in `MessageBubble` + `AnswerCard`. Other surfaces (e.g. chart insights, key insights, deck slides) render prose through different paths. If those gain pack citations in a future wave, the helper functions in `citationTokens.ts` are designed to be reusable; only the React component wiring would need duplication.
    - **Persistence of seen-citation state.** The hover-card opens on hover but does not record which packs the user has explored. A future telemetry wave could log this.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WQ7 · significance score by default on `run_two_segment_compare` + `run_breakdown_ranking`.** Extends the deterministic-floor evidence-carriage chain (WV4 correlation, WV5 significance, WV6 elasticity, WV7 segment-driver) to the two composite-style segment-comparison tools that had no inline statistical evidence on their summaries. Pre-WQ7, the `run_two_segment_compare` summary carried only the aggregated metric values for both segments + a mix ratio (`rate_ratio_A_per_B`), and `run_breakdown_ranking` carried only the ranked top-N rows — both had a meaningful per-row significance test available (the underlying row-level metric values are right there) but neither emitted p or n on the summary. WQ1 was therefore grading every segment-compare finding and every breakdown-ranking "the top region is the leader" finding as `medium / no evidence supplied`. WQ7 runs Welch's t-test by default on each tool's natural cohort split (A vs. B for the compare tool; headline group vs. all-others-combined for the ranking tool) and appends the canonical `(n = N; p = X)` suffix to the success-path summary so WW2's extractor catches the evidence and WQ1's tier classifier grades the finding on real numbers.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/twoSegmentCompareTool.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/twoSegmentCompareTool.ts) edit (~50 LOC):
      - New imports: `runSignificanceTest` from [`../../../significanceTests.js`](server/lib/significanceTests.ts), `composeFindingDetail` from [`../formatFindingEvidence.js`](server/lib/agents/runtime/formatFindingEvidence.ts), `type FindingEvidence` from [`../scaleNarrativeByConfidence.js`](server/lib/agents/runtime/scaleNarrativeByConfidence.ts).
      - `aggregateSegment` extended to also return `values: number[]` — the row-level numeric values for the metric column inside the filtered segment, collected during the existing sum / mean / count pass. For `count` mode the values array is empty (skipped downstream). Previously these values were folded into `sum` and discarded; now they ride along for the t-test.
      - New helper `buildSegmentCompareEvidence(aggregation, valuesA, valuesB)` runs `runSignificanceTest({ test: "welch_t", sampleA: valuesA, sampleB: valuesB })` when `aggregation ∈ {mean, sum}` AND both segments have ≥3 finite obs, builds `{ pValue, n: nA + nB }`, returns `composeFindingDetail("", evidence)`. Skips on count aggregation (different test shape; proportion Z-test needs a global baseline the tool doesn't carry) and on insufficient n. All exceptions short-circuit to `""`.
      - Success-path summary concatenates `wq7EvidenceSuffix` at the end: `` `run_two_segment_compare: ${aggregation}(${metricColumn}) for "${A}" vs "${B}" (capped_input=${frame0.length}).\n${sample.slice(0, 4500)}${wq7EvidenceSuffix}` ``. When the suffix is empty (count / insufficient n / failure), summary is byte-identical to pre-WQ7.
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/breakdownRankingTool.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/tools/breakdownRankingTool.ts) edit (~70 LOC):
      - Same import block.
      - New helper `buildBreakdownRankingEvidence(frame, breakdownColumn, metricColumn, topGroupLabel, aggregation)` does a second pass over the frame, splitting row-level metric values into the headline (top-ranked) group vs. all other groups combined. Runs `runSignificanceTest({ test: "welch_t", sampleA: topValues, sampleB: otherValues })`. Same skip rules as the compare tool (count / insufficient n). Returns the canonical suffix or `""`. The two-pass design — `aggregate` reduces sum/count per group first, then the helper makes a second values pass for exactly two buckets — keeps memory bounded: capturing values per group would explode on high-cardinality breakdowns (e.g. 5,000 SKUs × N rows of values arrays).
      - Simple-path return only — the composite (rankBy) branch is scope-bounded out. Composite ranking aggregates multiple metrics via a user-provided expression; "is the top group different on the *score*?" is ill-posed for a t-test (the score is a weighted combination, not a sample). Future waves can add a per-metric or per-component test if needed.
      - Headline group label resolved from `trimmed[0][breakdownColumn]` (the post-sort top row); `null` rows fall back to `"(null)"` to match the upstream `aggregate` key normalisation.
      - Success-path summary concatenates `wq7EvidenceSuffix` at the end of the simple-path return only.
    - Both tools share the same `runSignificanceTest` from [significanceTests.ts](server/lib/significanceTests.ts) (F3 / WV5). No new math dependency, no t-CDF / chi-square implementation; the WV5 helper already handles Welch–Satterthwaite df + Hill (1970) survival function for the t-distribution.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Cohort split that matches the tool's natural question.** Two-segment compare is literally about A vs. B — that's the t-test. Breakdown ranking implicitly stages a "leader vs. field" comparison — the headline finding the narrator's prose around the top row implies. Both splits are unambiguous; neither requires the planner to specify the comparison. The tool answers what its name promises.
    - **Welch's t-test on row-level values, not on aggregates.** A t-test on two `sum` values would have df=0 and zero variance — it's not a statistical test. A t-test on the underlying row-level values *is* a test: it asks "do the per-row metric values differ between segments meaningfully relative to within-segment variance?".
