This is the right question for both `mean` (where it's also the natural test of the aggregate) and `sum` (where it gracefully reframes the sum question as "are per-row magnitudes different?" — usually what the narrator's prose around the top row actually means).
    - **Skip count aggregation.** Count is the only aggregation where the row-level values aren't a meaningful sample (you'd be comparing "1, 1, 1, 1" vs. "1, 1, 1"). The natural test for "are the count proportions different from the global baseline?" is a Z-test for proportions or a chi-square, and both need a baseline the tool doesn't carry. Skipping is correct; future waves can add a `baseline` arg if needed.
    - **Top-vs-rest for breakdown ranking, not top-vs-second.** "Is region X the leader?" is the headline finding; the relevant comparison is "X vs. everything-not-X", not "X vs. the next region". The latter is a noisier signal (sample of one comparison column) that the narrator rarely cares about — the prose is "X leads with $5M, far above the rest" not "X leads with $5M vs Y at $4M".
    - **Two-pass over the frame, not values-per-group.** Capturing `values: number[]` per group inside `aggregate` would mean N × G memory for high-cardinality breakdowns. The second pass for exactly two buckets (top + other) is one extra O(N) scan — typically <1ms on the diagnostic slice cap (~5k rows) — and keeps the existing `aggregate` Map values cheap.
    - **Composite ranking explicitly excluded, asserted in source-inspection tests.** A future refactor could accidentally invoke `buildBreakdownRankingEvidence` from the composite branch; the test `composite (rankBy) path summary is unchanged (WQ7 scope-bounded)` guards against it.
    - **Empty-suffix on skip / failure is the contract.** Mirrors WV4-WV7. Empty `topValues` or `otherValues` (single-group frame) → empty suffix → byte-stable summary. NaN-only values → empty suffix. `runSignificanceTest` returns `ok: false` for nA/nB < 3 → empty suffix. Failure modes are silent and observable only by the absence of the canonical evidence block.

  **Tests.**
    - [tests/twoSegmentCompareSignificanceWQ7.test.ts](server/tests/twoSegmentCompareSignificanceWQ7.test.ts) — 7 cases across 3 suites: source-inspection wiring (imports + `aggregateSegment.values` exposure + `buildSegmentCompareEvidence` definition + summary concatenation), math anchor (clearly-different segments → p < 0.001, recovered via `extractFindingEvidence`; identical samples → p = 1, suffix still emitted), skip semantics (<3 obs → upstream fails; empty `FindingEvidence` → empty suffix).
    - [tests/breakdownRankingSignificanceWQ7.test.ts](server/tests/breakdownRankingSignificanceWQ7.test.ts) — 8 cases across 3 suites: source-inspection wiring (imports + helper definition with count short-circuit + simple-path summary concat + composite-path is unchanged), math anchor (top-vs-rest with clearly-stratified vs. marginal differences; both recoverable via `extractFindingEvidence`), skip semantics (empty evidence → empty suffix + the call-site count assertion that proves `buildBreakdownRankingEvidence` is called exactly once = simple-path only, composite stays untouched).
    - 15/15 passing. Both files appended to [server/package.json](server/package.json) per invariant #4.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors, identical to WV8 baseline — zero new from WQ7. Code commit `8a45067b`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Composite ranking significance.** A composite expression like `(growth * 0.6) + (share * 0.4)` is a weighted combination; the headline finding is "top group by composite score" but a t-test on the score requires the per-row score to be computable, which would need ANOTHER pass to compute the expression per-row, not per-group. Could ship as a separate wave; out of WQ7's atomic scope.
    - **Top-N significance (not just top-1).** Currently only the headline (top-ranked) group's evidence is on the summary. The same Welch's t-test could be run for each of the top-K groups, with K configurable. Skipped here because the narrator's prose around top-K is usually "X, Y, Z are the leaders" — a multi-group test of equal means (one-way ANOVA / Kruskal-Wallis) is the right shape, not multiple pairwise t-tests. Separate wave.
    - **Effect size on the suffix.** WV5 / WV6 / WV7 also defer Cohen's d (and the FindingEvidence `effectMagnitude` field needed to carry it). Same dormancy debt — its own wave touching the formatter + extractor + classifier.
    - **Confidence interval on the test difference.** WV4 / WV5 / WV6 / WV7 all defer this too; the `±X%` slot in the FindingEvidence formatter is unused on every statistical tool migration so far. A future wave could promote it for `welch_t` (CI on the mean difference) and `chi_square` (CI on Cramér's V).
    - **Proportion Z-test for the count aggregation.** Would need a global baseline (e.g. the count's expected proportion under uniform allocation, or a baseline period). Defer until a planner hint or tool arg surfaces the baseline.
    - **Per-segment / per-group breakdown of evidence inside `numericPayload`.** The current return only emits the headline evidence on the summary; structured `Finding.evidence` per-group is a future schema wave.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WV8 · `critic_verdict` SSE surfaces `ConfidenceOverclaimReport` tier counts.** Closes the WV1–WV7 deterministic-floor series with end-user-visible feedback. WV3 wired the verifier-side short-circuit so the narrator gets `revise_narrative` whenever it inflates confidence past WQ1's floor (n ≥ 30, p ≤ 0.05, R² ≥ 0.5, CI ≤ 30%) — but the underlying `ConfidenceOverclaimReport` (claimed vs. actual tier counts per the WQ1 classifier) was discarded after the verdict was built. The user saw `Verdict: revise_narrative; Issues: CONFIDENCE_OVERCLAIM` in the workbench critic entry but had no signal as to WHAT was overclaimed — was it 5 high-claimed magnitudes against 0 supporting findings? 3 against 2? Without the magnitudes the workbench entry is opaque, and the engineering-facing utility of the WV3 short-circuit is diminished. WV8 threads the report end-to-end so the workbench renders a one-line summary `Narrator confidence: claimed Xh/Ym/Zl; blackboard supports Xh/Ym/Zl` alongside the existing verdict line.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/types.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/types.ts) edit (~12 LOC): `VerifierResult` gains optional `confidenceOverclaim?: ConfidenceOverclaimReport` field, typed via lazy `import("./verifierConfidenceCheck.js").ConfidenceOverclaimReport` so the existing module-graph shape (types.ts imports from siblings like `analyticalBlackboard.js`, `investigationTree.js`) is unchanged. Existing consumers stay valid; the field is optional and only populated on the WV3 short-circuit path.
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/verifier.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/verifier.ts) edit (~6 LOC): the WV3 block-or-warning short-circuit return now spreads `confidenceOverclaim: report` onto the returned `VerifierResult`. The deep-LLM path and all other early-return paths leave the field undefined.
    - [server/lib/agents/runtime/agentLoop.service.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/agentLoop.service.ts) edits (~25 LOC across two `safeEmit("critic_verdict", ...)` call sites, line ~2068 per-step + line ~3782 FINAL): each emit spreads a `confidence_overclaim: { claimed, actual }` payload only when the verdict carries the field, shaped to drop the internal `flags[]` + `shouldRevise` (the former is verbose and already encoded in `issues[]`; the latter is implied by `verdict === reviseNarrative`). The per-step site's spread is defensive — per-step verifier rounds never see a `NarratorOutput` so the report is always undefined there, but the symmetry future-proofs against a wave that wires narrator state into the per-step path.
    - [server/services/chat/agentWorkbench.util.ts](server/services/chat/agentWorkbench.util.ts) edit (~50 LOC): new `ConfidenceTierCountsSse` type; `CriticSse` gains optional `confidence_overclaim?: { claimed?, actual? }`. New module-private helper `formatConfidenceOverclaim(oc)` renders the canonical line `Narrator confidence: claimed Xh/Ym/Zl; blackboard supports Xh/Ym/Zl` — `h/m/l` shorthand keeps the line tight, the full word `Narrator confidence:` anchors what's being compared so the line is self-explanatory in the workbench without prior context. The line is wired into the existing `parts[]` array of the `critic_verdict` branch in `agentSseEventToWorkbenchEntries`, between the `Issues:` line and the `Course correction:` line. `parts.filter(Boolean)` drops the empty string when the field is absent so pass verdicts and non-overclaim revise_narrative verdicts stay byte-stable with pre-WV8.
    - Defensive parsing: a `clamp(v)` helper inside `formatConfidenceOverclaim` rejects non-number / non-finite values (e.g. JSON-injected NaN, negative integers) via `Number.isFinite` and `Math.max(0, Math.floor(v))`. All-zero counts on both sides return the empty string so the helper never emits a vacuous `claimed 0h/0m/0l; supports 0h/0m/0l` line.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Thread the report through `VerifierResult`, not re-derive at emit time.** The alternative was to re-run `detectConfidenceOverclaims(narratorOutput, blackboard)` at the `safeEmit` site in `agentLoop.service.ts`. That would double the WQ1 tier-classification cost (cheap but not free) and would require threading the narrator output to a second consumer. Threading the already-computed report through the verdict matches the verifier's existing pattern (e.g. `scores?`, `user_visible_note?` are also optional fields populated only on certain paths). One source of truth for the report; the emit site is a pure projection.
    - **Lazy `import(...)` type reference vs. eager `import type` at the top of `types.ts`.** Eager would be cleaner stylistically but `types.ts` is widely imported and any new top-level import touches its dependency surface — preferable to keep the new field's type narrow to the one place that needs it. `import("./verifierConfidenceCheck.js").ConfidenceOverclaimReport` resolves at type-check time without affecting runtime import order.
    - **Drop `flags[]` + `shouldRevise` from the SSE payload.** The verdict already encodes `shouldRevise` (it's `reviseNarrative` whenever the report's `shouldRevise` was true). The `flags[]` array carries verbose per-flag messages already surfaced as `issues[].description` — re-shipping them would duplicate the workbench's `Course correction:` line. Shipping only `claimed` + `actual` keeps the payload minimal (≤200 bytes typical) and unambiguous: counts go to the workbench renderer; the human-readable rationale stays in the existing course-correction prose.
    - **`h/m/l` shorthand, not `high/medium/low`.** The line lives in the workbench critic-entry `code` block alongside other one-liners. `claimed 5h/0m/0l; supports 2h/1m/1l` is 12 characters tighter per side than `claimed 5 high, 0 medium, 0 low; supports 2 high, 1 medium, 1 low`. The full word `Narrator confidence:` at the start anchors the reading, so the shorthand stays unambiguous even on cold read.
    - **All-zero suppression.** `formatConfidenceOverclaim` returns the empty string when both sides are zero — the helper's caller filters via `parts.filter(Boolean)`, so the empty string is dropped from the rendered code block. This guards against the edge case where the WV3 detector fires on a degenerate `narratorOutput` (no magnitudes, no implications) with an empty blackboard — claiming `0h/0m/0l vs supports 0h/0m/0l` is vacuous and would clutter the workbench.
    - **Per-step + final emit symmetry.** Both `safeEmit("critic_verdict", ...)` call sites in `agentLoop.service.ts` are updated identically. The per-step site will *currently* never emit a non-empty `confidence_overclaim` (no narrator output exists yet at per-step granularity), but encoding the spread defensively means a future wave that wires narrator state into per-step verifier rounds (e.g. for partial revisions during long investigations) gets workbench surfacing for free.

  **Tests.** [tests/criticVerdictConfidenceOverclaimWV8.test.ts](server/tests/criticVerdictConfidenceOverclaimWV8.test.ts) — 7 cases across 3 suites:
    - **Source-inspection wiring** (4): `VerifierResult` declares `confidenceOverclaim?` typed against `verifierConfidenceCheck.ConfidenceOverclaimReport`; `verifier.ts` WV3 short-circuit return includes `confidenceOverclaim: report`; `agentLoop.service.ts` BOTH critic_verdict emit sites check `verdict.confidenceOverclaim` / `fv.confidenceOverclaim` and spread `confidence_overclaim: { claimed: ... }` (regex match enforces ≥2 occurrences); `agentWorkbench.util.ts` defines `formatConfidenceOverclaim` and `CriticSse` carries the optional `confidence_overclaim?:` field.
    - **Behavioural rendering** (3): calling `agentSseEventToWorkbenchEntries("critic_verdict", payload)` with a populated `confidence_overclaim` produces a workbench entry whose `code` contains `Narrator confidence: claimed 5h/0m/0l; blackboard supports 2h/1m/1l`; calling it without the field produces no `Narrator confidence` line (no regression on pass verdicts); calling it with malformed counts (NaN, negative, fractional, missing actual, all-zero) clamps to non-negative integers and either suppresses the line (all-zero) or substitutes a default (`0h/0m/0l` for missing actual).
    - 7/7 passing. Appended to [server/package.json](server/package.json) per invariant #4.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors, identical to WV7 baseline — zero new from WV8. The new types-ts lazy import works at type-check time without runtime cycles. Code commit `0643db42`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Client-side rich rendering of the tier-counts.** The workbench renderer is server-side (the entries are persisted as `code: string`); the client just displays the persisted text. A future wave could ship a structured renderer (e.g. a small bar chart visualising claimed vs. actual tier distributions) — that's a UI wave with its own client-side schema concerns.
    - **`flags[]` surfacing in workbench.** The flags' human-readable messages live in the verifier's `issues[].description` and surface in the existing `Course correction:` line. A future wave could deduplicate the duplication, but the cost is small and the prose serves a different audience than the tier counts.
    - **Per-step narrator output for partial revisions.** WV3 / WV8 only fire on the final verifier round because that's where the narrator output exists. Threading narrator state to per-step rounds would let intermediate revisions also catch overclaim — its own wave (the per-step emit symmetry in agentLoop.service.ts is the wave's hook for that future work).
    - **Persistence of `confidence_overclaim` to the chat document.** The SSE payload is workbench-only; not currently persisted with the final verifier verdict on the `ChatDocument`. A future wave could add `verifierVerdicts[].confidenceOverclaim` to the trace if cross-session analytics or audit needs require it. The workbench entry is persisted (per the existing W10 contract), so the line is recoverable via the persisted `code` string — just not as structured data.

- **2026-05-18** — **Wave WV7 · `run_segment_driver_analysis` migrated to `composeFindingDetail` (R² + n).** Fourth and final per-tool migration in the WV4 series. The WW1 → WW2 → WV1 → WV2 → WV3 chain has been structurally complete since WV3 wired the verifier-side short-circuit, but only three of the four high-volume statistical tools were emitting findings with the canonical phrasing the WW2 extractor recovers deterministically — WV4 promoted `run_correlation`'s strongest-pair R² + n, WV5 promoted `run_significance_test`'s p + effective n across all three sub-tests, WV6 promoted `run_price_elasticity`'s headline group's R² + n. The composite `run_segment_driver_analysis` was the last gap: it calls `analyzeCorrelations` internally on a `dimensionFilters`-narrowed slice and emits a correlation chart + insights, but the slice's R² + n weren't surfaced in the success-path summary, so WQ1 was still grading segment-driver correlation findings as `medium / no evidence supplied`. WV7 closes the immediate per-tool migration backlog for statistical findings; remaining tool migrations are second-order (effect-size as a fifth evidence field; per-group tier carriage; deck-level evidence merging) and require schema or formatter changes rather than the WV4-template tool wrapper edit.

  **What landed.**
    - [server/lib/segmentDriverAnalysisTool.ts](server/lib/segmentDriverAnalysisTool.ts) edit (~24 LOC):
      - New imports: `composeFindingDetail` from [`./agents/runtime/formatFindingEvidence.js`](server/lib/agents/runtime/formatFindingEvidence.ts), `type FindingEvidence` from [`./agents/runtime/scaleNarrativeByConfidence.js`](server/lib/agents/runtime/scaleNarrativeByConfidence.ts). Note the import path depth — segment driver lives one level above `agents/runtime/`, not inside `agents/runtime/tools/` like the other migrated tools, so the relative paths are `./agents/runtime/…` rather than `../formatFindingEvidence.js`.
      - The correlation branch (the third entry in the parallel `branches[]` array, the one that calls `analyzeCorrelations` on the filtered slice) destructures `topCorrelations` from the analyzer return — the optional field WV4 plumbed through `analyzeCorrelations`'s return type at [correlationAnalyzer.ts:111](server/lib/correlationAnalyzer.ts#L111). Pre-WV7 the branch destructured `{ charts, insights }` only and dropped the rest.
      - Builds `wv7EvidenceSuffix` from the strongest correlation when `topCorrelations` is non-empty: `R² = strongest.correlation²` (guarded `Number.isFinite && 0 ≤ R² ≤ 1`); `n = strongest.nPairs` (guarded `≥ 0`). When the analyzer produced no correlations (early-return / filter eliminated all), `topCorrelations` is undefined or empty, the guard short-circuits, and `wv7EvidenceSuffix === ""`.
      - Correlation branch text becomes `` `Correlation scan on filtered slice (n=${slice.length}) for **${outcome}**.${wv7EvidenceSuffix}` ``. When the suffix is empty, the text is byte-identical to pre-WV7.
    - Downstream path is *unchanged*: the parallel-branches loop joins each branch's `text` with `\n\n` and the composite tool returns the joined string as `summary`. The agent's centralised `addFinding` in [agentLoop.service.ts](server/lib/agents/runtime/agentLoop.service.ts) reads that summary as the blackboard finding's `detail`. WW2's extractor matches the first `R² = X` / `n = N` it sees in the prose — which, with WV7, is the correlation branch's canonical suffix anchored at the end of that line.

  **Why this design.**
    - **Pick the strongest correlation, not all of them.** The correlation branch may produce many `topCorrelations` (the analyzer caps at 20 here); appending evidence for each would inflate the summary and the WW2 extractor only reads the first match. The headline result is the strongest correlation (sorted by |r| descending — the same sort `analyzeCorrelations` applies internally for chart selection), which is also the correlation the narrator builds prose around. Future waves with structured `Finding.evidence` per-correlation would carry per-pair tiers without changing this baseline.
    - **Mirror WV4 exactly, not WV5/WV6.** WV5 introduced a `buildEvidenceSuffix(pValue, effectiveN)` helper because three sub-tests shared the same shape with one variant (effective n). WV6 needed similar logic for the per-group branch. WV7 has only one call site — one helper variable, no shared abstraction needed. Direct inline assignment matches WV4's pattern and keeps the wave footprint to ~24 LOC. If a fifth tool ever needs the same shape (n + R² from the strongest of N correlations), promoting this to a helper is a trivial follow-up.
    - **The correlation branch's text, not the joined summary.** The suffix lives inside the correlation branch's `text` field, not appended to the final summary after the join. This means it's structurally adjacent to the data it describes (`...for **${outcome}**.${wv7EvidenceSuffix}`), which keeps the prose readable for both humans and the WW2 extractor. Putting it at the very end of the joined summary would have placed it after a breakdown table or a benchmark line, where the regex could miss the n / R² context.
    - **Empty-evidence guard already in `composeFindingDetail`.** When `evidence` is `{}` (no fields), the formatter returns `""` rather than `" ()"`. This was the load-bearing WV2 design decision — every tool migration depends on it. Tested explicitly here (`empty topCorrelations → empty suffix → branch text unchanged from pre-WV7 shape`) so future formatter refactors that break the empty-evidence contract surface immediately on this branch's tests, not as a silent regression in production prose.
    - **Defensive guards on `Number.isFinite` + range.** Same policy as WV2/WV4/WV5/WV6. NaN or out-of-range silently drops the offending field. Worst case: pre-WV7 baseline (finding tiers as medium / no evidence). No throws, no error paths.
    - **Composite-tool migration template confirmed.** WV7 is the first migration of a composite tool (not a direct `tools/<name>Tool.ts` registration). The pattern transfers: import the formatter + type, destructure the analyzer's plumbed-through field, build the suffix, concat onto the text that names the headline metric. Future composite migrations (if any tool grows that calls `runSignificanceTest` or `runPriceElasticity` internally) can follow WV7's import-path adjustment + same body.

  **Tests.** [tests/runSegmentDriverAnalysisFindingDetailWV7.test.ts](server/tests/runSegmentDriverAnalysisFindingDetailWV7.test.ts) — 6 cases across 3 suites:
    - **Source-inspection wiring** (3): asserts the new imports + destructure of `topCorrelations` + ≥2 references to `wv7EvidenceSuffix` (1 assignment + 1 concat) + a regex match on the exact correlation-branch text template (`Correlation scan on filtered slice (n=${slice.length}) for **${outcome}**.${wv7EvidenceSuffix}`). The regex guards against future refactors that move the suffix elsewhere on the line or drop the wire-up entirely.
    - **Math anchor** (1): `calculateCorrelations` on a 60-row perfect-linear slice (Sales / Spend / Visitors) produces `r ≈ 1` and `nPairs = N` — the upstream contract WV7 piggybacks on. Mirrors WV4's anchor test; documents that any change to the underlying Pearson math would surface here before breaking the WV7 evidence chain.
    - **Roundtrip** (1): builds an evidence suffix from a real `calculateCorrelations` result, embeds it inside a simulated `run_segment_driver_analysis` summary (benchmark line + breakdown table + correlation branch text), and asserts `extractFindingEvidence` recovers `n = 60` and `R²` to 2dp.
    - **Empty-evidence guard** (1): `composeFindingDetail("", {})` returns `""` so the branch text is byte-stable with pre-WV7 when no correlations clear filtering. Documents the load-bearing WV2 contract.
    - 6/6 passing. Appended to [server/package.json](server/package.json) per invariant #4.

  **Verified.** `npx tsc --noEmit` reports 98 errors, identical to WV6 baseline — zero new from WV7. Spot-checked the affected migration chain (`runCorrelationFindingDetailWV4`, `runSignificanceTestFindingDetailWV5`, `runPriceElasticityFindingDetailWV6`, `runSegmentDriverAnalysisFindingDetailWV7`, `formatFindingEvidenceWV2`, `verifierConfidenceOverclaimWiringWV3`, `correlationAnalyzerDiagnostics`, `correlationInsightFallback`) — all green. Code commit `0e52864d`.

  **Out of scope.**
    - **Per-correlation evidence carriage.** The correlation branch may produce up to 20 correlations; only the strongest gets evidence into the summary. Structured `Finding.evidence` (a future schema wave) is the right place to land per-correlation tiers without inflating prose.
    - **Effect size as a fifth `FindingEvidence` field.** Same dormancy debt called out in WV5 / WV6. Adding `effectMagnitude` (Cohen's d, Cramér's V, |r|) would let WQ1 distinguish "statistically significant but practically negligible" from "real and large." Touches the `FindingEvidence` interface + WV2 formatter + WW2 extractor — its own wave.
    - **Workbench surfacing of `ConfidenceOverclaimReport`.** WV3's verifier short-circuit emits the report internally but the workbench doesn't render it. WV8 candidate: pipe tier counts (claimed vs. actual) into the `critic_verdict` SSE payload so the workbench can render "narrator claimed 5 high, blackboard supports 2." Pure addition to verifier.ts emit + client workbench renderer.
    - **Benchmark / breakdown evidence.** The segment-driver tool also produces a benchmark line (`segment sum vs. global sum, segment share≈X%`) and breakdown tables. These aren't statistical findings in the WQ1 sense (no R² / p / CI) but a future wave could attach effect-size / share-magnitude evidence so the WW2 extractor can surface them.
